AIDEEN MODEL STABILIZATION MASTER PLAN
======================================

Purpose
-------
This is the live stabilization task tree. Every investigation, change, validation, rejection, and next action must be recorded here with a short causal explanation.

Operating method
----------------
1. Freeze a minimal corridor.
2. Verify invariants before quality metrics.
3. Use oracle tests to isolate write/read/output failure surfaces.
4. Change one causal piece at a time.
5. Classify every piece: measurement, layout/invariant, architecture, dynamics, diagnostics.
6. Promote only with evidence across required seeds/profiles.

Current baseline corridor
-------------------------
Benchmark: assoc_recall
Command family:
AIDEEN_ASSOC_PERSISTENT=1 AIDEEN_DAMPING=0.4 AR_PAIRS_PER_SEQ=2 AR_AUDIT=1 AR_N_TRAIN=12 AR_N_EVAL=1 AIDEEN_DEBUG_SAMPLE=4 AIDEEN_ASSOC_EVENT_GATE=1 AIDEEN_ASSOC_BANKS=4 AIDEEN_ASSOC_LIBRARIAN_BWD=1 AIDEEN_ASSOC_LOGIT_LAMBDA=1.0 cargo run -p aideen-training --features wgpu --bin assoc_recall --release
Logs: logs/assoc_recall/

Root problem statement
----------------------
Long-gap associative recall remains near random because finite Assoc banks become contaminated/diffuse over long serialized token streams. The system has also had multiple instrumentation/layout/parity bugs that made some previous conclusions unreliable.

3. Layout and invariant fixes
   3.1. Fix b_delta layout mismatch.
        Status: done.
        Failure mode: CPU/debug packed b_delta as d, GPU layout uses h*d.
        Structural rationale: all HistParams offsets after b_delta were shifted unless CPU expands to h*d.
        Files: aideen-backbone/src/gpu_deq.rs, aideen-training-lab/src/bin/assoc_recall.rs, aideen-training-lab/src/trainer.rs, aideen-backbone/src/shaders/segment_memory_promote.wgsl
        Evidence: cargo check passed; event_b stats became nonzero after layout correction.
        Classification: layout/invariant, default stable if no regression appears.
   3.2. Verify full HistParams offset table.
        Status: pending.
        Why: one offset bug invalidated downstream metrics; need systematic parity.
        Subtasks:
        - Trace every layout function in Rust and WGSL.
        - Build an offset table.
        - Add a parity test/assert if feasible.

4. Forward/backward parity
   4.1. Fix Assoc forward/backward compile constant mismatch.
        Status: implemented, validation pending.
        Failure mode: AIDEEN_ASSOC_EVENT_GATE and related Assoc flags were passed to backward but not forward pipeline constants.
        Structural rationale: backward optimized event gate while forward still used default event_gate=1, so trained parameters did not affect writes.
        Anti-patch check: restores equation parity; does not tune around symptoms.
        File: aideen-backbone/src/gpu_deq.rs
        Validation plan: run assoc_recall with AIDEEN_ASSOC_EVENT_GATE=1 and confirm event_b movement reduces forward w_allow/w_gate/write_mass compared to previous logs.
        Classification: layout/equation parity, pending validation.
   4.2. Validate event gate after parity fix.
        Status: pending next run.
        Command: same baseline corridor, log to logs/assoc_recall/exp_forward_event_constant_parity_probe.log
        Success criteria:
        - cargo run completes without NaNs.
        - event_b becomes negative/nonzero.
        - forward w_allow/w_gate changes relative to no-gate/default probe.
        - gap128/gap256 improve or at least write contamination metric decreases.

5. Assoc write policy
   5.1. Diagnose diffuse writes across fillers.
        Status: observed.
        Evidence: gap64/gap128/gap256 logs show w_n proportional to token length and nonzero w_allow/w_gate across filler spans.
        Current interpretation: finite banks act like online EMA over many tokens; binding value becomes diffuse.
   5.2. Test stronger event L1.
        Status: rejected as full solution.
        Log: logs/assoc_recall/exp_event_l1_005_probe.log
        Result: event_b moved more negative and gap256 improved somewhat in one run, but w_n remained proportional to length and quality remained near random.
        Classification: dynamics/experimental, not default.
   5.3. Test dense-local training.
        Status: rejected as full solution.
        Log: logs/assoc_recall/exp_dense_local_event_l1_probe.log
        Result: did not solve selectivity; gap256 worsened in observed run.
        Classification: training-dynamics/rejected for current corridor.
   5.4. Oracle write diagnostic.
        Status: pending.
        Purpose: prove whether correct sparse writes are sufficient for read/LM path to recall.
        Subtasks:
        - Add experimental flag only, not default.
        - Write only known binding events in assoc_recall corridor if marker info is available in shader or via supplied metadata.
        - Compare bank_value target logits and answer_loss.
        Success if gap128/gap256 improve strongly and banks stay less diffuse.
        Failure means read/output path is also broken.

6. Assoc read and LM head coupling
   6.1. Oracle read diagnostic.
        Status: pending after oracle write or if write remains ambiguous.
        Purpose: test whether selecting the correct bank can influence target logits.
   6.2. Oracle LM/output diagnostic.
        Status: pending.
        Purpose: test whether correct value injected near LM head produces correct answer.
   6.3. Review AIDEEN_ASSOC_LOGIT_LAMBDA path.
        Status: pending.
        Why: direct assoc logit path exists but must be traced fully to determine if it is active, too weak, or diagnostic-only.

7. Backward integrity
   7.1. Assoc RHS buffer lifecycle.
        Status: fixed previously, needs documentation in token circuit.
        Failure mode: s_h_rms_buf reused as assoc_grad_buf under Metal storage limit; stale/ignored targets could contaminate RHS.
        Fix summary: zero for IGNORE_TARGET and overwrite with dlassoc on active tokens.
   7.2. Staged adjoint slot-major layout.
        Status: fixed previously, needs documentation.
        Failure mode: adjoint layout mismatch could corrupt gradients.
   7.3. Divergent barrier/reduce NaNs.
        Status: fixed previously, needs documentation.
        Failure mode: workgroup barrier inside divergent lane condition caused NaNs.

8. FPM/Assoc role separation
   8.1. Preserve design intent.
        Status: active principle.
        Assoc role: explicit/literal binding persistence.
        FPM role: slower contextual/general consolidation enriched by Assoc.
   8.2. Verify FPM is not masking Assoc failure.
        Status: pending.
        Subtasks:
        - Trace FPM direct write scale and disabled/frozen backward flags.
        - Verify FPM paths are not silently altering Assoc bank evaluation.

9. Cleanup and hygiene
   9.1. Temporary diagnostics cleanup criteria.
        Status: pending.
        Remove or relocate temporary debug slots once:
        - no NaNs for corridor,
        - forward/backward parity confirmed,
        - oracle tests isolate the failure,
        - permanent metrics are chosen.
   9.2. Legacy/basura cleanup.
        Status: ongoing.
        Rule: do not delete useful diagnostics while stabilization is unresolved; classify and gate experimental paths instead.

Runtime validation update - 2026-04-28
--------------------------------------
- Ran exp_forward_event_constant_parity_probe.log after passing Assoc constants into forward shader compilation.
- Command: baseline corridor with AIDEEN_ASSOC_EVENT_GATE=1, AIDEEN_ASSOC_EVENT_LR_MULT=4, AIDEEN_ASSOC_BANKS=4, AIDEEN_ASSOC_LIBRARIAN_BWD=1, AIDEEN_ASSOC_LOGIT_LAMBDA=1.0.
- Result: completed without NaNs.
- Evidence: event_b_mean=-3.6726e-4, event_b_min=-7.3454e-4; event gradients and updates nonzero.
- Forward behavior: w_allow remained around 4e-2 and w_gate around 2e-2 in long chunks; w_n remains proportional to token count.
- Quality: gap0=3.9000, gap64=3.6230, gap128=3.1498, gap256=3.8472 vs random_base=3.9120.
- Classification: forward/backward constant parity fix remains default-stable candidate because it restores a real invariant. It is not sufficient to solve write selectivity.
- Decision: proceed to oracle write/read/LM diagnostics. Stop tuning event LR/L1 until oracle boundary is known.

Next gate - Oracle write diagnostic
-----------------------------------
1. Target failure mode: Assoc may be failing because write policy stores too many filler/current-token transitions into finite banks, making bank values diffuse before read.
2. Structural rationale: Force or select only known binding writes in the assoc_recall corridor to test whether sparse correct writes are sufficient for read + LM path. This isolates write policy from read/output failures.
3. Anti-patch check: Oracle write is diagnostic-only behind an explicit experimental flag. It is not a proposed default behavior; it tests the causal boundary.
4. Validation plan: compare logs against exp_forward_event_constant_parity_probe.log. Success means lower long-gap write contamination and strong improvement in bank target logits / answer_loss. Failure means read/output/LM path also needs isolation.

Change gate - AssocHist segmented global indexing
-------------------------------------------------
1. Target failure mode: in segmented forward, AssocHist snapshots are written using local segment index `t` and `shape.token_count`, while backward reads them using full-sequence `t` and `params.seq_len`. Long sequences/chunks can therefore train against stale or wrong pre-write banks.
2. Structural rationale: AssocHist is the forward/backward bridge for associative bank state. Its invariant is: forward snapshot index == backward token index == `(batch * full_seq_len + global_t) * h_slots + slot`. Forward already computes `global_t = shape.token_start + t` for S_in/H/Scratch; AssocHist must use the same global coordinate.
3. Anti-patch check: this does not tune gates, losses, or scales. It restores the required layout/ownership invariant at the buffer boundary where the mismatch originates, and remains valid across segment lengths, seeds, and profiles.
4. Validation plan: cargo check; then rerun the baseline corridor log. Success requires no NaNs and changed/cleaner backward behavior without relying on oracle flags. If metric remains random, proceed to oracle write/read/LM diagnostics with the history invariant fixed.
Classification target: layout/invariant, default-stable candidate if validation passes.


Validation - AssocHist segmented global indexing
------------------------------------------------
Log: logs/assoc_recall/exp_assoc_hist_global_index_probe.log
Result: cargo check passed; runtime completed without NaNs.
Metrics: gap0=3.8315, gap64=3.7056, gap128=3.1570, gap256=3.8280 vs random_base=3.9120.
Evidence: long-gap write counters remain length-proportional and w_allow/w_gate remain nonzero across filler chunks.
Classification: layout/invariant default-stable candidate. It fixes a real forward/backward history coordinate mismatch but is not sufficient to solve recall.
Next decision: implement oracle write diagnostic behind explicit flags to isolate write selectivity from read/output paths.

Change gate - Oracle write position mask/force
----------------------------------------------
1. Target failure mode: Assoc finite banks are still updated on nearly every serialized token transition, so key/value banks become diffuse before query even after history indexing is fixed.
2. Structural rationale: assoc_recall has known binding events in the prefix pairs: value positions are odd indices below `2 * pairs_per_seq`. A diagnostic oracle can mask all non-binding writes, and optionally force valid binding writes, without adding buffers or depending on token IDs. This isolates whether sparse correct writes are enough for existing read + LM coupling.
3. Anti-patch check: the oracle is disabled by default and controlled by explicit `AIDEEN_ASSOC_ORACLE_WRITE_POS` / `AIDEEN_ASSOC_ORACLE_FORCE_WRITE` constants. It is not promoted architecture; it only creates a causal boundary test. Forward and backward receive matching constants so training diagnostics are not silently inconsistent.
4. Validation plan: cargo check; run baseline corridor with oracle flags and log to `logs/assoc_recall/exp_oracle_write_positions_force_probe.log`. Success means write counters collapse to prefix binding positions and target answer loss improves materially. Failure means read addressing and/or LM-head coupling must be isolated next.
Classification target: diagnostic temporary, not default.


Oracle implementation correction - forward constants also live in deq_bridge.rs
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------
Finding: the first oracle run was invalid as an oracle write test. `gpu_deq.rs` passed oracle constants to the backbone fused pipeline/backward, but the actual `deq_slot_attn_unified_clean.wgsl` forward pipeline is compiled in `aideen-block/src/deq_bridge.rs` with a separate `slot_coord_constants` map.
Evidence: backward showed `event_grad_signed=0` under oracle stop-grad, but forward trace still had nonzero `w_allow` and length-proportional write counters across filler chunks.
Target failure mode: diagnostic flag parity failure between forward pipeline creation sites.
Structural rationale: every WGSL override used by the unified forward shader must be set at the pipeline that compiles that shader, not only in the backbone wrapper.
Anti-patch check: this does not alter default behavior; it completes the diagnostic flag path at the compile-constant boundary where the mismatch originates.
Validation plan: cargo check; rerun oracle write force and require forward `w_allow` to collapse outside prefix binding positions before interpreting quality metrics.
Classification target: measurement/diagnostic infrastructure, default-stable for flag plumbing while oracle behavior remains experimental.


Change gate - LM sampled-softmax target loss reduction
------------------------------------------------------
1. Target failure mode: assoc_recall answer_loss can report 23.0258 even when full-logit debug shows target probability near random (~0.02). This makes validation metrics unreliable.
2. Structural rationale: lm_train.wgsl computes `s_target_exp` only in the lane that owns the sampled target index, but loss is emitted by `tid == 0`. If the target sample is not processed by lane 0, `target_prob` becomes zero and the loss saturates at `-log(1e-10)`. The target exponential must be reduced across the workgroup just like the softmax denominator.
3. Anti-patch check: this fixes the measurement equation at its origin. It does not clamp, tune, or hide model behavior; it computes the same sampled-softmax CE intended by the shader for every target lane.
4. Validation plan: cargo check; rerun a short assoc_recall oracle/global probe. Success means `answer_loss` aligns with printed `target_p` scale (near random around log(50)=3.912 when target_p~0.02) instead of saturating at 23.0258.
Classification target: measurement/default stable.


Change gate - LM eval sampled-target diagnostic
-----------------------------------------------
1. Target failure mode: `answer_loss` still saturates at 23.0258 for some assoc_recall gaps after reducing target exp, while external `lm_top` debug can show nonzero full-vocab target probability. The validation metric may be reading a different target/sample/input path than the debug display.
2. Structural rationale: `eval_cached_hpooled_token_loss` calls `GpuLmHeadTrainer::train_step_no_readback` with `seq_len=1`; the only valid sampled-softmax invariant is that the requested target is present in `last_sampled_indices`, the shader receives that same target buffer, and the read loss corresponds to that call. A CPU-side diagnostic at sample construction/readback verifies the boundary before changing equations again.
3. Anti-patch check: this is diagnostic-only under `AIDEEN_LM_DEBUG`; it does not change model behavior, logits, gradients, memory, or defaults. It tests whether the measurement path itself is coherent instead of masking the loss.
4. Validation plan: cargo check; run a short assoc_recall probe with `AIDEEN_LM_DEBUG=1`. Success means logs show `contains_target=true`, a concrete `target_pos`, and loss values explainable by the sampled target path. If target is missing or loss remains impossible, isolate shader/readback next.
Classification target: diagnostic temporary; removal criterion is a trusted LM loss path or replacement with permanent metric.

Change gate - assoc_recall pre-GPU sequence-cap planning
--------------------------------------------------------
1. Target failure mode: assoc_recall can externally split long prompt/document sequences at `ctx_len` even when `AIDEEN_SEQ_CAP` is set higher. The split decision happens before the lazy GPU backend exists, so `trainer.gpu_sequence_capacity()` falls back to `config.ctx_len`; this prevents a valid full-document/internal-segment test and makes long-gap runs measure outer serialization loss.
2. Structural rationale: the benchmark chunk planner must use the same declared forward capacity that `GpuDeqBackend` will allocate from `AIDEEN_SEQ_CAP`. Sequence ownership invariant: if the configured forward buffer can hold the full document, the benchmark must pass it as one prompt/document instead of resetting local token coordinates through outer chunks.
3. Anti-patch check: this is not a model-quality compensation. It fixes the measurement/execution corridor at the benchmark planner boundary, restoring consistency between env-declared capacity and actual sequence slicing. It remains valid across seeds and profiles because it changes only when the declared capacity is larger than ctx_len and local explicit segment mode is not forcing smaller segments.
4. Validation plan: cargo check; run short assoc_recall with `AIDEEN_SEQ_CAP=512` and verify LM debug for gap128/gap256 uses single calls with seq_len > 128 rather than 128+1 chunks. Quality can remain random; success criterion is correct prompt/document serialization.
Classification target: measurement/layout corridor fix, default-stable candidate for assoc_recall.

Validation - assoc_recall sequence-cap planner and take_gpu cap fix
-------------------------------------------------------------------
Log: logs/assoc_recall/exp_seqcap_takegpu_fix_probe.log
Result: cargo check passed; runtime completed without NaNs.
Evidence: `cap_debug` reported env_AIDEEN_SEQ_CAP=512, trainer_gpu_sequence_capacity=512, effective_full_cap=512. After changing train_sequence to read `gpu.forward_seq_cap` while the backend is locally borrowed, gap128 used `seq_len=132` and gap256 used `seq_len=260` instead of being truncated to 128 plus an eval token.
Classification: measurement/execution-corridor default-stable candidate. It fixes the origin of the outer serialization measurement bug; quality remains random under one training sample, as expected.
Next decision: rerun oracle write with matching AR_PAIRS_PER_SEQ-derived prefix count and full-document capacity. Do not set AIDEEN_ASSOC_ORACLE_PREFIX_PAIRS unless intentionally overriding the benchmark pair count.

Validation - LM sampled target diagnostic
-----------------------------------------
Log: logs/assoc_recall/exp_lm_eval_sample_probe.log and exp_seqcap_takegpu_fix_probe.log
Result: target is present in sampled indices for active targets; loss no longer saturates at 23.0258 after the sampled target-exp reduction.
Evidence: `contains_target=true`, target_pos matches target id when vocab-sized sampling is active, and loss_int is near 39120 for random cases.
Classification: LM loss reduction remains measurement/default-stable candidate; debug prints are diagnostic temporary under AIDEEN_LM_DEBUG.

Change gate - adjoint sequence capacity parity
----------------------------------------------
1. Target failure mode: after allowing assoc_recall to pass full long documents with `AIDEEN_SEQ_CAP=512`, training panics in `run_clean_adjoint_picard_no_readback` because `dl_dh_src` for seq_len>ctx_len is copied into `Adjoint b_dl` sized only for `ctx_len`.
2. Structural rationale: forward h/AssocHist and backward adjoint buffers are one train-step circuit. If forward accepts `forward_seq_cap`, adjoint RHS (`b_dl`) and slot adjoint state (`b_v_out`) must be allocated for the same sequence capacity; otherwise long-sequence training cannot satisfy the buffer ownership/layout invariant.
3. Anti-patch check: this does not clamp sequence length or hide the panic. It fixes the buffer allocation at the owner where the OOB originates, preserving the same equations for all seq_len <= forward_seq_cap.
4. Validation plan: cargo check; rerun gap128 with AIDEEN_SEQ_CAP=512 and require no copy OOB panic. Then rerun oracle aligned probe and inspect quality separately.
Classification target: layout/invariant default-stable candidate.

Change gate - assoc_recall oracle prefix propagation
----------------------------------------------------
1. Target failure mode: oracle write diagnostic can be enabled with `AIDEEN_ASSOC_ORACLE_WRITE_POS=1` but still perform zero oracle writes when `AIDEEN_ASSOC_ORACLE_PREFIX_PAIRS` and `AR_PAIRS_PER_SEQ` are absent. assoc_recall knows `pairs_per_seq` locally, but the shader constants are populated only from env vars.
2. Structural rationale: the oracle write-position function needs the benchmark's prefix pair count to map binding value positions (`global_t` odd and `< 2*pairs`). The benchmark must propagate its local `pairs_per_seq` into the diagnostic constant path before GPU pipeline creation.
3. Anti-patch check: this affects only the explicit oracle diagnostic flag path and does not alter default model behavior. It fixes the diagnostic boundary so the oracle actually tests sparse binding writes rather than silently disabling them.
4. Validation plan: cargo check; run audited oracle with no manual prefix override and require nonzero `w_allow`/usage/value on binding positions. If quality remains random after banks contain values, proceed to oracle read/output.
Classification target: diagnostic infrastructure default-stable for oracle path; oracle behavior remains temporary.

Change gate - enable Assoc read-to-LM logit bridge by default
-------------------------------------------------------------
1. Target failure mode: after fixing full-document serialization and oracle writes, Assoc banks can contain/read the correct value, but default answer logits remain random because the LM head decodes mostly `h_pooled`; the explicit Assoc read vector is not visible to the decoder unless `AIDEEN_ASSOC_LOGIT_LAMBDA` is manually set.
2. Structural rationale: Assoc stores literal token/value evidence in the embedding/source space. The decoder must receive that explicit read as a logit-space evidence term `lambda * <emb_ref[v], assoc_read_t>`; otherwise precise memory can exist and be selected while having no causal path to the output distribution.
3. Anti-patch check: this restores the intended information-flow invariant between explicit memory and output, rather than tuning gates to make `h_pooled` accidentally carry literal values. The scale remains overrideable, and validation with lambda=1 solved oracle long gaps without tying LM weights.
4. Validation plan: cargo check; rerun oracle full-document probe without manually setting AIDEEN_ASSOC_LOGIT_LAMBDA. Success means gap128/gap256 remain far below random. Non-oracle write policy remains a separate hypothesis.
Classification target: architecture/information-flow default-stable candidate if validation passes; still requires non-oracle validation before claiming full stabilization.

Investigation gate - learned temporal write selectivity after oracle boundary
----------------------------------------------------------------------------
1. Target failure mode: with full-document capacity and default Assoc->LM logit bridge, oracle write positions solve long gaps, but normal writes contaminate banks by writing fillers/query transitions. Linear write mass improves oracle-mask cases but no-oracle long gaps remain random.
2. Structural rationale: explicit Assoc memory needs a persistence policy that decides which transitions become durable bindings. The required invariant is not merely nonzero write mass; it is high write mass on binding transitions and low write mass on irrelevant filler/query transitions, while preserving readable bank values.
3. Anti-patch check: do not tune loss or clamp output to hide contamination. The next change, if any, must affect the write-selection mechanism at its origin or fix an existing selector/gradient path that is currently ineffective.
4. Validation plan: first inspect existing librarian/owner/reuse/event mechanisms. Then test or implement one selector change behind a flag/default only if structurally justified. Success requires no-oracle gap128/256 materially below random and telemetry showing reduced filler write mass, not just lower loss.
Classification target: pending architecture/dynamics; no default promotion until no-oracle validation passes.

Change gate - protect occupied Assoc banks from filler overwrites
-----------------------------------------------------------------
1. Target failure mode: no-oracle Assoc writes still contaminate long-gap memory because every token transition writes into the finite bank set. With one/few banks, the original key->value binding is overwritten or averaged away by fillers before query.
2. Structural rationale: explicit Assoc banks are durable literal bindings, not a dense recurrent accumulator. A write into an already occupied bank should require either an empty-bank allocation, a reuse/match decision, or another strong replacement policy. In the absence of that, write mass must be reduced by available capacity `(1-usage)` so occupied banks preserve stored evidence.
3. Anti-patch check: this fixes the ownership/lifetime invariant of finite banks at the write equation. It does not clamp logits or use benchmark token IDs. It remains valid for generic finite associative memory: preserve occupied bindings unless replacement is justified.
4. Validation plan: cargo check; run no-oracle full-document probe with linear write and occupied protection. Success requires lower long-gap loss and telemetry showing reduced effective writes after bank occupation. If too conservative, test with multiple banks or replacement threshold rather than disabling the invariant.
Classification target: architecture/dynamics default candidate only after no-oracle validation.

Change gate - promote linear Assoc write mass
---------------------------------------------
1. Target failure mode: with occupied-bank protection active, quadratic write mass (`g*g`) underwrites the initial binding, leaving long-gap recall only partial (~2.9 loss). Linear write mass with the same protection solves no-oracle long gaps (~0.95 loss).
2. Structural rationale: Assoc is a literal binding memory. Once the selector decides to commit a binding into an empty bank, the write mass should correspond to selector confidence, not confidence squared. Squaring is appropriate as a conservative damping patch, but here it starves the only durable write before the bank becomes protected.
3. Anti-patch check: this changes the write equation at the origin of underwritten bindings. It does not use token IDs, oracle positions, or output clamps. It remains bounded by bank protection and existing gate factors.
4. Validation plan: set ENABLE_ASSOC_LINEAR_WRITE default true; cargo check; rerun no-oracle full-document corridor with no `AIDEEN_ASSOC_LINEAR_WRITE` env. Success requires gap0/64/128/256 materially below random and no NaNs.
Classification target: dynamics/default-stable candidate after validation.

Change gate - suppress writes from already-stored value sources
---------------------------------------------------------------
1. Target failure mode: with multiple key/value pairs, occupied-bank protection preserves banks but still stores alternating bad transitions such as value->next_key before banks are full. This consumes finite literal capacity and leaves only a subset of queryable key->value bindings.
2. Structural rationale: in explicit associative memory, a token/vector already stored as a bank value should not automatically become the source key for another durable binding on the next step. Suppressing writes when the previous source matches an existing bank value prevents value-chain contamination while still allowing new key-like sources to allocate empty banks.
3. Anti-patch check: this uses only memory geometry (`PrevHStar` vs stored bank values), not benchmark token IDs, positions, or target labels. It restores a role invariant: values are retrievable payloads, not default write addresses, unless a stronger replacement/reuse policy later justifies it.
4. Validation plan: cargo check; run pairs_per_seq=4 with AIDEEN_ASSOC_BANKS=4 and full-document capacity. Success requires gap128/256 materially below random and audit showing preserved multiple bindings. Also rerun pairs=1 default corridor to ensure no regression.
Classification target: architecture/dynamics default candidate after validation.

Validation - default Assoc logit bridge, occupied protection, linear write
-------------------------------------------------------------------------
Logs:
- logs/assoc_recall/exp_default_assoc_logit_oracle_probe.log
- logs/assoc_recall/exp_default_linear_protect_no_oracle_probe.log
- logs/assoc_recall/exp_protect_occupied_quadratic_default_probe.log
Result:
- Oracle full-document with default Assoc->LM bridge solved gap128/gap256 (~0.001 loss), proving the output bridge is now active by default.
- No-oracle pairs_per_seq=1 with occupied-bank protection + linear write solved gap0/64/128/256 (~0.91-1.00 loss) with no NaNs.
- Occupied protection with quadratic write stayed partial (~2.9 loss), so linear write is required for sufficient initial binding mass.
Classification:
- Assoc->LM logit bridge default: default-stable candidate for this corridor.
- Occupied-bank protection: default-stable candidate for single-binding corridor; structurally correct finite-bank lifetime invariant.
- Linear write: default-stable candidate for this corridor.

Validation - multi-binding pairs_per_seq=4
------------------------------------------
Logs:
- logs/assoc_recall/exp_default_pairs4_banks_default_probe.log
- logs/assoc_recall/exp_default_pairs4_banks4_probe.log
- logs/assoc_recall/exp_pairs4_banks4_value_source_suppress_probe.log
Result:
- Default 1 bank remains insufficient for 4 bindings: gap128/gap256 partial/random.
- 4 banks alone did not solve; loss remained around 3.4.
- Suppressing writes from already-stored value sources did not materially improve multi-binding.
Classification:
- Multi-binding selector remains pending. The base single-binding stabilization is real, but scaling to multiple bindings needs a better temporal/bank assignment policy, not just capacity.
Next action:
- Investigate bank allocation trace for pairs_per_seq=4 to see which exact transitions occupy banks. Candidate next fix: explicit transition role state/refractory write state or learned write salience with a sequence-level sparse budget, but do not promote without oracle-style boundary validation.

Change gate - hard commit mass for selected empty bank
-----------------------------------------------------
1. Target failure mode: with multiple bindings and multiple banks, writes into empty banks are diluted by slot and bank soft probabilities (`p_slot_i * bank_prob`), leaving each binding weak (`usage_max < 0.1`, qctx ~0.03) even when a bank is available.
2. Structural rationale: bank choice is already made as a discrete `final_best_bank`. Once the librarian selects an empty bank, the commit mass should not be attenuated by the softmax probability of that selected bank; soft probabilities are useful for differentiable choice, but the persistent bank update is a hard allocation event.
3. Anti-patch check: this does not use benchmark positions/tokens. It fixes the mismatch between hard state mutation (one chosen bank is written) and soft probability-scaled update mass, restoring a finite-memory allocation invariant.
4. Validation plan: under occupied protection, use full event/slot confidence for empty-bank commits and remove bank-prob attenuation from the actual write mass. Run pairs=1 and pairs=4 corridors. Success means stronger usage/qctx and lower multi-binding loss without regressing single-binding.
Classification target: architecture/dynamics pending validation.

Validation - multi-binding follow-up probes
-------------------------------------------
Logs:
- logs/assoc_recall/exp_pairs4_bank_occupancy_audit.log
- logs/assoc_recall/exp_pairs4_hard_bank_commit_probe.log
- logs/assoc_recall/exp_pairs4_hard_commit_hard_read_probe.log
Results:
- Audit showed weak multi-binding state: usage/qctx too low and only Assoc slots 2/3 active.
- Hard commit mass improved pairs=4 from ~3.4 to ~3.02, but still partial/random.
- Hard read + beta=8 did not solve, so the current bottleneck is not read softness alone.
Current classification:
- hard bank commit: experimental useful, not validated as default for multi-binding.
- value-source suppression: rejected/insufficient as standalone for multi-binding; keep only if later selector needs it, otherwise candidate for revert/gating.
- occupied protection + linear write + Assoc->LM bridge remain validated for single-binding corridor.
Next action:
- Investigate explicit multi-binding allocation: either use all Assoc slots as independent binding lanes, or add a sparse write allocator that commits only queryable key sources and maps distinct source keys to distinct banks/slots. Must be validated by bank occupancy traces, not only loss.

Change gate - normalize Assoc write ownership over active Assoc slots
---------------------------------------------------------------------
1. Target failure mode: Assoc writes are diluted by `p_slot_i = 1 / h_slots` even though only slots with `is_assoc_slot` can write. With h_slots=4 only slots 2/3 write, so every durable binding receives half the intended active-slot mass. This is tolerable for one pair but weakens multi-binding occupancy/qctx.
2. Structural rationale: write ownership probabilities must normalize over eligible Assoc writer slots, not all model slots. Non-Assoc slots are FPM/DEQ slots and cannot participate in Assoc writes, so including them in the denominator violates conservation of write mass across the active writer set.
3. Anti-patch check: this fixes the normalization at the write allocation equation. It does not use token IDs, positions, or task-specific oracle information, and remains valid for any h_slots where Assoc writers are the upper half.
4. Validation plan: update default p_slot_i to 1/assoc_writer_count and, if slot-owner is enabled, normalize owner competition over assoc slots only. Run pairs=1 to ensure no regression, then pairs=4/banks=4 to check stronger occupancy/qctx and lower loss.
Classification target: layout/equation invariant default candidate if validation passes.

Validation - Assoc slot active-writer normalization
---------------------------------------------------
Logs:
- logs/assoc_recall/exp_pairs1_assoc_slot_norm_probe.log
- logs/assoc_recall/exp_pairs4_assoc_slot_norm_probe.log
- logs/assoc_recall/exp_pairs4_assoc_slot_norm_audit_short.log
Result:
- pairs_per_seq=1 remains solved after normalizing write ownership over active Assoc slots only: gap0=0.1037, gap64=0.1372, gap128=0.1047, gap256=0.0885, random=3.9120. This confirms multislot Assoc (slots 2/3) is not itself the failure mode.
- pairs_per_seq=4 with AIDEEN_ASSOC_BANKS=4 improved from previous partial/random probes (~3.0-3.4) to gap128=2.2687 and gap256=2.2759, but remains partial. The normalization fixed a real write-mass bug but did not solve multi-binding allocation.
- Short AR_AUDIT=1 run shows the current failure is still not NaN/explosion. It is poor literal binding specificity: best_bank_target_p stays near random (~0.02) in short audit cases, while read entropy remains high across banks.
Classification:
- Active Assoc slot normalization: default-stable candidate for pairs=1; beneficial but insufficient for pairs=4.
- Current next suspected locus: write-event/allocation policy. With event gate disabled, Assoc tries to store generic adjacent-token transitions; multi-pair sequences need sparse selection of key->value transitions, not every transition until banks fill.
Next action:
- Inspect and align forward/backward librarian equations before promoting any allocation dynamics. In particular, the backward allocator still normalizes slot probability over all h slots and still includes bank probability in gradients although forward hard-commit write mass no longer does.

Change gate - forward/backward parity for Assoc librarian allocation
--------------------------------------------------------------------
1. Target failure mode: multi-binding stabilization requires activating/validating the Assoc allocation/event router, but the backward librarian path still contains legacy equations: slot ownership normalizes over all slots instead of active Assoc writer slots, and allocation gradients still treat bank soft probability as part of write mass although forward now performs hard bank commit without bank-prob attenuation.
2. Structural rationale: the trained allocation variables must receive gradients for the same equation executed in forward. Forward write mass is `event_gate * p_assoc_slot` at allocation time, with bank probability only choosing the discrete bank. Backward must therefore normalize `p_slot` over Assoc slots and must not multiply event/slot gradients by `p_bank_best` as if bank probability attenuated the write.
3. Anti-patch check: this does not tune a metric or clamp a symptom. It restores forward/backward equation parity for an existing path and only affects the librarian backward path when that path is enabled. It remains valid across pair counts because it corrects the owner set and derivative chain, not a benchmark-specific case.
4. Validation plan: patch `fused_fpm_retain_bwd.wgsl`; run cargo check; rerun pairs=1 default corridor to ensure the validated path does not regress; then run pairs=4 with `AIDEEN_ASSOC_BANKS=4` and, separately, an experimental event/librarian-bwd probe if defaults still stay partial.
Classification target: layout/equation invariant default-stable for backward parity; event/librarian activation remains experimental until validated.

Validation - Assoc librarian backward parity and event-gate probe
-----------------------------------------------------------------
Logs:
- logs/assoc_recall/exp_pairs1_bwd_librarian_parity_probe.log
- logs/assoc_recall/exp_pairs4_event_librarian_bwd_probe.log
Result:
- Backward parity cleanup compiles and does not regress the validated pairs=1 corridor: gap0=0.1523, gap64=0.0823, gap128=0.0622, gap256=0.0842, no NaNs.
- Experimental activation `AIDEEN_ASSOC_EVENT_GATE=1 AIDEEN_ASSOC_LIBRARIAN_BWD=1` with pairs_per_seq=4, banks=4 regressed to near-random: gap128=3.5076, gap256=3.4205. This is worse than the non-event default after slot normalization (~2.27).
Classification:
- Backward parity cleanup: default-stable candidate because it does not alter default active behavior and preserves the pairs=1 corridor.
- Event gate + librarian activation: rejected as default in current form. It remains experimental only; current initialization/training does not learn sparse key->value selection fast enough and reduces write mass before it has a useful policy.
Next action:
- Run an oracle-write multi-binding probe. If forced key->value-position writes solve pairs=4, the remaining defect is allocator/event selection. If oracle writes do not solve, the defect is addressing/read/output despite clean writes.

Validation - default multi-binding scale ladder
-----------------------------------------------
Logs:
- logs/assoc_recall/scale/default_scale_ladder_summary.log
- logs/assoc_recall/scale/default_pairs1_banks1_gap128.log
- logs/assoc_recall/scale/default_pairs2_banks2_gap128.log
