Classification:
- The current Assoc path is not scalable. It solves single binding and partially handles small multi-binding, but separability collapses as the number of simultaneous bindings grows.
- This broadens the failure mode beyond a pairs=4 artifact. The next audit must inspect pairs8 for output saturation versus memory/addressing failure.
Next action:
- Run AR_AUDIT=1 on a small pairs8 case to inspect LM top logits, selected banks, best-bank target probability, read entropy, and whether values are finite.

Change gate - disable default Assoc-slot direct consolidation into FPM
---------------------------------------------------------------------
1. Target failure mode: scale ladder shows pairs8 can collapse to CE ceiling (23.0258) in default hybrid mode, while `AR_ASSOC_ONLY=1` and/or per-step debug/control avoid the ceiling (~2.07). Audit shows FPM write dynamics saturate under high binding density (`z≈0.999`, `sat=582/584`, `u2v≈24`).
2. Structural rationale: Assoc slots are the literal binding subsystem. After each Assoc bank write, the shader also consolidates the Assoc slot trace into `fpm_m_cache` via `ASSOC_TO_FPM_SCALE=0.02`. With many bindings this creates a second blurred memory inside the same Assoc slots and violates the role split: Assoc holds exact key->value bindings; FPM holds contextual traces in non-Assoc slots. The direct bridge must be explicit/experimental until it has a sparse consolidation policy.
3. Anti-patch check: this is not hiding loss by clipping or tuning a benchmark token. It removes the mechanism that contaminates literal Assoc slots with dense contextual FPM writes while leaving normal FPM slots active. The bridge remains available behind an override for future validated consolidation.
4. Validation plan: make `ASSOC_TO_FPM_SCALE` a shader override defaulting to 0.0; plumb `AIDEEN_ASSOC_TO_FPM_SCALE`; cargo check; rerun pairs1 to ensure no regression; rerun scale points pairs4/pairs8 to confirm no CE-ceiling collapse and document remaining multi-binding precision gap separately.
Classification target: architecture/dynamics default-stable if it removes saturation without regressing single-binding.

Change gate - align Assoc bank capacity clamp across bridge and GPU shader
-------------------------------------------------------------------------
1. Target failure mode: scale tests using `AIDEEN_ASSOC_BANKS=8` show unstable/contradictory behavior. Inspection found `aideen-block/src/deq_bridge.rs` clamps `AIDEEN_ASSOC_BANKS` to 1..4 for buffer/layout allocation, while `aideen-backbone/src/gpu_deq.rs` passes the env value directly to shader constants. This allows shader code to address 8 banks against bridge buffers sized for 4 banks.
2. Structural rationale: Assoc state layout invariant is `assoc_buf_size = h_slots * ASSOC_BANKS * (ASSOC_RANK + d_model + 1)`. Every CPU allocation, GPU shader constant, history carry, and debug read must agree on `ASSOC_BANKS`. A 4-vs-8 mismatch corrupts adjacent state and invalidates any scalability result.
3. Anti-patch check: this fixes a buffer shape/stride invariant at the origin of the failure. It does not tune loss, gate values, or benchmark-specific outputs. It remains valid for any profile using up to the shader-supported 8-bank local arrays.
4. Validation plan: change bridge clamp to 1..8; cargo check; rerun pairs1 and pairs8 default scale probes. Success requires no pairs1 regression and no CE-ceiling collapse for pairs8.
Classification target: layout/invariant default-stable if validation passes.

Validation - layout-fixed pairs8 and read-sharpness probes
----------------------------------------------------------
Logs:
- logs/assoc_recall/scale/default_pairs8_banks8_layout_fixed_gap128.log
- logs/assoc_recall/scale/default_pairs1_layout_fixed_gap128.log
- logs/assoc_recall/scale/tie_qk_pairs8_banks8_layout_fixed_gap128.log
- logs/assoc_recall/scale/hard_read_beta8_pairs8_banks8_layout_fixed_gap128.log
Results:
- After aligning `AIDEEN_ASSOC_BANKS` clamp to 8 in `deq_bridge.rs`, pairs8 no longer hits the CE ceiling: loss moved from 23.0258 to 3.3784. This validates the OOB/layout mismatch as the source of the catastrophic collapse.
- pairs1 remains solved after the layout fix: gap128=0.0945.
- `AIDEEN_ASSOC_TIE_QK=1` did not solve pairs8: gap128=3.3466, so the failure is not only W_q/W_k divergence.
- `AIDEEN_ASSOC_HARD_READ=1 AIDEEN_ASSOC_READ_BETA=8` produced low train loss but eval stayed random (3.9359), so read sharpening alone overfits/does not generalize the bank addressing policy.
Classification:
- Bank clamp/layout fix: default-stable candidate.
- Tie-QK for scale: rejected as standalone.
- Hard read/beta8: rejected as standalone default; may remain diagnostic only.
Next action:
- Multi-binding now needs a structural bank/slot assignment policy. The next likely fix is not read temperature, but ensuring distinct key sources allocate stable distinct banks/lanes without duplicating or blurring across both Assoc slots.

Change gate - freeze learned Assoc address residual by default
--------------------------------------------------------------
1. Target failure mode: after the bank-layout fix, pairs_per_seq=8 no longer collapses to the CE ceiling but remains weak (gap128=3.3784). Audit shows read entropy near uniform and large Wq/Wk address drift. Setting AIDEEN_ASSOC_LR_MULT=0 improves pairs8 to gap128=2.2186 without changing forward capacity, indicating learned address updates are degrading the literal key geometry.
2. Structural rationale: Assoc addressing already contains a direct normalized token/source component (`direct_key/direct_src`) plus a learned residual (`W_k_assoc`, `W_q_assoc`). For explicit literal memory, the direct component is the invariant address manifold. Until the bank allocator/event policy is stable, training the residual rotates keys/queries away from that shared manifold across many bindings; freezing the residual preserves address identity while leaving value/event/alpha paths available.
3. Anti-patch check: this does not clamp loss, hide NaNs, or special-case pair counts. It removes an unvalidated residual dynamics term at the locus where the invariant is broken: key/query address geometry. The learned residual remains opt-in through AIDEEN_ASSOC_ADDR_LR_MULT for future validation.
4. Validation plan: add a separate `assoc_addr_lr_mult` uniform, default `AIDEEN_ASSOC_ADDR_LR_MULT` to 0.0 while preserving `AIDEEN_ASSOC_LR_MULT` for non-address Assoc parameters. Run cargo check, pairs1 gap128, and pairs8/banks8 gap128. Success requires pairs1 to remain solved and pairs8 to match the freeze probe improvement without CE ceiling.
Classification target: dynamics default-stable if validation passes; learned address residual remains experimental pending allocator stability.

Validation - default frozen Assoc address residual
--------------------------------------------------
Logs:
- logs/assoc_recall/scale/default_pairs1_addr_frozen_gap128.log
- logs/assoc_recall/scale/default_pairs8_addr_frozen_gap128.log
Result:
- Separating `AIDEEN_ASSOC_ADDR_LR_MULT` from `AIDEEN_ASSOC_LR_MULT` compiles.
- With address residual frozen by default, pairs1/banks1 gap128 remains solved: 0.0973.
- pairs8/banks8 gap128 improves from the layout-fixed default 3.3784 to 2.1582, close to the env freeze probe 2.2186 and far below random 3.9120.
Classification:
- Frozen learned address residual: default-stable candidate for the current explicit-memory corridor.
- Remaining failure: not catastrophic layout/NaN and not single-pair capacity; multi-binding still has high bank-read entropy and only partial retention.
Next action:
- Run oracle-write with frozen address residual. If forced key->value writes solve pairs8, the remaining locus is write selection/allocation. If not, the remaining locus is read/output geometry.

Change gate - repair oracle-write diagnostic activation
-------------------------------------------------------
1. Target failure mode: the pairs8 oracle-write probe reported no improvement, but audit counters matched the default path. Inspection showed the runtime expects `AIDEEN_ASSOC_ORACLE_WRITE_POS`, while the attempted run used `AIDEEN_ASSOC_ORACLE_WRITE_POSITIONS`; additionally `assoc_recall` only auto-sets `AIDEEN_ASSOC_ORACLE_PREFIX_PAIRS` when `AR_PAIRS_PER_SEQ` is absent, which prevents multi-pair oracle activation in the intended scale probes.
2. Structural rationale: this is a measurement/diagnostic invariant. An oracle-write experiment must force writes exactly at the generated prefix key/value transitions for the configured `pairs_per_seq`; otherwise it cannot distinguish write selection from read/output geometry.
3. Anti-patch check: this does not alter default model behavior because oracle overrides remain disabled unless an explicit oracle env var is set. It fixes only the activation path for a diagnostic override and preserves both env spellings as aliases.
4. Validation plan: accept both oracle env names in Rust plumbing; auto-fill prefix pairs from `pairs_per_seq` whenever oracle is enabled and prefix is unset; rerun the oracle pairs8 probe and compare `w_allow/w_gate` and eval loss against the invalid probe.
Classification target: measurement/diagnostic default-stable.

Validation - repaired oracle-write diagnostic
---------------------------------------------
Logs:
- logs/assoc_recall/scale/oracle_pairs8_addr_frozen_fixed_gap128.log
Result:
- After accepting both oracle env spellings and auto-filling `AIDEEN_ASSOC_ORACLE_PREFIX_PAIRS`, forced oracle writes materially improve pairs8/banks8 gap128 to 1.2455, with `w_allow/w_gate` rising to 5.479e-2 and `r_usage` to ~0.931.
- This invalidates the prior oracle run (`oracle_pairs8_addr_frozen_gap128.log`) as a diagnostic wiring failure.
Classification:
- Oracle activation repair: default-stable measurement fix.
- Remaining model failure: write selection/allocation. The read path and Assoc->LM output bridge are capable of using correctly written banks, but the default allocator does not select the right key->value transitions with high precision under multi-binding serialization.
Next action:
- Inspect the benchmark serialization and write allocator. Implement a non-oracle boundary/role rule only if it restores a general invariant of explicit memory rather than using benchmark token IDs.

Change gate - empty-first allocation for novel Assoc bindings
-------------------------------------------------------------
1. Target failure mode: default pairs8/banks8 remains partial even with frozen address residual, while valid oracle writes improve strongly. Forward allocator computes `found_empty`/`empty_bank` but then ignores them and chooses `final_best_bank` by softmax over occupied+empty scores. For a novel key, an occupied bank with moderately high cosine can win; occupied protection then zeros `allow_write`, so the binding is dropped although free capacity exists.
2. Structural rationale: finite explicit associative memory must preserve the invariant `novel key + available empty bank => allocate empty bank`. Similarity competition is only valid after deciding whether the transition is a reuse/update or a new allocation. Free-bank placement should dominate for novel bindings; occupied banks should be reused only when key similarity exceeds the reuse threshold.
3. Anti-patch check: this does not use AR token IDs, positions, or pair counts. It corrects the allocator state machine: empty capacity must be consumed before rejecting a novel write due to occupied-bank protection. It remains valid for any serialized stream with finite banks.
4. Validation plan: force `final_best_bank=empty_bank` when `found_empty && best_cos_safe <= 0.85`; cargo check; run pairs1 and pairs8 default. Success requires pairs1 unchanged and pairs8 closer to the valid oracle-write result without oracle flags.
Classification target: architecture/allocation default-stable if validation passes.

Change gate - full write mass for unowned replicated Assoc slots
-----------------------------------------------------------------
1. Target failure mode: after empty-first allocation, pairs8 remains partial with bank usage around 0.46, while valid oracle-force writes raise usage to ~0.93 and loss to 1.2455. The default path uses `p_slot_i=1/assoc_slot_count` even when `ENABLE_ASSOC_SLOT_OWNER=false`, but in that mode Assoc slots execute the same binding lane as replicas rather than a mutually exclusive owner competition.
2. Structural rationale: slot-probability normalization is required only when slots compete for ownership. Without slot-owner routing, dividing write mass across identical replicas weakens every bank copy and makes literal retrieval diffuse. The invariant should be: unowned replicated Assoc slots write full local binding mass; owned slots use normalized owner probability.
3. Anti-patch check: this does not use task positions/tokens or increase capacity artificially. It fixes the role of `p_slot_i`: probability only belongs to a competition. When there is no competition, applying it as attenuation is mathematically wrong. Backward parity must match the same default.
4. Validation plan: set default `p_slot_i=1.0` in forward/backward, retaining normalized softmax only under `ENABLE_ASSOC_SLOT_OWNER`; cargo check; rerun pairs1 and pairs8. Success requires pairs1 unchanged and pairs8 usage/loss closer to oracle-force.
Classification target: equation invariant default-stable if validation passes.

Validation - full write mass for unowned replicated Assoc slots
---------------------------------------------------------------
Logs:
- logs/assoc_recall/scale/default_pairs1_full_slot_write_gap128.log
- logs/assoc_recall/scale/default_pairs8_full_slot_write_gap128.log
Result:
- pairs1/banks1 gap128 improves to 0.0005 with `r_usage≈0.924` and no NaNs.
- pairs8/banks8 gap128 improves from 2.0631 after empty-first to 1.0406, with `r_usage≈0.931`, matching the mass level seen in the valid oracle-force probe.
Classification:
- Full write mass for unowned replicated Assoc slots: default-stable candidate. It fixes the slot-probability invariant and does not regress the single-binding corridor.
- Empty-first allocation: still structurally correct but not sufficient alone; keep as allocator invariant because it prevents dropping novel writes when free banks exist.
Remaining failure:
- Read entropy remains high (~2.03 for 8 banks), so banks are written strongly but the query does not sharply select the correct bank. Next locus is address separability/read-query geometry, not write mass or LM-head reachability.
Next action:
- Test whether sharing the frozen write-key residual for query (`AIDEEN_ASSOC_TIE_QK=1`) sharpens read selection now that slot mass and layout are fixed. If not, inspect fixed key geometry and consider a non-learned literal address basis.

Change gate - make explicit Assoc retrieval winner-take-all by default
----------------------------------------------------------------------
1. Target failure mode: with bank layout, address residual, allocation, and slot write mass fixed, pairs8/banks8 still stays around 1.0406 under soft bank mixing and read entropy remains near uniform (~2.03). Enabling hard read with the same writes solves pairs8/gap128 to 0.0001.
2. Structural rationale: Assoc is the literal binding memory. Once a query address is compared against finite banks, returning a weighted mixture of several bank values contaminates the payload whenever multiple bindings coexist. Literal retrieval requires selecting the best matching bank (winner-take-all) rather than averaging values. FPM remains the subsystem for graded/contextual blending.
3. Anti-patch check: this is not a loss clamp or benchmark-specific threshold. It restores the role split between explicit memory and contextual FPM: Assoc stores and retrieves discrete key->value bindings; FPM handles continuous summaries. It remains overrideable via `AIDEEN_ASSOC_HARD_READ=0` for experiments that need differentiable soft read.
4. Validation plan: make `ENABLE_ASSOC_HARD_READ` default true in forward plumbing; cargo check; rerun pairs1 and pairs8 default without env hard-read flags. Success requires pairs1 solved and pairs8 matching the hard-read probe without explicit flags.
Classification target: architecture/read equation default-stable if validation passes.

Validation - hard-read default
------------------------------
Logs:
- logs/assoc_recall/scale/default_pairs1_hard_read_default_gap128.log
- logs/assoc_recall/scale/default_pairs8_hard_read_default_gap128.log
Result:
- Default pairs1/banks1 gap128 solves at ~0.0000 without explicit hard-read flags.
- Default pairs8/banks8 gap128 solves at 0.0001 without explicit hard-read flags.
- Read entropy drops to 0 and read max to 1.0, confirming the previous failure was value mixing across banks rather than inability to store or bridge to LM logits.
Classification:
- Hard read default: default-stable candidate for explicit Assoc retrieval.
- Full unowned-slot write mass and empty-first allocation remain part of the stable causal package.
Next action:
- Run the multi-gap pairs8 corridor (0,64,128,256) to verify long-gap stability beyond the single gap128 probe.

Validation - default pairs8 multi-gap stabilized corridor
---------------------------------------------------------
Log:
- logs/assoc_recall/scale/default_pairs8_hard_read_multigap.log
Result:
- Default pairs8/banks8 with gaps 0,64,128,256 and no explicit hard-read flag solves all evaluated gaps:
  - gap0=0.0004
  - gap64=0.0004
  - gap128=0.0002
  - gap256=0.0002
- Read entropy is 0.0, read max is 1.0, context RMS is 1.0, and bank usage is ~0.952 in active Assoc slots.
Final classification for this stabilization package:
- Bank layout clamp 1..8: default-stable layout/invariant fix.
- Frozen learned Assoc address residual default (`AIDEEN_ASSOC_ADDR_LR_MULT=0`): default-stable dynamics fix for literal address preservation; learned residual remains opt-in.
- Oracle diagnostic activation repair: default-stable measurement fix.
- Empty-first allocation for novel bindings: default-stable allocator invariant.
- Full write mass for unowned replicated Assoc slots: default-stable slot equation invariant.
- Hard read default for explicit Assoc retrieval: default-stable read equation invariant.
Residual risks / next validation:
- Validate beyond synthetic AR: higher pair counts up to bank cap, different seeds, longer train/eval counts, and interaction with `ENABLE_ASSOC_SLOT_OWNER` once real slot ownership is reintroduced.
- If soft/differentiable read is needed for another task, keep it experimental via `AIDEEN_ASSOC_HARD_READ=0`; do not make it default for literal recall without a non-contaminating sparse mixture rule.

Change gate - clamp GPU Assoc bank count to shader-supported capacity
---------------------------------------------------------------------
1. Target failure mode: current WGSL forward/read/write paths use fixed local arrays of length 8 for bank scores/probabilities. `deq_bridge.rs` clamps `AIDEEN_ASSOC_BANKS` to 1..8, but `gpu_deq.rs` still accepts the raw env value. Values above 8 can compile constants that make shader loops index beyond local arrays or desynchronize CPU/GPU layout expectations.
2. Structural rationale: the capacity invariant is `ASSOC_BANKS <= shader local bank array capacity`. Until the shader arrays and layouts are generalized, every Rust plumbing path must clamp to the same max bank count.
3. Anti-patch check: this does not hide a model-quality issue. It enforces a memory/layout safety bound at the source of configuration, and preserves all validated behavior for banks <= 8.
4. Validation plan: clamp `gpu_deq.rs` bank env to 1..8; cargo check; run a small assoc_recall compile/run with `AIDEEN_ASSOC_BANKS=16` and confirm it no longer crashes or indexes beyond supported capacity, while documenting that effective capacity is capped at 8.
Classification target: layout/invariant default-stable.

Capacity probe - more pairs than literal Assoc banks
----------------------------------------------------
Logs:
- logs/assoc_recall/scale/capacity_pairs8_banks4_gap128.log
- logs/assoc_recall/scale/capacity_pairs16_banks8_gap128.log
Result:
- pairs8/banks4/gap128: eval loss=3.5877, near random baseline 3.9120.
- pairs16/banks8/gap128: eval loss=6.2753, worse than random because the hard literal read confidently retrieves a stored but wrong binding when the queried pair was not retained.
Classification:
- Confirmed capacity invariant: in the current default replicated Assoc path, one bank stores one exact active key->value binding. Exact recall requires active literal bindings <= banks unless a validated replacement, promotion, persistence, or compression policy is introduced.
Next action:
- Design capacity hierarchy instead of raising banks blindly: local Assoc banks for exact active segment bindings; persistent Assoc for selected inter-segment literals; FPM for contextual/general compression; optional slot-owner lanes to multiply exact capacity once validated.

Research alignment - external/scalable memory directions
-------------------------------------------------------
Sources reviewed:
- DNC / Neural Turing-style memory: content/location addressing, usage/allocation vectors, explicit external memory.
- Product-Key Memory: very large key-value memory accessed by structured/exact nearest-neighbor style lookup.
- kNN-LM / Memorizing Transformer / RETRO / LongMem: external or cached key-value/chunk retrieval for long-tail facts and long context.
- Transformer-XL / Compressive Transformer: segment recurrence and compressed long-range memory.
Implication for AIDEEN:
- Current Assoc hard-read behavior is aligned with kNN/key-value literal retrieval, not with soft attention over values.
- FPM should remain the graded contextual/compressive memory.
- The next learning problem is not raw recall but memory management: salience, replacement, promotion, persistence, and learned routing between literal Assoc and contextual FPM.

Capacity roadmap - from replicated Assoc to scalable lanes
---------------------------------------------------------
Problem:
- Current validated corridor uses h_slots=4 and ASSOC_BANKS<=8 with Assoc slots replicated. Exact capacity is therefore banks, not banks × assoc_slots.
- Larger goals such as 32 banks and 16 slots require distinguishing technical limits from architectural policy.
Current technical limits:
- WGSL local bank arrays are fixed length 8, so ASSOC_BANKS>8 is currently unsupported without shader refactor.
- Assoc slots are the upper half of h_slots. With h_slots=4, there are 2 Assoc slots, but default slot-owner is off, so they replicate the same memory.
Target architecture:
- Local exact capacity should become assoc_lanes × banks_per_lane once slot-owner/lane routing is validated.
- FPM should contextualize/compress over time, not carry every exact binding.
- Persistent Assoc should promote selected exact bindings across segments.
Next focus:
1. Validate slot-owner/lane routing as a capacity multiplier with current 8-bank shader limit.
2. If lane routing works, test h_slots=8 or 16 with banks<=8 to estimate practical capacity/cost.
3. Only then refactor shader local arrays to support banks=16/32, with layout checks and performance measurements.

Lane-capacity probe - h_slots=8, banks=8, pairs16
--------------------------------------------------
Logs:
- logs/assoc_recall/scale/lanes_h8_b8_p16_no_owner.log
- logs/assoc_recall/scale/lanes_h8_b8_p16_owner_anchor.log
Result:
- h_slots=8, banks8, pairs16, no owner: eval loss=5.6103. Active Assoc slots 4..7 replicate the same eight-bank capacity; this does not multiply exact capacity.
- h_slots=8, banks8, pairs16, `AIDEEN_ASSOC_SLOT_OWNER=1 AIDEEN_ASSOC_SLOT_ANCHOR=1`: eval loss=2.6277. This is materially better but still partial. It indicates the owner path can distribute writes across lanes, but current anchor routing is not sufficient for exact lane assignment and retrieval.
- Performance drops from ~100+ TPS in h_slots=4 corridors to ~30 TPS in h_slots=8/pairs16 probes on M1 Pro, so slot count is an expensive capacity lever.
Classification:
- Slot-owner/lane routing: experimental useful, not default-stable.
- Raising slots without robust routing is not a correct capacity solution.
Next action:
- Implement/validate explicit lane assignment policy before increasing slots or banks: stable hash/geometric router, least-used lane router, or learned owner only after backward parity. For exact recall, lane routing must guarantee that query and write choose the same lane.

Change gate - deterministic literal-address lane router
-------------------------------------------------------
1. Target failure mode: h_slots=8 with four Assoc lanes and banks8 still cannot recall pairs16 exactly. Without owner, lanes replicate the same eight banks. With anchor owner, eval improves to 2.6277 but remains partial because slot anchors provide a soft learned/geometric prior, not a guaranteed write/read-consistent lane assignment.
2. Structural rationale: to multiply exact capacity by lanes, the lane identity must be a deterministic function of the literal key address, and the same function must be used on write and read. Then capacity becomes approximately `assoc_lanes * banks_per_lane`, bounded by collisions. Learned slot-owner can be trained later, but a stable hash router is the invariant baseline for exact lane consistency.
3. Anti-patch check: this does not use token IDs, AR positions, targets, or pair counts. It routes by the same normalized Assoc address vector that already defines bank keys/queries. It is experimental behind `AIDEEN_ASSOC_HASH_LANE=1` and does not alter the validated default h_slots=4 corridor unless explicitly enabled.
4. Validation plan: add WGSL/Rust plumbing for `ENABLE_ASSOC_HASH_LANE`; under `ENABLE_ASSOC_SLOT_OWNER`, make write/read gate hard to the hash-selected Assoc lane. Run cargo check and compare h_slots=8,banks8,pairs16 with hash lane vs prior anchor owner. Success requires large improvement over 2.6277 and stable no-NaN behavior.
Classification target: experimental useful; default only after broader validation.

Change gate - conserve Assoc read mass under exclusive hash lanes
-----------------------------------------------------------------
1. Target failure mode: deterministic hash-lane routing improves pairs16/h8/b8 to 2.1153 but remains partial. Active lanes show strong per-slot reads, yet only one Assoc lane emits for a queried binding. The previously solved replicated path emitted the same literal context from every active Assoc slot, so downstream slot aggregation received more total Assoc signal.
2. Structural rationale: lane ownership should affect storage locality, not reduce total read energy. If `assoc_slot_count` replicated lanes are replaced by one exclusive owner lane, the owner lane must carry the aggregate read mass that the replicas previously supplied, otherwise capacity routing trades exact storage for weaker output coupling.
3. Anti-patch check: this is not a loss clamp or benchmark-specific boost. It restores conservation of Assoc read mass when changing from replicated lanes to exclusive lanes. It is active only with experimental `ENABLE_ASSOC_HASH_LANE` + `ENABLE_ASSOC_SLOT_OWNER`.
4. Validation plan: multiply `assoc_inj` by `assoc_slot_count` only in hash-lane owner mode; cargo check; rerun h_slots=8,banks8,pairs16 hash-lane. Success requires improvement over 2.1153 without destabilizing compile/runtime.
Classification target: experimental useful pending validation.

Validation - hash lane and read-mass conservation probe
-------------------------------------------------------
Logs:
- logs/assoc_recall/scale/lanes_h8_b8_p16_hash_lane.log
- logs/assoc_recall/scale/lanes_h8_b8_p16_hash_lane_mass.log
Result:
- Deterministic hash lane routing improved h8/b8/pairs16 from anchor-owner 2.6277 to 2.1153, so stable write/read lane consistency is useful.
- Read-mass conservation scaling worsened eval to 3.0722 and was reverted. The remaining bottleneck is not merely output-scale dilution.
Classification:
- `AIDEEN_ASSOC_HASH_LANE`: experimental useful, not default-stable.
- Hash-lane read mass scaling: rejected and removed.
Next action:
- Investigate collisions/drop directly. The key issue is whether 16 key tokens distribute across four lanes with <=8 per lane and whether every key->value prefix write survives protection. If collisions are acceptable but recall still partial, inspect lane read/output selection; otherwise implement better lane router or replacement policy.

Next focus - scalable pair capacity root-cause split
---------------------------------------------------
Goal:
- Scale the number of exact key->value pairs beyond one local bank set.
Clarification:
- Example values like 32 banks / 16 slots are not targets yet. The architectural target is effective scalable capacity.
Current hypothesis:
- Exact local capacity should scale as `assoc_lanes * banks_per_lane` only if lane routing is write/read consistent and collisions/drop are controlled.
Immediate diagnostic split:
1. Collision/drop: are all prefix key->value writes placed into lanes/banks, and how many land per lane?
2. Read locality: does the query route to the same lane as the original write?
3. Output coupling: if the correct lane/bank is selected, does LM output the value?
Next action:
- Add/inspect diagnostics to count per-lane occupancy and selected lane during write/read for hash-lane, then run h8/b8/pairs16 with audit.

Change gate - global value-source suppression across hash lanes
---------------------------------------------------------------
1. Target failure mode: hash-lane h8/b8/pairs16 remains partial and audit shows target values are often not present in any useful bank. The current `ENABLE_ASSOC_SUPPRESS_VALUE_SOURCE` only checks whether the previous source matches a value already stored in the current lane. In lane-routed mode, a just-written value token can hash to a different lane on the next transition, so `VAL -> next KEY` transitions can consume banks and contaminate exact capacity.
2. Structural rationale: value-source suppression is a global role invariant, not a lane-local invariant. If any Assoc lane already stores the previous token as a value payload, that token should not become a durable key source in another lane by default. Otherwise lane routing breaks the key/value role separation established by replicated Assoc.
3. Anti-patch check: this uses only memory geometry across Assoc lanes (`PrevHStar` vs stored bank values), not token IDs, labels, AR positions, or pair counts. It corrects the origin of lane contamination: cross-lane role leakage.
4. Validation plan: in `ENABLE_ASSOC_SLOT_OWNER && ENABLE_ASSOC_HASH_LANE`, compute best previous-value cosine across all Assoc lanes before suppression. Run cargo check and h8/b8/pairs16 hash-lane. Success requires improvement over 2.1153 and no regression in compile/runtime.
Classification target: experimental useful; default only if hash-lane corridor validates.

Validation - global value-source suppression across hash lanes
--------------------------------------------------------------
Log:
- logs/assoc_recall/scale/lanes_h8_b8_p16_hash_lane_global_suppress.log
Result:
- h8/b8/pairs16 hash-lane with global value-source suppression produced eval loss=2.3492, worse than hash-lane baseline 2.1153.
Classification:
- Global value-source suppression across lanes: rejected for now and reverted. Cross-lane VAL->KEY contamination may exist, but this intervention over-suppresses or does not address the dominant cause.
Next action:
- Add/derive a lane occupancy/collision report from AssocState. We need to know whether every key has storage capacity in its lane before designing a new router or replacement policy.

Change gate - hash lane must route on slot-independent direct literal address
----------------------------------------------------------------------------
1. Target failure mode: `AIDEEN_ASSOC_HASH_LANE=1` improves h8/b8/pairs16 but remains partial. Inspection shows the hash is computed from `q_self` / `assoc_scratch`, which include `W_k_assoc`/`W_q_assoc` residuals indexed by `slot_idx`. Even with address LR frozen, these residuals are randomly initialized per slot, so different slots can compute different owner lanes for the same literal key.
2. Structural rationale: lane routing is only a capacity multiplier if write and read compute a slot-independent owner lane from the same literal key address. Therefore hash-lane mode must route and store using the direct normalized source component, not the per-slot residual address. Learned residual addressing can remain for non-hash experiments, but deterministic lanes require invariant direct geometry.
3. Anti-patch check: this does not use token IDs, labels, or AR positions. It removes slot-local randomness from the lane router at the mathematical origin of inconsistent lane ownership. It is active only under experimental `ENABLE_ASSOC_HASH_LANE`.
4. Validation plan: in hash-lane mode, set read query/write key candidate to `tanh(direct)` before hashing/storing. Run cargo check, then h8/b8/pairs16 hash-lane. Success requires improvement over 2.1153 and no regression in existing h4/b8 default path.
Classification target: experimental useful pending validation.

Validation - hash lane direct literal address
---------------------------------------------
Log:
- logs/assoc_recall/scale/lanes_h8_b8_p16_hash_lane_direct_addr.log
Result:
- h8/b8/pairs16 hash-lane with direct-only read/write address produced eval loss=5.5814, worse than hash-lane baseline 2.1153 and worse than random baseline behavior.
Classification:
- Direct-only hash-lane address: rejected and reverted. The residual Assoc projection is not merely slot-noise; it appears to contribute useful address spreading or alignment. Removing it collapses effective lane/bank retrieval.
Next action:
- Inspect actual lane/bank occupancy and per-key routing rather than removing the residual blindly. The next causal split is whether failure comes from collisions/drop, read lane mismatch, or LM/output coupling after correct bank selection.

Change gate - AR LM debug must include Assoc direct-logit path
--------------------------------------------------------------
1. Target failure mode: `assoc_recall` audit reports `answer_loss` from the GPU LM head but `format_lm_top_debug` computes logits only from `h_pooled`. The actual LM shader also adds `AIDEEN_ASSOC_LOGIT_LAMBDA * Emb[token] dot assoc_pooled`, so audit can falsely classify solved cases as random and misdirect stabilization work.
2. Structural rationale: the metric/debug invariant is that diagnostic logits must use the same equation as `lm_train.wgsl::lm_probs_main`: `logit_v = b_v + W_v·RMSNorm(h) + lambda * Emb_v·assoc_pooled`. Adding assoc_pooled readback to the diagnostic restores equation parity without changing model behavior.
3. Anti-patch check: this is a measurement/diagnostic fix only. It does not alter forward, backward, weights, routing, banks, or loss. It corrects the observer at the source of the mismatch rather than hiding model errors.
4. Validation plan: add a temporary `read_assoc_pooled_at` diagnostic readback and update `format_lm_top_debug`; cargo check; rerun a short `AR_AUDIT=1` hash-lane probe and verify reported target probability aligns qualitatively with low/high `answer_loss` cases.
Classification target: measurement default-stable / diagnostic temporary readback.

Change gate - AR eval/debug must use current GPU embedding reference
--------------------------------------------------------------------
1. Target failure mode: after adding the Assoc direct-logit term, `assoc_recall` audit can still report low `answer_loss` with low CPU-computed target probability. The LM shader uses `emb_ref_buf` copied from `gpu_emb.weights_buffer()`, while the audit used `trainer.tokenizer.embeddings`, which can be stale after GPU embedding updates. `eval_cached_hpooled_token_loss` also did not explicitly refresh `emb_ref_buf` for the one-token eval call.
2. Structural rationale: the observer/eval invariant is that loss and debug must use the same embedding reference tensor as `lm_train.wgsl`. The source of truth on the GPU path is `gpu_emb.weights_buffer()`, not the CPU tokenizer matrix after training begins.
3. Anti-patch check: this does not alter model routing, banks, memory writes, or training equations. It restores CPU/GPU measurement parity and prevents stale-buffer evaluation. If metrics change, the old metrics were observing the wrong tensor.
4. Validation plan: pass `gpu_emb.weights_buffer()` into `eval_cached_hpooled_token_loss`; read GPU embedding weights in `format_lm_top_debug`; cargo check; rerun short AR audit and verify target probability aligns with answer loss direction.
Classification target: measurement default-stable.

Validation - AR LM audit parity with GPU embedding reference
-----------------------------------------------------------
Log:
- logs/assoc_recall/scale/lanes_h8_b8_p16_hash_lane_audit_gpu_emb.log
Result:
- The diagnostic now aligns with loss direction. Example solved case: loss=0.0001, target=30, target_logit=12.618, target_p=9.998e-1, lm_top=30.
- Non-solved cases remain near uniform: loss around 3.8, target_p around 2.1e-2.
Classification:
- `read_assoc_pooled_at` and GPU-embedding audit path: measurement/default-stable while AR diagnostics are active; readback remains temporary diagnostic.
- `eval_cached_hpooled_token_loss` now refreshes `emb_ref` from `gpu_emb.weights_buffer()`: measurement correctness fix.
Next action:
- With metric parity restored, treat h8/b8/pairs16 partial recall as real Assoc coverage/routing problem. Diagnose whether missed cases lack an owner-lane read, route to the wrong lane/bank, or have insufficient assoc_pooled target contribution.

Validation - hash-lane baseline after metric parity fix
-------------------------------------------------------
Log:
- logs/assoc_recall/scale/lanes_h8_b8_p16_hash_lane_metric_fixed.log
Result:
- h8/b8/pairs16/hash-lane now evaluates at loss=1.4189, 36.3% of random baseline, classified as MEMORY WORKS.
- The previous ~2.1 partial reading was confounded by stale/incomplete LM audit/eval parity. The model path was stronger than the observer indicated.
Classification:
- Hash-lane h8/b8/pairs16: experimental useful and now a stronger capacity baseline.
Next action:
- The next scaling blocker is the benchmark itself: AR_N_KEYS is hardcoded to 16 and `pairs_per_seq` clamps to 16. To test scalable pair capacity, make AR vocabulary size configurable while preserving the default 50-token baseline.

Change gate - make AR pair capacity benchmark configurable beyond 16 pairs
-------------------------------------------------------------------------
1. Target failure mode: `assoc_recall` cannot test more than 16 key->value pairs because `N_KEYS`, `N_VALS`, token bases, and `VOCAB_SIZE` are compile-time constants and `pairs_per_seq` clamps to `N_KEYS`. This blocks validation of the architecture's scalable pair capacity.
2. Structural rationale: pair-capacity validation requires the data generator and LM vocab to expose more unique key/value identities. The model capacity question is independent of the old benchmark's 16-key toy vocabulary. Making the token layout env-configurable restores measurement capacity without changing model equations.
3. Anti-patch check: this is not a model-quality patch. Defaults reproduce the existing 50-token benchmark exactly. Larger vocab/pair counts are explicit experimental profiles via env vars.
4. Validation plan: introduce an `ArVocab` layout from env (`AR_N_KEYS`, `AR_N_VALS`, `AR_N_FILLER`) with old defaults; cargo check; rerun default/pairs16 smoke; then run a higher-pair probe such as 24 or 32 pairs with sufficient vocab and h_slots.
Classification target: measurement/benchmark default-stable.

Change gate - report per-lane Assoc occupancy for capacity diagnosis
--------------------------------------------------------------------
1. Target failure mode: p24/h8 fails, but current audit only reports aggregate Assoc usage. We cannot tell whether failures come from lane imbalance/collisions, empty lanes, or output coupling.
2. Structural rationale: exact capacity depends on the invariant `active bindings per owner lane <= banks_per_lane` plus correct read routing. Reporting occupied bank counts and usage means per slot directly observes the capacity invariant without changing model behavior.
3. Anti-patch check: diagnostic-only. It reads `AssocState` after training/eval and prints occupancy; no equations, weights, buffers, or runtime flags are changed.
4. Validation plan: add per-slot occupancy summary to `AR_AUDIT`; cargo check; rerun p24 audit and inspect whether lanes saturate unevenly or all lanes are full.
Classification target: diagnostic temporary.

Validation - oracle write positions for p24
------------------------------------------

Classification:
- Oracle write-position filtering: rejected as sufficient fix. It remains a diagnostic, not architecture.
Next action:
- Separate lane routing from bank address geometry. Previous direct-only attempt changed both lane selection and stored/read key geometry and failed. Try direct literal only for owner-lane hash while preserving residual Wq/Wk key/query inside the selected lane.

Change gate - direct literal owner-lane hash with residual bank address
-----------------------------------------------------------------------
1. Target failure mode: p24/h8 hash-lane saturates all four Assoc lanes and most failed cases have no strong target contribution in `assoc_pooled`. Earlier direct-only address routing failed because it also removed the residual key/query geometry used for bank matching.
2. Structural rationale: lane identity and bank address are different invariants. Lane identity must be stable and slot-independent for the same literal key; bank address can still use the learned/residual Assoc projection to spread and match within that lane. Therefore only the owner-lane hash should use the normalized direct previous signal; stored keys/read queries remain `tanh(W_assoc source + direct)`.
3. Anti-patch check: this does not use AR token IDs, labels, target values, or pair counts. It corrects the routing invariant at the lane-selection level without suppressing the residual geometry that validation showed was useful.
4. Validation plan: add WGSL direct-source hash for owner selection under `ENABLE_ASSOC_HASH_LANE`; cargo check; rerun p16 and p24 hash-lane corridors. Success requires p16 not to regress materially and p24 to improve over random/previous p24.
Classification target: experimental useful pending validation.

Validation - direct owner-lane hash with residual bank address
--------------------------------------------------------------
Log:
- logs/assoc_recall/scale/lanes_h8_b8_p16_hash_lane_direct_owner.log
Result:
- p16/h8/b8 regressed to eval loss=3.0963 (79.1% of random), worse than the metric-fixed hash-lane baseline. The change failed the no-regression criterion before p24 validation.
Classification:
- Direct literal owner-lane hash: rejected and reverted. Residual address geometry is not only useful for bank matching; current owner selection also depends on that geometry in a way the validated corridor needs.
Next action:
- Keep current residual hash-lane as experimental baseline. The p24 failure is now best explained by all lanes being full and weak target presence, requiring better write/replacement/salience policy or larger validated bank arrays, not a direct hash-only router.

Change gate - raise Assoc bank cap from 8 to 16 for capacity testing
--------------------------------------------------------------------
1. Target failure mode: p24/h8 saturates all four Assoc lanes at 8/8 banks. Current Rust config clamps `AIDEEN_ASSOC_BANKS` to 8 and forward/backward shaders have local bank-score arrays of length 8, preventing direct validation of whether more banks per lane solves pair scaling.
2. Structural rationale: exact capacity is bounded by `assoc_lanes * banks_per_lane` and by replacement policy. Raising the supported bank cap requires matching Rust clamps and WGSL local arrays so loops over `ASSOC_BANKS` remain in-bounds in forward and backward paths.
3. Anti-patch check: this is a layout/capacity invariant change, not a quality mask. It does not alter equations for banks<=8 and only enables explicit experimental profiles with banks>8. If p24 improves with 16 banks, it supports the capacity/saturation diagnosis; if not, replacement/routing remains the bottleneck.
4. Validation plan: update clamps/audit to 16 and bank local arrays to 16; cargo check; rerun p16/b8 to ensure no regression in old cap; run p24/b16/h8 hash-lane.
Classification target: layout/invariant default-stable for supported cap, architecture experimental for banks>8.

Validation - bank cap 16 p24 probe
----------------------------------

- logs/assoc_recall/scale/lanes_h8_b16_p24_vocab66_hash_lane.log

Result:

- Occupancy is uneven: s4=16/16, s5=14/16, s6=16/16, s7=8/16. Some eval cases solve strongly through assoc_pooled; others remain near uniform.

- Bank cap 16: experimental useful for capacity testing. It supports the capacity/saturation diagnosis but does not fully solve routing.
Next action:
- Test deterministic multi-probe hash lanes: write/read to owner lane plus one secondary lane. This is aligned with hashed memory/cuckoo-style redundancy and should reduce lane imbalance while preserving explicit Assoc memory.

Change gate - experimental two-lane hash replication
----------------------------------------------------
1. Target failure mode: h8/b16/p24 remains partial with uneven lane occupancy and failed cases where target is not present in the selected read lane. Single-owner hash routing is too brittle under higher pair counts.
2. Structural rationale: exact hash memories commonly use multi-probe/replicated candidate buckets to reduce collision sensitivity. For AIDEEN, writing a binding to owner lane plus deterministic adjacent lane and reading from the same two lanes preserves the invariant that query and write share deterministic lane choices, while increasing probability that one lane keeps the binding.
3. Anti-patch check: this does not use labels, target IDs, or AR positions. It changes only the experimental `hash_lane` routing policy behind an explicit flag and remains valid across pair counts as a collision-reduction mechanism.
4. Validation plan: add `AIDEEN_ASSOC_HASH_REPLICA=1`; cargo check; run p16/b8 or p16/b16 no-regression and p24/b16 target profile. Success requires p24 improvement over 2.4274 without catastrophic p16 regression.
Classification target: experimental useful pending validation.

Validation - two-lane hash replication p24
------------------------------------------
Log:
- logs/assoc_recall/scale/lanes_h8_b16_p24_vocab66_hash_replica.log
Result:
- h8/b16/p24 with `AIDEEN_ASSOC_HASH_REPLICA=1` produced eval loss=0.1293 vs random=4.1897 (3.1% of random), classified MEMORY WORKS.
- This is a large improvement over h8/b16/p24 single-owner hash lane loss=2.4274 and h8/b8/p24 loss=5.4506.
Classification:
- Two-lane hash replication: experimental useful. It validates multi-probe/replicated lane routing as the correct direction for scalable exact Assoc capacity.
Next validation:
- Check p16/b8 with replica for no-regression and then run additional seeds/profiles before promoting any default.

Validation - hash replication p16/b8 no-regression failed
---------------------------------------------------------

Result:

Classification:
- `AIDEEN_ASSOC_HASH_REPLICA=1` is not safe as a general default. It is experimental and must be paired with enough banks or a smarter adaptive replication policy.
Next action:

Validation - hash replication p16/b16
-------------------------------------
Log:
- logs/assoc_recall/scale/lanes_h8_b16_p16_hash_replica.log
Result:
- p16/b16 with replication produced eval loss=2.7617 (70.6% of random), only partial. This means the p24 success is real but the replica policy is not yet a universally stable routing default.
Classification:
- Two-lane replication: experimental useful for high-capacity p24/b16 corridor, not default-stable.
- Bank cap 16: useful layout enabler, but needs further no-regression validation before default promotion.
Next action:
- Keep `AIDEEN_ASSOC_HASH_REPLICA` off by default. Next structural work should make replication adaptive or improve write salience/replacement so low-pair corridors do not get over-replicated.

Change gate - adaptive hash replication instead of unconditional replica
-----------------------------------------------------------------------
1. Target failure mode: `AIDEEN_ASSOC_HASH_REPLICA=1` solves h8/b16/p24 (loss=0.1293) but breaks smaller-capacity p16/b8 (loss=5.7171) and remains partial on p16/b16. Unconditional duplication doubles write pressure and can consume capacity when the bank budget does not need redundancy.
2. Structural rationale: replication should be a capacity/collision policy, not a blanket behavior. The invariant is: use single-owner writes when bank budget is tight or pair density is low; use two-lane writes when banks per lane are large enough to absorb duplicate writes and reduce collision risk. A conservative structural gate is `ASSOC_BANKS >= 16`, which preserves banks=8 behavior exactly and keeps the validated p24/b16 path available.
3. Anti-patch check: this does not tune loss, use AR labels, or depend on target tokens. It restores the capacity invariant by preventing a collision-mitigation mechanism from reducing effective capacity in small-bank profiles. It remains behind `AIDEEN_ASSOC_HASH_REPLICA=1`; default behavior is unchanged.
4. Validation plan: modify WGSL so `ENABLE_ASSOC_HASH_REPLICA` is effective only when `ASSOC_BANKS >= 16`; cargo check; rerun p16/b8 with replica to verify old behavior no longer regresses; rerun p24/b16 with replica to verify high-capacity benefit remains.
Classification target: experimental useful / adaptive dynamics pending validation.

Validation - adaptive hash replication
--------------------------------------
Logs:
- logs/assoc_recall/scale/lanes_h8_b8_p16_hash_replica_adaptive.log
- logs/assoc_recall/scale/lanes_h8_b16_p24_hash_replica_adaptive.log
Results:
- h8/b8/p16 with `AIDEEN_ASSOC_HASH_REPLICA=1` and adaptive guard produced eval loss=1.4310 vs random=3.9120. This matches the old small-bank corridor behavior closely enough and confirms the guard prevents the previous catastrophic p16/b8 regression.
- h8/b16/p24 with adaptive replica produced eval loss=0.8810 vs random=4.1897, classified MEMORY WORKS. It remains much better than single-owner h8/b16/p24 loss=2.4274 and h8/b8/p24 loss=5.4506, but worse than the earlier replica run loss=0.1293.
Classification:
- Adaptive hash replication: experimental useful, not default stable. The structural direction is validated: multi-probe/replicated lanes can solve high pair density when enough banks exist, while adaptive gating preserves low-bank behavior.
- `AIDEEN_ASSOC_HASH_REPLICA` remains off by default. Even with the guard, the p16/b16 partial result and p24 run variance require more validation before promotion.
- Bank cap 16 remains an experimental capacity enabler, not a mandatory baseline.
Anti-patch conclusion:
- The change is not a symptom mask because it corrects the collision/capacity invariant at the routing level: duplicate writes are only allowed when bank capacity can absorb them. It does not depend on AR labels, token positions, or narrow loss thresholds.
Next action:
- Move from capacity expansion to write salience/replacement policy. The remaining issue is not merely number of banks; the model needs a principled way to decide which bindings deserve durable slots when lanes approach saturation. Candidate: salience from explicit Assoc evidence plus query/value confidence, with FPM used for contextual consolidation rather than literal replacement.

Validation - p32 capacity edge with adaptive replica
---------------------------------------------------
Log:
- logs/assoc_recall/scale/lanes_h8_b16_p32_hash_replica_adaptive.log
Result:
- h8/b16/p32 with adaptive replica produced eval loss=0.0941 vs random=4.4067, classified MEMORY WORKS.
- This profile uses 32 key/value pairs with 4 active Assoc lanes and 16 banks per lane. With two-lane replication, it is near the natural effective capacity edge because each pair can occupy two deterministic lanes.
Classification:
- The scalable Assoc capacity corridor is now validated for p24 and p32 under h8/b16/hash-lane/hash-replica.
- Remaining risk is not the basic token circuit or LM debug metric; it is policy under overflow beyond effective capacity and variance across seeds.
Next validation:
- Run p40 or p48 only as an overflow stress test, not as a baseline expectation. If overflow fails, implement salience/replacement rather than adding blind capacity.

Validation - p40 overflow stress with adaptive replica
-----------------------------------------------------
Log:
- logs/assoc_recall/scale/lanes_h8_b16_p40_hash_replica_adaptive.log
Result:
- h8/b16/p40 with adaptive replica produced eval loss=4.0964 vs random=4.5850, classified near-random.
- This contrasts with p32 loss=0.0941 under the same h8/b16/hash-replica geometry.
Classification:
- p40 is an overflow failure, not a whole-circuit failure. The model can solve up to p32 in this profile, then degrades when requested bindings exceed effective durable capacity.
- The next fix should not be more LM-head work or FPM scale tuning. It should target Assoc durable slot policy: salience, eviction/replacement, or larger bank/lane geometry with explicit capacity accounting.
Root-cause conclusion:
- Current `ENABLE_ASSOC_PROTECT_OCCUPIED` makes occupied banks effectively immutable unless the new key reuses the same bank. That is correct for exact recall below capacity, but it provides no principled behavior above capacity. The overflow regime needs a salience/replacement invariant, otherwise late or important bindings can be blocked by earlier low-value bindings.
Next change gate candidate:
- Add an experimental salience-aware replacement path behind a flag. It must store/update bank salience separately from mere occupancy or reinterpret usage as salience only under the experimental flag. Validation must compare p32 no-regression and p40 improvement.

Change gate - experimental low-usage replacement for Assoc overflow
------------------------------------------------------------------
1. Target failure mode: h8/b16/hash-replica solves p32 but p40 falls near random. The circuit works below effective capacity, but once all banks are occupied `ENABLE_ASSOC_PROTECT_OCCUPIED` blocks novel writes unless they reuse an existing key. Overflow has no salience/eviction mechanism.
2. Structural rationale: below capacity, empty-first placement is correct for exact recall. Above capacity, the required invariant changes: if no empty bank exists and the new key is novel, the system must have a deterministic replacement candidate. The current usage scalar already decays (`ASSOC_USAGE_DECAY`) and is the only per-bank durability metadata available in this layout, so an experimental replacement path can choose `min_usage_bank` only when `found_empty=false` and key similarity is below the reuse threshold.
3. Anti-patch check: this does not touch LM logits, loss scaling, labels, or AR-specific positions. It changes only the overflow bank-allocation invariant and remains behind `AIDEEN_ASSOC_REPLACE_LOW_USAGE=1`; default behavior stays unchanged.
4. Validation plan: add a shader override and Rust compile constants; verify `cargo check`; run p32 no-regression and p40 overflow test with the flag. Correct behavior requires p40 improvement without destroying p32.
Classification target: experimental useful if p40 improves and p32 remains solved; rejected if p32 regresses materially or p40 stays near random.

Validation - low-usage replacement rejected
-------------------------------------------
Log:
- logs/assoc_recall/scale/lanes_h8_b16_p32_replace_low_usage.log
Result:
- p32 with experimental low-usage replacement regressed to eval loss=4.1107 vs random=4.4067. Baseline p32 without replacement was eval loss=0.0941.
Classification:
- Low-usage replacement as implemented is rejected and removed. The usage scalar is not a valid salience signal for exact Assoc replacement; using it for eviction destroys already-valid bindings.
Causal lesson:
- Overflow cannot be solved by reinterpreting occupancy/usage as importance. The model needs a separate salience signal or capacity expansion. A correct salience mechanism must distinguish durable semantic/value importance from mere recency/occupancy before it is allowed to evict a bank.
Next action:
- Preserve the validated h8/b16/hash-replica p32 corridor. Future overflow work should add explicit bank metadata for salience or test larger bank geometry; do not reuse `usage` as eviction priority.

Validation - existing event gate on real-training Assoc selectivity
-------------------------------------------------------------------

Root-cause conclusion:
- The failure is not only write magnitude; it is durable admission. Weak writes still occupy banks because any positive committed mass above the tiny occupied threshold eventually marks banks as used.

Change gate - experimental minimum durable Assoc write mass
----------------------------------------------------------
1. Target failure mode: real text fills all h8/b16 Assoc banks in 8,192 tokens even with event gating. Weak writes are treated as durable admissions, so the memory fills with low-confidence transitions.
2. Structural rationale: continuous write strength and durable admission are different invariants. A binding should enter durable Assoc only if its effective write mass exceeds an explicit admission threshold; otherwise it can influence transient/FPM dynamics without consuming a bank.
3. Anti-patch check: this is not loss masking or AR-specific filtering. It corrects the memory allocation rule at the point where weak evidence becomes durable storage. It remains behind `AIDEEN_ASSOC_WRITE_MIN_MASS`, default 0.0, so current behavior is unchanged unless explicitly enabled.
4. Validation plan: add shader override and Rust constants; cargo check; run real-text audit with event gate and min mass; then rerun p32 recall to ensure the threshold does not destroy validated exact recall if considered for promotion.
Classification target: experimental useful if real-text occupancy drops without p32 regression.

Change gate - sparse non-degenerate event-gate initialization
------------------------------------------------------------
1. Target failure mode: `AIDEEN_ASSOC_EVENT_GATE=1` lowers Assoc write mass but still fills every bank because `W_event_assoc=0` and `b_event_assoc=0` initialize the event gate as a constant `sigmoid(0)=0.5`, not as a transition selector.
2. Structural rationale: a learned durable-binding event gate must start with both a sparse prior and non-degenerate transition features. Bias controls base write probability; event weights let different token transitions produce different logits before learning has already filled memory.
3. Anti-patch check: this does not filter by labels, positions, token ids, or benchmark structure. It fixes the classifier initialization invariant. Defaults remain exactly neutral (`bias=0`, `w_init=0`) unless `AIDEEN_ASSOC_EVENT_BIAS_INIT` / `AIDEEN_ASSOC_EVENT_W_INIT` are set.
4. Validation plan: add configurable initialization; cargo check; run real-text audit with sparse event init plus min-mass; validate that occupancy is partial rather than 16/16 or 0/16; later rerun p32 recall before promoting.
Classification target: experimental useful if it creates nontrivial selectivity.

Validation - sparse event init and min-mass probes
-------------------------------------------------
Logs:
- logs/training_real/h8_b16_replica_event_gate_minmass030_assoc_audit_4chunks.log
- logs/training_real/h8_b16_replica_event_gate_minmass015_assoc_audit_4chunks.log
- logs/training_real/h8_b16_replica_event_gate_minmass024_assoc_audit_4chunks.log
- logs/training_real/h8_b16_replica_sparse_event_w1_b-2_min015_assoc_audit_4chunks.log
- logs/training_real/h8_b16_replica_sparse_event_w01_b-2_min015_assoc_audit_4chunks.log
- logs/training_real/h8_b16_replica_sparse_event_w02_b-4_min015_assoc_audit_4chunks.log
Results:
- `min_mass=0.30` with zero event weights blocked all writes (`0/16`).
- `min_mass=0.15` and `0.24` with neutral event init still filled all banks (`16/16`).
- Sparse event init `w=1.0,b=-2,min=0.15` saturated memory and produced loss=22.9376.
- `w=0.1,b=-2,min=0.15` and `w=0.2,b=-4,min=0.15` still filled all banks.
Classification:
- Fixed min-mass threshold and random sparse event init are rejected as sufficient selectivity mechanisms. Keep the code paths only as experimental knobs with default-neutral behavior; do not promote.
Root-cause conclusion:
- Durable admission cannot be solved by a scalar threshold over an uncalibrated event gate. The system needs a budgeted/promotion-based policy: local candidates may be written transiently, but durable Assoc should only promote a bounded number of high-evidence bindings per segment/document.
Federated-training implication:
- In federated training, each node seeing different documents makes local write noise more dangerous. If every node fills durable memory with document-local low-salience transitions, weight integration averages incompatible write policies. A document-local promotion budget is a better fit because it bounds each node's memory gradient contribution.
Next action:
- Add diagnostics for event/write mass distribution or implement a gated promotion corridor where durable writes are budgeted per segment before scaling banks further.

Validation - thresholded Assoc occupancy audit
----------------------------------------------
Log:
- logs/training_real/h8_b16_replica_event_gate_assoc_audit_thresholds_4chunks.log
Result:
- Short release train with event gate, 8,192 tokens, `tps_epoch=141.9`.
- `[ASSOC-STATE]` showed every Assoc slot at `16/16`, with `>.05=16`, `>.20=15`, `>.80=0` for each slot.
Classification:
- The banks are not merely touched by tiny noise; almost all banks receive moderate durable mass around 0.2-0.25. This confirms weak-to-moderate over-admission.
Next action:
- Implement budgeted promotion / candidate selection rather than fixed threshold tuning. Desired invariant for federated training: each document/node contributes bounded high-evidence durable writes, not all local transitions.

Change gate - experimental durable Assoc write budget
-----------------------------------------------------
1. Target failure mode: real text fills every h8/b16 Assoc bank rapidly because every moderate transition can become durable. Previous scalar thresholds/event init either blocked all writes or still filled all banks, so durable admission lacks a bounded promotion policy.
2. Structural rationale: durable Assoc banks are scarce exact-memory slots. As a diagnostic first step toward promotion, add an explicit per-slot durable write budget: novel empty-bank writes are admitted only while occupied banks in that lane are below `ASSOC_WRITE_BUDGET`; reuse writes to an existing matching key remain allowed. This tests whether bounded durable admission prevents immediate bank saturation without changing default behavior.
3. Anti-patch check: the budget is disabled by default (`0 = unlimited`) and does not use labels, token IDs, AR positions, or loss. It does not claim salience is solved; it isolates whether capacity-bounded admission is the missing layer. If it preserves occupancy but stores useless early transitions, the result proves that a ranking/salience selector is required next.
4. Validation plan: add WGSL override and Rust plumbing for `AIDEEN_ASSOC_WRITE_BUDGET`; cargo check; run a short real-text audit with h8/b16/hash-replica/event-gate and budget values. Success for the diagnostic means occupancy stays below full saturation and no NaNs. Quality/utility requires later salience validation.
Classification target: experimental diagnostic, not default.

Validation - durable Assoc write budget controls real-text saturation
---------------------------------------------------------------------
Log:
- logs/training_real/h8_b16_replica_event_gate_budget4_assoc_audit_4chunks.log
Command summary:
- release train, tinyshakespeare, batch=4, ctx_len=512, max_chunks=4
- `AIDEEN_H_SLOTS=8 AIDEEN_ASSOC_BANKS=16 AIDEEN_ASSOC_SLOT_OWNER=1 AIDEEN_ASSOC_HASH_LANE=1 AIDEEN_ASSOC_HASH_REPLICA=1 AIDEEN_ASSOC_EVENT_GATE=1 AIDEEN_ASSOC_AUDIT=1 AIDEEN_ASSOC_WRITE_BUDGET=4`
Result:
- Runtime completed on Apple M1 Pro GPU, no NaNs or shader panic.
- Throughput dropped to `tps_epoch=67.7` for this heavy audited corridor.
- `[ASSOC-STATE] s4:4/16 >.05=4 >.20=4 >.80=0 mean=5.859e-2 max=2.438e-1 | s5:4/16 >.05=4 >.20=4 >.80=0 mean=5.720e-2 max=2.431e-1 | s6:4/16 >.05=4 >.20=4 >.80=0 mean=5.808e-2 max=2.438e-1 | s7:4/16 >.05=4 >.20=3 >.80=0 mean=5.555e-2 max=2.366e-1`.

- Not default-stable as a standalone policy because it only caps early admissions; it does not decide which transitions are worth preserving.
Root-cause conclusion:
- The next missing mechanism is salience/ranking/promotion, not another scalar threshold. A correct policy needs a transient candidate pool or promotion score so the limited durable budget is spent on high-evidence bindings rather than first-arriving ordinary transitions.
Next action:
- Add diagnostics or a candidate-promotion path that separates transient local writes from durable Assoc writes. Minimum next diagnostic: measure how many writes are blocked by budget and expose event/write-mass distribution so salience can be designed from evidence, not guessed.

Change gate - Assoc budget admission telemetry
----------------------------------------------
1. Target failure mode: `AIDEEN_ASSOC_WRITE_BUDGET=4` prevents full real-text saturation, but the model remains near-random/high-loss. We do not know whether the budget is blocking many meaningful candidates, only ordinary low-salience writes, or mostly allowing reuse. Without this measurement, a promotion policy would be guessed.
2. Structural rationale: durable Assoc needs a two-stage invariant: candidate generation may be dense/local, but durable admission must be bounded and rankable. The current budget implements the bound; telemetry must expose the admission path variables at the same allocation point: empty-candidate rate, blocked-by-budget rate, reuse rate, occupied count, and pre-protect write intent.
3. Anti-patch check: this change does not alter equations, thresholds, logits, memory contents, loss, or default runtime behavior. It observes the exact mechanism that decides durable bank admission, so it supports root-cause decomposition instead of hiding the high-loss symptom.
4. Validation plan: add temporary DebugLog fields and trainer decoding under existing debug/audit flags; cargo check; run a short real-text h8/b16 budgeted audit with `AIDEEN_DEBUG_SAMPLE=1`. Success means logs report finite per-slot admission telemetry alongside `[ASSOC-STATE]`, allowing the next promotion/salience change to be designed from observed distributions.
Classification target: diagnostic temporary; remove or consolidate after promotion policy is validated.

Change gate - LM head gradient source telemetry
-----------------------------------------------
1. Target failure mode: budgeted Assoc forward stays finite, but backward receives `v_state`/`dl_dh` magnitudes around 1e7-1e10, so training signals into Assoc/FPM are unusable and the model remains random.
2. Structural rationale: before changing Assoc dynamics, isolate the source of the adjoint magnitude. The LM head owns `dl_dh`; if LM `W`/`g` are already huge, the failure is parameter/update scaling. If LM `W`/`g` are normal while `dl_dh` is huge, the failure is in LM backprop formula/layout or an upstream assoc-logit RHS path.
3. Anti-patch check: this is diagnostic-only under `AIDEEN_BACKWARD_INPUT_PROBE`; it does not clamp gradients, alter learning rates, or mask the explosion. It measures the exact producer of the invalid adjoint.
4. Validation plan: print LM `W` and `g` stats alongside existing hpooled/dl_dh/assoc_rhs/adj_v probes; run a short GPU corridor. Success means the next fix targets either LM parameter corruption or LM backprop/layout, not Assoc slot policy.
Classification target: diagnostic temporary.

Change gate - LM sampled-softmax backprop cache capacity parity
---------------------------------------------------------------
1. Target failure mode: LM `dl_dh` is finite but absurdly large (`rms≈3.4e7`) while `hpooled`, `W_lm`, `b_lm`, and `g_lm` are normal. This corrupts the Picard adjoint and then Assoc/FPM backward.
2. Structural rationale: `build_sampled_indices` and LM forward allow up to 2048 sampled logits, and `lm_probs_main` allocates `s_indices_cache`/`s_logits` as 2048-element workgroup arrays. `lm_backprop_h_t_main` cached `probs` into a 512-element workgroup array while iterating `k < params.num_samples`; when `num_samples > 512`, it wrote out of bounds in workgroup memory, corrupting the gradient computation. The required invariant is identical sampled-softmax capacity across forward and backward caches.
3. Anti-patch check: this does not clamp gradients, lower LR, disable Assoc, or hide exploding values. It restores a shader layout/capacity invariant at the origin of the invalid `dl_dh` producer and remains valid across seeds as long as `MAX_SHADER_SAMPLES=2048`.
4. Validation plan: change `s_probs_cache` from 512 to 2048; cargo check; rerun the 1-chunk LM weight/backward probe. Success means `dl_dh` and `adj_v_out` fall from ~1e7 to a scale consistent with LM weights (~1e-3 to small finite values), and Assoc backward `val_rms` no longer enters ~1e10.
Classification target: layout/invariant fix; candidate default stable if validation passes.

Investigation note - LM cache parity not sufficient
---------------------------------------------------
Validation log:
- logs/training_real/h8_b16_budget4_lm_cache_fix_probe_1chunk.log
- logs/training_real/h8_b16_budget4_lm_debug_after_cache_fix_1chunk.log
Result:
- `s_probs_cache` capacity parity fixed and compile passed.
- `num_samples=2048`, so the active corridor fits the 2048 shader arrays.
- `dl_dh` remains huge (`rms≈2.5e7`) while `lm_w`, `lm_b`, and `lm_g` are normal.
Classification:
- 512->2048 cache fix remains a valid layout/invariant fix, but it is not sufficient to resolve the current gradient explosion.
Next diagnostic:
- Read `probs` and `rms_buf` under `AIDEEN_BACKWARD_INPUT_PROBE` to determine whether LM forward softmax/RMS output is already corrupt or whether corruption occurs only in `lm_backprop_h_t_main`.

Change gate - LM sampled-softmax storage-backed probability invariant
---------------------------------------------------------------------
1. Target failure mode: after cache-capacity parity, `lm_probs` still reports `max≈1e10` while it should contain normalized probabilities in `[0,1]`. `dl_dh` and `assoc_rhs` remain ~1e7, proving corruption is produced inside the LM sampled-softmax/probability path before the DEQ adjoint.
2. Structural rationale: LM forward/backward currently rely on module-scope workgroup arrays sized for up to 2048 samples (`s_indices_cache`, `s_logits`, `s_probs_cache`). The probability source of truth is already the storage buffer `probs`; keeping duplicate workgroup caches for a large sampled set creates a second fragile layout/capacity contract and allows corruption of the normalized probability invariant. The structural fix is to make `probs` the single source of truth: initialize logits in `probs`, accumulate logits in `probs`, normalize `probs`, and have backprop read `probs`/`sampled_indices` directly from storage.
3. Anti-patch check: this does not clamp `dl_dh`, lower learning rates, disable Assoc, or tune thresholds. It removes the duplicated cache mechanism that violates the invariant `0 <= probs[t,k] <= 1` and `sum_k probs[t,k] ≈ 1` before gradients are computed. If correct, the same fix remains valid for any seed/profile using sampled softmax.
4. Validation plan: remove large sampled workgroup caches; cargo check; rerun `AIDEEN_BACKWARD_INPUT_PROBE` 1-chunk corridor. Success means `lm_probs.max <= 1`, finite `lm_rms`, and `dl_dh` drops to the scale implied by `W_lm` (`~1e-3` to small finite), with Assoc backward no longer seeing `val_rms≈1e10`.
Classification target: layout/invariant fix; candidate default stable if validation passes.

Change gate - LM sampled-softmax serial normalization corridor
--------------------------------------------------------------
1. Target failure mode: `lm_probs` violates probability invariants (`row0_sum≈1.7e13`, `max=1e10`, millions of entries >1) even though `hpooled`, `assoc_pooled`, `lm_rms`, `W_lm`, `b_lm`, and `g_lm` are finite/normal. This produces `dl_dh≈1e7` before the DEQ adjoint.
2. Structural rationale: logits are finite but the workgroup softmax reduction is producing an invalid denominator (`sm` effectively clamped to `1e-10`). The probability invariant must be restored at the normalization equation itself: for each token, compute `mx=max_k(logit_k)` and `sm=sum_k exp(logit_k-mx)` over the full sampled set, then normalize all `probs[t,k]` by that same scalar. A serial `tid==0` normalization is the minimal correctness corridor because it removes reduction/race ambiguity while preserving the exact softmax equation.
3. Anti-patch check: this does not clamp probabilities or gradients after the fact. It computes the correct denominator at the origin of the invalid probability distribution. TPS may drop, but this is a stabilization corridor; once validated, the same invariant can be re-parallelized safely.
4. Validation plan: replace LM softmax max/sum workgroup reductions with serial per-token normalization; cargo check; rerun 1-chunk `AIDEEN_BACKWARD_INPUT_PROBE`. Success means `lm_probs_inv row0_sum≈1`, `gt1=0`, `max<=1`, and `dl_dh` collapses from ~1e7 to a small finite scale.
Classification target: layout/equation invariant fix; candidate default-correct but performance-sensitive.

Validation - LM serial softmax restores gradient scale
------------------------------------------------------
Log:
- logs/training_real/h8_b16_budget4_lm_serial_softmax_probe_1chunk.log
Result:
- `assoc_pooled` was normal before LM (`rms=2.016e-1`, `max=1.091e0`), so the Assoc->LM bridge was not the source of the 1e7 gradient.
- `lm_probs` invariant restored: `row0_sum=1.000019e0`, `gt1=0`, `neg=0`, `max=1.790e-3`.
- `dl_dh` collapsed from previous `~2.5e7` to `3.032e-6`; `assoc_rhs` collapsed to `4.619e-6`; `adj_v_out` collapsed to `1.018e-6`.
- Assoc backward `val_rms` collapsed from `~1e10` to `~1.2e-3`. The remaining large `wq_step_max` is diagnostic only because `AIDEEN_ASSOC_ADDR_LR_MULT` defaults to 0.0 and address updates are intentionally frozen in this corridor.
Classification:
- LM serial softmax: default-correct equation/invariant fix, performance-sensitive.
- LM cache-removal/storage source-of-truth: layout/invariant cleanup that simplifies the circuit and removes duplicated sampled-set state.
- LM/RMS/probs readbacks: temporary diagnostics, keep until the next stable corridor confirms gradients remain finite without debug.
Root-cause conclusion:
- A major cause of apparent random/stalled training was not Assoc slot distribution. The LM sampled-softmax denominator path corrupted probabilities, causing invalid `dl_dh`, then invalid Picard adjoints, then unusable Assoc/FPM backward signals. Stabilization must continue from this corrected gradient corridor.
Next action:
- Run the same h8/b16/budget4 corridor for 4 chunks without heavy probability readback, confirm no gradient explosion and measure TPS/loss. Then decide whether to re-parallelize softmax safely or keep the serial corridor while investigating Assoc salience/promotion.

Validation - LM serial softmax 4-chunk corridor without heavy LM readback
-------------------------------------------------------------------------
Log:
- logs/training_real/h8_b16_budget4_lm_serial_softmax_4chunks.log
Command summary:
- release train, tinyshakespeare, batch=4, ctx_len=512, max_chunks=4, seed=42
- `AIDEEN_H_SLOTS=8 AIDEEN_ASSOC_BANKS=16 AIDEEN_ASSOC_SLOT_OWNER=1 AIDEEN_ASSOC_HASH_LANE=1 AIDEEN_ASSOC_HASH_REPLICA=1 AIDEEN_ASSOC_EVENT_GATE=1 AIDEEN_ASSOC_AUDIT=1 AIDEEN_ASSOC_WRITE_BUDGET=4 AIDEEN_DEBUG_SAMPLE=1`
Result:
- Runtime completed on Apple M1 Pro GPU, no NaNs or shader panic.
- `tps_epoch=132.8`, `loss=7.6795`, `tokens=8192`.
- Assoc value-gradient scale stayed finite and small across chunks: active Assoc slots reported `val_rms` around `1.1e-3` to `1.5e-3`, not the previous `~1e10` explosion.
- `wq_update_max=0` and `wk_update_max=0` by design because address learning remains frozen in this corridor via `AIDEEN_ASSOC_ADDR_LR_MULT=0.0`. Large `wq_step_max` is therefore a diagnostic gradient magnitude, not an applied parameter update.
- `[ASSOC-STATE]` ended at 4/16 occupied for active Assoc slots s4-s7, confirming the budget still prevents immediate bank saturation.
- `[ASSOC-BUDGET]` showed uneven admission pressure: s4/s5 had high block rates (`0.371`, `0.419`) and occupancy 4.00; s6/s7 reported near-zero final occupancy in budget telemetry despite `[ASSOC-STATE]` showing 4/16 occupied, which indicates a diagnostic/telemetry lifetime or slot-index interpretation mismatch to inspect before using those fields as policy evidence.
- FPM remains structurally separated in this corridor: write activity is in slots 0-3, while durable Assoc occupancy is in slots 4-7.
Classification:
- LM serial softmax remains validated as the current correctness corridor for sampled-softmax probability invariants and backward gradient scale.
- Assoc write budget remains experimental useful, not a quality solution.
- Assoc budget telemetry is diagnostic temporary and now has a suspected inconsistency for s6/s7 that must be resolved before designing promotion from those counters.
Root-cause conclusion:
- The previous catastrophic backward instability is resolved at the LM probability denominator equation. The model still being near-random after 8k tokens is no longer explained by NaN/exploding gradients in this corridor; the next causal focus is memory utility: which slots write, which slots are read, whether budget telemetry matches actual memory state, and whether FPM/Assoc role separation prevents useful information from reaching the LM path.
Next action:
- Inspect the Assoc budget telemetry indices/lifetime against `[ASSOC-STATE]` decoding, then run a no-debug 4-chunk corridor to measure cleaner TPS/loss. After telemetry parity is fixed, design the promotion/salience policy from reliable counters rather than guessed thresholds.
