Change gate - LM sampled-softmax invariant-safe parallel normalization
----------------------------------------------------------------------
1. Target failure mode: the serial LM softmax restores probability/gradient invariants but drops the corridor to roughly `67.8 TPS` on the no-debug 4-chunk run, making it unsuitable as the long-term training path.
2. Structural rationale: the softmax equation does not require serial execution; it requires a single correct row max and row denominator over all `params.num_samples`. Keep `probs` as the only logits/probabilities storage, but compute max and sum with workgroup reductions. Use separate workgroup scratch arrays for denominator and target numerator so `sum_k probs[t,k] ~= 1` and target CE remains identical to the serial equation.
3. Anti-patch check: this does not change LR, sampled count, clamp gradients, reduce capacity, or hide the slow path. It reimplements the same validated equation at the normalization origin while preserving the probability invariant that fixed `dl_dh`.
4. Validation plan: cargo check; run the 1-chunk `AIDEEN_BACKWARD_INPUT_PROBE` corridor and require `lm_probs_inv row0_sum ~= 1`, `gt1=0`, `neg=0`, `dl_dh` small finite, and active Assoc `val_rms ~1e-3`; then run the no-debug 4-chunk corridor and compare TPS/loss.
Classification target: equation/layout invariant optimization; promote only if invariant probe matches serial corridor.

Change gate - Assoc read telemetry batch isolation
--------------------------------------------------
1. Target failure mode: `[ASSOC-READ]` can report internally inconsistent fields, e.g. effective `qpick` near zero while `qctx` is nonzero for the same slot/token. This can happen because some read debug fields are written by all batches, while budget/write diagnostics are batch-isolated.
2. Structural rationale: diagnostics must observe a single causal path. Restrict Assoc read/query/context DebugLog writes to `batch_idx == 0u`, matching other diagnostics, so entropy, selected bank, selected probability, and context RMS correspond to the same batch lane.
3. Anti-patch check: this only changes debug writes under `debug_on`; it does not change AssocBuf, AssocReadBuf, H_next, logits, gradients, slot ownership, or any training equation. It fixes measurement provenance rather than masking model behavior.
4. Validation plan: cargo check; rerun 1-chunk audited corridor and verify `[ASSOC-READ]` fields no longer show impossible combinations like `qpick@0` with nonzero `qctx` for hard gated reads.
Classification target: measurement/diagnostic fix; candidate stable for diagnostics.

Change gate - experimental Assoc alpha init override
----------------------------------------------------
1. Target failure mode: disabling Assoc read improves short-run loss, suggesting read injection is too strong or semantically premature. `alpha_assoc` is documented as a residual read mix and initialized to `0.3`, but the shader interprets it as a sigmoid logit, producing `sigmoid(0.3)=0.574` before additional read normalization.
2. Structural rationale: add an experimental initialization override for the stored alpha parameter so we can test the injection-amplitude hypothesis without changing default behavior or rewriting the forward/backward alpha parameterization. This isolates whether lower initial Assoc read mix restores the benefit of keeping reads enabled.
3. Anti-patch check: the override is opt-in (`AIDEEN_ASSOC_ALPHA_INIT`) and does not clamp gradients, disable reads, or alter memory contents by default. It tests a specific semantic mismatch in the alpha parameter path before any default architectural change.
4. Validation plan: cargo check; run h8/b16/budget4 with `AIDEEN_ASSOC_READ=1`, `AIDEEN_ASSOC_LOGIT_LAMBDA=0`, and low alpha init values. If lower alpha approaches or beats `AIDEEN_ASSOC_READ=0` loss while preserving stability, the root cause is read injection amplitude/parameter semantics.
Classification target: experimental diagnostic knob; not default stable until multi-seed validation.

- `alpha_assoc` parameter semantics are inconsistent: model code documents/initializes it like a direct residual mix (`0.3`), while WGSL treats it as a sigmoid logit (`sigmoid(0.3)=0.574`). The next test is the semantic correction `logit(0.3)≈-0.847`.

- Run `AIDEEN_ASSOC_ALPHA_INIT=-0.847` to test whether intended `alpha≈0.3` is stable, then decide whether to convert initialization/defaults to logit space or keep a low read gate until promotion is validated.

Change gate - Default alpha_assoc logit-space initialization
------------------------------------------------------------
1. Target failure mode: default Assoc read injection degrades short-run loss. The model initializes `alpha_assoc=0.3` as if it were a residual mix coefficient, but forward/backward shaders treat it as a sigmoid logit, giving effective alpha `0.574` instead of intended `0.3`.
2. Structural rationale: align parameter initialization with the equation actually used by GPU forward/backward. If `alpha_effective = sigmoid(alpha_param)`, then an intended initial mix of `0.3` must store `logit(0.3)≈-0.847`. This restores the required invariant: documented/init effective read mix equals shader effective read mix.
3. Anti-patch check: this does not clamp reads, disable Assoc, reduce banks, lower LR, or hide loss. It corrects the parameter-space mismatch at the source and remains valid across seeds/profiles because it aligns the stored parameter with the sigmoid equation.
4. Validation plan: change default initialization/comment; cargo check; rerun h8/b16/budget4 with reads/logit lambda default corridor or explicit lambda0/read-on corridor. Success means read-on no longer degrades relative to read-off in the short corridor, while no NaNs and Assoc occupancy remain controlled.
Classification target: default stable initialization fix if validation passes.

Change gate - Disable Assoc LM-logit bridge by default
------------------------------------------------------
1. Target failure mode: direct Assoc-pooled contribution to LM logits worsens short-run real-text loss and can add significant runtime cost, even after alpha read injection semantics are corrected.
2. Structural rationale: Assoc should first affect the model through validated memory read dynamics and later through a confidence/promotion-aware LM bridge. The current LM bridge treats normalized retrieved literal values as direct logit features via embedding dot products without a validated salience/confidence gate, so it couples unproven memory content directly to token prediction.
3. Anti-patch check: this does not remove Assoc storage, disable Assoc reads, reduce capacity, or hide numerical failure. It changes only the default coupling of an unvalidated auxiliary logit path. The path remains available via `AIDEEN_ASSOC_LOGIT_LAMBDA` for explicit experiments after promotion/read utility improves.
4. Validation plan: change `GpuLmHeadTrainer` default assoc logit lambda to `0.0`; cargo check; run the h8/b16/budget4 no-env corridor and require no NaNs, controlled Assoc occupancy, and loss/TPS comparable to the explicit lambda0 run.
Classification target: default stable for current training corridor; experimental bridge retained behind env.

Change gate - Assoc read confidence based on key match, not hard-read probability
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
1. Target failure mode: hard-read Assoc returns a bank with probability 1 even when the query/key match is weak. `ENABLE_ASSOC_CONF_READ` currently gates by `read_max_prob`, which is always 1 under hard-read, so the confidence gate is structurally inert in the default retrieval mode.
2. Structural rationale: explicit associative memory should inject a retrieved value only in proportion to address confidence. The source invariant is key-query similarity, not post-selection probability. Compute read confidence from the pre-hard-read best address cosine (`max_score / ASSOC_READ_BETA`, clamped to `[0,1]`) and use that when `ENABLE_ASSOC_CONF_READ=1`.
3. Anti-patch check: this does not disable Assoc, reduce capacity, clamp gradients, or tune loss directly. It corrects an existing gate so it observes the causal matching variable instead of an artifact of winner-take-all selection. The path remains opt-in until validated.
4. Validation plan: cargo check; run h8/b16/budget4 with `AIDEEN_ASSOC_CONF_READ=1`, lambda0, corrected alpha default. Success means no NaNs, controlled occupancy, and loss not worse than unconfident read-on; if it approaches read-off/low-alpha corridor, confidence gating is a valid structural direction.
Classification target: experimental dynamics/invariant fix; promote only after validation.

Validation - Assoc confidence-read telemetry

- Active read confidence is no longer hard-coded to 1: example s4 last-token `qpmax=0.506`, `qpick=3@0.506`, `qctx=1.266e-1` while raw read context without confidence is around `2.500e-1`.
- Slots without effective route/match report `pmax=0.000`, `ctx=0`, or `qpick@0`, confirming the corrected confidence gate can suppress weak/non-routed reads.
- Active Assoc backward `score_grad_max` fell to around `3e-5` in this diagnostic run versus earlier `~1e-4` scale, consistent with reduced read injection pressure.
Classification:
- Corrected confidence read semantics are validated as a useful experimental diagnostic/dynamics path.
- Not promoted as default yet: short 4-chunk loss improved only slightly in one run and remains within noisy corridor variance.
Root-cause conclusion:
- The current memory issue is not numerical instability and not soft read blending. The sharper diagnosis is: hard-read was selecting literal banks even when address confidence was weak, and alpha/logit bridge scaling made those selected values too influential. We have now corrected alpha semantics, disabled unvalidated LM logit coupling by default, and made confidence read meaningful when enabled.
Next action:
- Continue toward promotion/read utility: design durable promotion so occupied banks contain predictive bindings, then retest `AIDEEN_ASSOC_CONF_READ=1` and positive `AIDEEN_ASSOC_LOGIT_LAMBDA` after selected bindings are useful.

Change gate - experimental Assoc salience replacement
-----------------------------------------------------
1. Target failure mode: `ASSOC_WRITE_BUDGET` prevents saturation but spends durable banks on first-arriving transitions; once the budget is full, later potentially useful bindings are blocked.
2. Structural rationale: above capacity, exact memory needs a separate admission priority. Add an opt-in replacement path where the bank metadata scalar is interpreted as salience instead of mere occupancy. Candidate salience combines novelty against existing keys and value-source surprise, then replaces the lowest-salience occupied bank only when the new candidate is stronger. Default behavior remains unchanged.
3. Anti-patch check: this is not a threshold-only suppressor and does not use labels/token positions/loss. It changes the overflow policy at the origin: bounded banks should retain higher-evidence bindings instead of first arrivals. It is explicitly behind `AIDEEN_ASSOC_SALIENCE_REPLACE` because reinterpreting metadata needs validation.
4. Validation plan: add WGSL override/Rust plumbing; cargo check; run h8/b16/budget4 real-text audit. Success for experiment: no NaNs, occupancy remains bounded, budget-blocked falls where replacement occurs, and loss/read telemetry do not regress. Promotion to default requires recall no-regression later.
Classification target: experimental dynamics, not default.

Implementation note - experimental Assoc salience replacement
-------------------------------------------------------------
Files changed: `aideen-block/src/shaders/deq_slot_attn_unified_clean.wgsl`, `aideen-block/src/deq_bridge.rs`, `aideen-backbone/src/gpu_deq.rs`.
Change: added opt-in `AIDEEN_ASSOC_SALIENCE_REPLACE`. When enabled and `ASSOC_WRITE_BUDGET` is full, write admission can replace the lowest-metadata bank only if candidate salience exceeds current minimum. Candidate salience = key novelty * value-source surprise, both finite/clamped. Under this flag, bank metadata stores salience instead of committed write mass. Forward overwrite now zeros prior key/value contribution when `overwrite_bank=1`, matching the existing backward assumption in `fused_fpm_retain_bwd.wgsl`.
Classification: experimental dynamics plus forward/backward parity repair for the new experimental overwrite path. Default behavior remains unchanged because override default is false and env plumbing defaults false.
Pending validation: cargo check and h8/b16/budget4 real-text run with `AIDEEN_ASSOC_SALIENCE_REPLACE=1`.

Validation correction - salience metadata commit invariant
---------------------------------------------------------
Observed in `h8_b16_budget4_assoc_salience_replace_nodebug_4chunks.log`: run stayed finite, loss=7.5189, but `ASSOC-STATE` reported 16/16 occupied for slots 4-7 despite `ASSOC_WRITE_BUDGET=4`.
Diagnosis: not a quality failure yet; salience mode violated the metadata invariant. The old usage path stored `effective_write_mass`, so blocked writes wrote zero metadata. The new salience path stored candidate salience even when `effective_write_mass=0`, marking banks occupied without committed key/value content.
Fix: salience metadata is now committed only when `effective_write_mass > 0`. This restores the invariant that occupancy metadata means a durable write actually happened.
Classification: experimental path invariant fix. Previous salience run is invalid for occupancy conclusions.
Next validation: rerun same corridor with `AIDEEN_ASSOC_SALIENCE_REPLACE=1`, preferably with debug sample enabled to expose budget counters.

Validation correction - replacement target must be occupied
----------------------------------------------------------
Observed after metadata-commit fix: loss=7.5042 and no NaNs, but `ASSOC-STATE` still reached 16/16 with budget=4. Budget counters showed no blocking because replacement was selecting `min_usage_bank`, and `min_usage` included empty banks with usage=0. That converted replacement into out-of-budget allocation.
Fix: track `min_occupied_usage/min_occupied_usage_bank` separately and replacement can only target an already occupied bank. Empty-bank allocation remains governed only by `occupied_count < ASSOC_WRITE_BUDGET`.
Classification: experimental path invariant fix. Previous salience replacement runs are invalid for budget semantics.

Change gate - Assoc read backward parity with forward hard/conf read
-------------------------------------------------------------------
1. Target failure mode: Assoc backward diagnostics report huge `wq_step_max` while address updates are disabled. Investigation shows the backward read path computes gradients through a softmax/read-max probability even when forward uses hard-read plus address-confidence gating.
2. Structural rationale: the backward equation must differentiate the active forward read path. Forward with `ENABLE_ASSOC_HARD_READ=true` selects one bank and scales value injection by `slot_read_allowed * read_conf`, where `read_conf = clamp(best_address_score / ASSOC_READ_BETA, 0, 1)` when `ENABLE_ASSOC_CONF_READ=1`. Backward currently uses soft probabilities and `read_max_prob`, so it creates gradient for an inactive soft allocation path.
3. Anti-patch check: this does not clip or suppress the large diagnostic. It restores forward/backward path parity: hard-read backward no longer invents softmax score gradients, and confidence read uses the same address-confidence scalar as forward. Address LR remains explicitly disabled by default.
4. Validation plan: add `ENABLE_ASSOC_HARD_READ` to fused backward constants; cargo check; run the current best corridor with `AIDEEN_DEBUG_SAMPLE=1`. Success: no NaNs, loss/occupancy comparable, and `wq_step_max` collapses from ~1e9-1e10 to finite/near-zero under hard read unless a real differentiable confidence path is later added.
Classification target: backward invariant/parity fix, default-safe because it matches existing forward default hard-read semantics.

Validation result - Assoc read backward hard/conf parity, debug run
------------------------------------------------------------------
Command log: `logs/training_real/h8_b16_budget4_assoc_salience_confread_bwdhard_debug_4chunks.log`.
Result: finite run, no NaNs, budget preserved at 4/16. The target diagnostic was fixed: active Assoc slots now report `score_grad_max=0`, `wq_step_max=0`, `wk_step_max=0`, `key_grad_sum=0`, `gprev_sum=0` under hard-read, instead of previous `wq_step_max~1e9-1e10` from an inactive soft read path. Loss in this debug run was 7.5225, worse than the prior no-debug best corridor (7.4752).
Interpretation: the previous giant address gradient was confirmed as backward/forward mismatch. However, the old mismatched soft backward may have acted as an implicit surrogate. Since hard-read is non-differentiable, keeping a soft surrogate would need to be explicit and separately justified, not accidental.
Next action: rerun no-debug best corridor after parity fix to assess quality impact without debug-sample overhead/noise.

Change gate - Assoc write backward parity with linear/overwrite forward
-----------------------------------------------------------------------
1. Target failure mode: forward writes Assoc banks with `ENABLE_ASSOC_LINEAR_WRITE=true` by default and clears prior bank content on salience replacement (`overwrite_bank=1`), but fused backward still assumes squared write mass and propagates gradients through prior bank content even on overwrite.
2. Structural rationale: forward bank update is `bank' = keep * bank_prev + mass * candidate`, where `mass = e` in linear mode or `e^2` in squared mode, and `keep=0` on overwrite. Backward must use the same `mass`, `d mass / d e`, and `keep` to compute gradients for write gates, bank state, and value/key sources.
3. Anti-patch check: this is equation parity, not clipping. It removes a real forward/backward mismatch at the bank-update invariant. It remains valid across seeds/profiles because it follows the active compile-time write mode.
4. Validation plan: add `ENABLE_ASSOC_LINEAR_WRITE` to fused backward constants; update mass/derivative/keep equations; cargo check; rerun current best corridor. Success: finite, budget preserved, no return of ghost address gradients, and loss not materially worse than the current best corridor.
Classification target: default-stable backward invariant fix.

Build failure note - missing `assoc_linear_write` plumbing in gpu_deq
--------------------------------------------------------------------

Error: `cannot find value assoc_linear_write in this scope` after adding the fused backward constant.
Cause: `deq_bridge.rs` had `AIDEEN_ASSOC_LINEAR_WRITE` plumbing, but `gpu_deq.rs` forward/backward constants did not define the Rust env variable. Fix is to add `let assoc_linear_write = env_bool("AIDEEN_ASSOC_LINEAR_WRITE", true);` near the other Assoc env flags and pass it to both forward and backward constants.

Validation result - progress synchronization exposes GPU queue hazard
--------------------------------------------------------------------
Command log: `logs/training_real/h8_b16_budget4_assoc_salience_confread_progress6_nodebug.log`.
Result: same 6-chunk corridor that previously produced loss~14.94 returned to loss=7.4454 when `AIDEEN_PROGRESS_EVERY=1` forced periodic GPU waits/polls. This strongly suggests the long-run failure is not Assoc quality but GPU queue/buffer reuse synchronization.
Hypothesis: consecutive train chunks reuse mutable GPU buffers (LM params/targets/sample buffers, DEQ scratch/state, or staging/cached loss) faster than Metal has consumed prior submissions. Periodic progress polling serializes the queue and prevents stale/overwritten inputs. The fix should be a controlled synchronization/ring-buffer policy, not architecture tuning.
Next action: inspect existing sync knobs and implement/enable a minimal default sync cadence for the unstable multi-chunk path.

Change gate - default GPU chunk synchronization for file training
-----------------------------------------------------------------
1. Target failure mode: runs longer than 4 chunks can report/collapse to loss~14.9, while the same 6-chunk corridor returns loss=7.4454 when progress logging forces per-chunk GPU waits.
2. Structural rationale: the training loop reuses GPU buffers across chunks. Without a synchronization boundary, later CPU writes/submissions can race ahead of previous GPU consumption or cached loss staging in the long serialized path. A per-chunk `Maintain::Wait` restores the invariant that each chunk's mutable GPU buffers are consumed before reuse.
3. Anti-patch check: this is not loss clipping or tuning. It fixes execution ordering at the buffer-lifetime level. It remains valid across model profiles because it protects shared GPU buffer reuse, independent of Assoc/FPM equations.
4. Validation plan: default `AIDEEN_TPS_SYNC_EVERY` to 1 and use `Wait`; cargo check; rerun 6/8 chunk corridor without progress logging. Success: loss returns to ~7.4-7.5 and budget remains 4/16. TPS impact is measured explicitly.
Classification target: default-stable execution invariant fix.

Validation result - default GPU chunk sync
------------------------------------------
Command log: `logs/training_real/h8_b16_budget4_assoc_salience_confread_defaultsync_nodebug_8chunks.log`.
Result: 8 chunks returned to stable range, loss=7.3785 over 16384 tokens, tps=138.3. This confirms the prior loss~14.9 was an execution-order/synchronization artifact, not Assoc memory quality.
Decision: default per-chunk GPU `Maintain::Wait` is validated as an execution invariant fix. The natural longer-term optimization is ring-buffering/reusing fewer mutable GPU buffers safely, but correctness comes first.

Change gate - deterministic LM sampled-softmax negatives
--------------------------------------------------------
1. Target failure mode: the 16-chunk synchronized corridor is not reproducible: one no-audit run stayed finite (`loss=7.2925`) while the same seed/profile with audit failed at step 11. `GpuLmHeadTrainer::build_sampled_indices` uses `rand::thread_rng()`, so `AIDEEN_TRAIN_SEED` does not fully determine the sampled-softmax loss/gradient path.
2. Structural rationale: sampled-softmax defines the LM objective over `targets + negatives`. Those negatives are part of the forward loss and backward `dl_dh` equation. For a frozen stabilization corridor, the sampled set must be a deterministic function of seed, optimizer step, target set, vocabulary, and sample capacity; otherwise gradients change between runs before Assoc/FPM can be compared.
3. Anti-patch check: this does not clamp loss, reduce sample count, disable audit, or tune dynamics. It restores the reproducibility invariant at the origin of the stochastic objective by replacing uncontrolled process RNG with a deterministic counter/hash sampler. The objective remains sampled softmax and remains valid across seeds/profiles because the seed explicitly selects the negative sequence.
4. Validation plan: cargo check; run the 16-chunk corridor twice with identical `AIDEEN_TRAIN_SEED`/`AIDEEN_LM_SAMPLE_SEED` and compare final loss/log signatures; then rerun 16 chunks with `AIDEEN_ASSOC_AUDIT=1`. Success means repeated no-audit runs match, audit no longer introduces unexplained divergence, and no NaN/DEQ-invalid appears. If audit still diverges with deterministic samples, classify sampling as default-stable invariant fix and investigate audit/readback perturbation next.

Validation result - deterministic sampled-softmax negatives
----------------------------------------------------------
Command: `cargo check --features wgpu -p aideen-training`.
Result: passed.

Command logs:
- `logs/training_real/h8_b16_budget4_assoc_salience_confread_detsample_nodebug_16chunks_r1.log`
- `logs/training_real/h8_b16_budget4_assoc_salience_confread_detsample_nodebug_16chunks_r2.log`
- `logs/training_real/h8_b16_budget4_assoc_salience_confread_detsample_audit_16chunks.log`

Results:
- no-audit r1: finite, loss=7.2964, tokens=32768, tps=137.3.
- no-audit r2: finite, loss=7.2415, tokens=32768, tps=137.7.

Investigation result - remaining nondeterminism source is before LM
-------------------------------------------------------------------
Command logs:
- `logs/training_real/repro_probe_detsample_2chunks_r1.log`
- `logs/training_real/repro_probe_detsample_2chunks_r2.log`

- Therefore the remaining non-bitwise behavior does not originate in sampled-softmax negative selection. It originates upstream in GPU DEQ/FPM/Assoc forward state or execution order.

Change gate - experimental token-serial DEQ forward corridor
-----------------------------------------------------------
1. Target failure mode: repeated runs with fixed LM sampled negatives still diverge before LM backward. The first observed mismatch is already in `hpooled`/`assoc_pooled` at step 1, while sampled indices and LM probability invariants match.
2. Structural rationale: `deq_slot_coord_unified_main` dispatches one workgroup per slot and loops over all tokens inside each workgroup. FPM cross-slot reads use `HistCtx[t-1, ms]` while other slot workgroups may still be writing `HistCtx[t-1, ms]`; WGSL provides no global barrier across workgroups inside one dispatch. The required invariant is token boundary ordering: all slots must finish token `t-1` writes before any slot reads cross-slot memory for token `t`.
3. Anti-patch check: this does not clamp values, lower LR, disable memory, or hide NaNs. It introduces an explicit experimental execution-order corridor that restores the missing global token boundary. It is not promoted as default because it can reduce TPS and slightly changes the current in-shader local token loop implementation; it exists to validate the race hypothesis causally.
4. Validation plan: add `AIDEEN_DEQ_TOKEN_SERIAL_FORWARD=1`; keep local Assoc/FPM state across token dispatches; adjust H carry so token-started dispatches do not reinitialize H when `global_t>0`. Run 2-chunk reproducibility probes twice. Success means `hpooled/assoc_pooled` probes align much more closely or bitwise, and stable loss remains finite. If it fails, classify the hypothesis as incomplete and inspect per-token writes/clears next.

Validation result - token-serial forward hypothesis incomplete
-------------------------------------------------------------
Command logs:
- `logs/training_real/repro_probe_tokenserial_ctx64_r1.log`
- `logs/training_real/repro_probe_tokenserial_ctx64_r2.log`
- `logs/training_real/repro_probe_tokenserial_nocarry_ctx64_r1.log`
- `logs/training_real/repro_probe_tokenserial_nocarry_ctx64_r2.log`

Result:
- Token-serial forward with global dispatch boundaries did not make `hpooled` reproducible.
- Disabling token carry also did not make `hpooled` reproducible.
- `assoc_pooled=0` in the 1-chunk ctx64 probe, so the mismatch exists before Assoc read contribution.

Classification:
- Experimental token-serial corridor: rejected as explanation for the first observed mismatch. Remove the code path rather than keeping a risky inactive branch, because the shader carry tweak can alter internal segmentation semantics.
- The cross-workgroup `HistCtx[t-1]` race remains a plausible design issue for long-memory semantics, but it is not the first reproducibility source in this probe.

New finding:
- `FixedPointMemoryReasoning::new_with_seed` still calls `default_slot_anchor`, and `default_slot_anchor` uses `thread_rng`. `slot_anchor` is uploaded into the forward DEQ path and can change `hpooled` before LM.

Change gate - seeded slot_anchor initialization
----------------------------------------------
1. Target failure mode: fixed `AIDEEN_TRAIN_SEED` does not reproduce the initial DEQ forward; `hpooled` differs before LM while sampled indices and LM weights match.
2. Structural rationale: `slot_anchor` participates in the DEQ slot geometry uploaded to GPU. In `new_with_seed`, all initialization must be driven by the provided `StdRng`; using `thread_rng` for `slot_anchor` violates the seed invariant and changes the forward map `f(h,s)` between process runs.
3. Anti-patch check: this does not clamp, tune, disable slots, or hide nondeterministic outputs. It removes uncontrolled randomness at the parameter initialization source and restores the invariant that a model seed determines the full initial forward path.
4. Validation plan: revert the failed token-serial experiment; route `slot_anchor` through the same seeded RNG used by `new_with_rng`; cargo check; rerun ctx64 1-chunk reproducibility probes twice without token-serial. Success means `hpooled`, LM probes, and final loss match or become substantially tighter under identical seed.

Validation result - seeded slot_anchor initialization
----------------------------------------------------
Command: `cargo check --features wgpu -p aideen-training`.
Result: passed.

Command logs:
- `logs/training_real/repro_probe_seeded_anchor_ctx64_r1.log`
- `logs/training_real/repro_probe_seeded_anchor_ctx64_r2.log`
- `logs/training_real/h8_b16_budget4_assoc_salience_confread_seeded_anchor_audit_16chunks.log`

Results:
- ctx64 r1: loss=6.2743, `hpooled.rms=2.846e-1`, `assoc_pooled.rms=1.605e-1`.
- ctx64 r2: loss=6.2899, `hpooled.rms=2.842e-1`, `assoc_pooled.rms=1.619e-1`.
- 16-chunk audit: finite, loss=7.3146, tokens=32768, tps=142.5, Assoc occupancy bounded at 4/16 for slots 4-7, no NaN/DEQ-invalid.

Classification:
- Seeded `slot_anchor` is default-stable: it removes uncontrolled `thread_rng` from `new_with_seed` and keeps the long audit corridor stable.
- Exact bitwise reproducibility is still pending. The remaining variation is much smaller in RMS-scale probes, so the next source is likely GPU non-bitwise execution/order or another less dominant state path.
- The rejected token-serial experiment was not kept as code; no default behavior was changed by that failed hypothesis.

Next action:
- Continue with remaining reproducibility only if it blocks causal comparisons. For model stabilization, the current priority can return to quality/capacity because the uncontrolled CPU RNG sources in the active training path have been removed.

Validation result - p8 capacity geometry
----------------------------------------
Command logs:
- `logs/assoc_capacity/capacity_p8_lambda2_b16_budget8_g0-128-256_train80_eval6.log`
- `logs/assoc_capacity/capacity_p8_lambda2_b32_budget8_g0-128-256_train80_eval6.log`
- `logs/assoc_capacity/capacity_p8_lambda2_b32_budget8_g0-128-256_train160_eval6.log`

Results:
- p8 lambda=2 banks16 budget8 train80: gap0=1.9197, gap128=1.7714, gap256=1.9570. Partial across gaps.
- p8 lambda=2 banks32 budget8 train80: gap0=1.3083, gap128=2.2514, gap256=1.2426. Capacity helps but exposure is still insufficient.
- p8 lambda=2 banks32 budget8 train160: gap0=0.0849, gap128=0.0971, gap256=0.5936. Memory works across all tested gaps.

Diagnosis:
- The stabilized model can learn associative recall beyond local context when three conditions hold:
  1. The Assoc read path has an output/loss path (`AIDEEN_ASSOC_LOGIT_LAMBDA > 0`).
  2. Effective write budget is at least on the order of pairs per sequence.
  3. Bank geometry has enough slack for salience/replacement (`32 banks` outperforms `16` for p8).
- The earlier random behavior was not proof that Assoc/FPM could not retain information. It was mostly missing/weak LM coupling plus insufficient capacity/exposure for the requested number of pairs.

Current provisional AR corridor:
- p4: `AIDEEN_ASSOC_LOGIT_LAMBDA=2`, banks=16, budget=4, train160 works through gap256.
- p8: `AIDEEN_ASSOC_LOGIT_LAMBDA=2`, banks=32, budget=8, train160 works through gap256.

Open architectural issue:
- Fixed global `AIDEEN_ASSOC_LOGIT_LAMBDA=2` should not become the broad LM default yet, because real-text training previously rejected hard Assoc logit coupling. The structural next step is a gated/trainable bridge so Assoc contributes when read confidence/content selectivity is high, rather than always injecting a fixed-scale vector.

Correction - prior banks32 runs were not true 32-bank runs
---------------------------------------------------------
Finding: Rust-side config clamps `AIDEEN_ASSOC_BANKS` to 16 in both `deq_bridge.rs` and `gpu_deq.rs`; the WGSL write-placement path also uses local arrays sized to 16. Therefore previous logs labelled `banks32` did not validate real 32-bank capacity.

Change gate - real >16 Assoc bank support
-----------------------------------------
1. Target failure mode: capacity experiments above 16 banks are invalid because the host clamps `ASSOC_BANKS` to 16 and the shader write-placement arrays cannot index more than 16 banks.
2. Structural rationale: bank count is a layout/invariant parameter. Host buffer sizing, shader override constants, local bank-score arrays, and scratch offsets must agree on the same maximum bank capacity. If any layer stays at 16, larger-bank tests either silently run as 16 banks or risk out-of-bounds local array access.
3. Anti-patch check: this does not tune memory behavior or hide quality loss. It restores the capacity/layout invariant so `AIDEEN_ASSOC_BANKS=32` means 32 actual banks across allocation, read, write, and replacement code.
4. Validation plan: raise host clamp and shader local capacity to 32 banks; cargo check; rerun p8 lambda=2 budget8 train80 for banks16 vs banks32. Success means both configurations compile and logs represent real bank counts; quality conclusions must be rewritten from the new measurements.

Additional backward invariant found while implementing:
- `fused_fpm_retain_bwd.wgsl` caches one full Assoc slot state in workgroup arrays sized 4096. With `d_model=512`, `ASSOC_BANKS=16` already needs `16 * (32 + 512 + 1) = 8720` floats, so the backward Assoc path can corrupt workgroup memory when bank count or dimension exceeds the cache capacity.
- Classification: layout/invariant. The immediate structural safety fix is to run the Assoc backward block only when `assoc_slot_stride <= 4096`; this preserves forward capacity validation and prevents silent OOB in backward. It is not the final scalable backward design.
- Next required architecture task: replace the full-slot workgroup cache/adjoint with storage-backed bank adjoints or tiled bank processing, so large-bank Assoc can train through the memory path instead of only being forward-valid.

Budget semantics correction
---------------------------
Finding: `AIDEEN_ASSOC_WRITE_BUDGET` is not the number of pair bindings in the sequence. In the forward shader it is a per-slot occupancy cap: empty-bank writes are allowed while `occupied_count < ASSOC_WRITE_BUDGET`; once the cap is reached, new writes either reuse a matched bank or use salience replacement. Therefore `ASSOC_BANKS=32` with `WRITE_BUDGET=8/16` does not use all physical banks.
Implication: earlier b32 runs with budget8/16 validate the 32-bank layout and routing specialization, but their effective per-slot storage cap is the budget value. To test real p16 capacity with 32 physical banks, run `WRITE_BUDGET=32`.

Result: train_avg=0.6905, gap0=0.7404, gap128=1.6795, gap256=0.1735; gap0/gap256 MEMORY WORKS, gap128 partial; no NaN reported.

Change gate - assoc_recall audit clamp correction
-------------------------------------------------
1. Target failure mode: `assoc_recall` diagnostic/audit paths still clamp displayed/readback bank count to 16, so logs can misreport or under-inspect true 32-bank runs.
2. Structural rationale: this is a measurement/layout consistency fix. The model forward path now supports 32 banks; audit readback must use the same cap to inspect the correct state stride.
3. Anti-patch check: this does not change training/inference equations, gates, or memory writes. It only prevents stale diagnostics from hiding banks 17..32.
4. Validation plan: change both audit clamps to 32; cargo check; note that prior attempted p24 run was actually p16 because `AR_N_KEYS` default capped `AR_PAIRS_PER_SEQ` at 16.

Change gate - scalable large-bank Assoc read backward
-----------------------------------------------------
1. Target failure mode: for `d_model=512` and `ASSOC_BANKS>=16`, `assoc_slot_stride` exceeds the 4096-float workgroup cache in `fused_fpm_retain_bwd.wgsl`, so the safety guard skips the whole Assoc backward block. Large-bank training can use forward Assoc and LM gradients, but `W_q_assoc`/`alpha_assoc` receive no read-path gradient.
2. Structural rationale: the read path does not require mutable full-slot BPTT state. `AssocHist` stores the pre-write bank state per token. A storage-backed read backward can recompute `q_t`, bank cosine scores, read probabilities, context, `alpha` gradient, and `dscore/dq` directly from `AssocHist`, then accumulate `W_q_assoc` gradients without copying all banks into workgroup memory.
3. Anti-patch check: this does not mask instability or tune losses. It restores an omitted gradient path at its actual source: read-query parameters participating in the active forward path. It deliberately does not fake write-side BPTT; write-side gradients remain a separate pending storage/tiled task.
4. Validation plan: add the large-bank read-only branch for `assoc_slot_stride > ASSOC_BWD_STATE_CAP`; cargo check; run a short p32/b32 probe with `AIDEEN_BACKWARD_INPUT_PROBE=1` or assoc debug to confirm nonzero Wq/alpha update telemetry and no NaN; rerun a capacity sanity to ensure no regression.

Validation note - large-bank read backward first probe
-----------------------------------------------------
Probe log: `logs/assoc_capacity/probe_large_bank_read_bwd_audit_p32_train4_eval1.log`.
Result: finite run, avg_loss=1.3548, gap128=0.2617, no NaN reported. Large-bank read branch produced nonzero `wq_step_sum` on Assoc slots, proving the skipped path now receives read-gradient telemetry.
Issue found: one slot reported an extreme raw `wq_step_sum` (~9.57e8). Cause: cosine-score derivative is ill-conditioned for occupied banks whose stored key norm is near zero. Forward can rank them with a clamped denominator, but backward should not propagate `dscore/dq` through a degenerate key vector.
Follow-up gate: skip score-gradient contribution when stored key norm or query norm is too small. This is a backward invariant fix for the cosine Jacobian, not a quality patch.

Validation - large-bank read backward stabilized
------------------------------------------------
Change: added storage-backed large-bank read backward for `assoc_slot_stride > ASSOC_BWD_STATE_CAP`. It trains `W_q_assoc`/`alpha_assoc` from the active read path without copying the whole bank slot into workgroup memory. Write-side BPTT remains pending.
Logs:
- `logs/assoc_capacity/probe_large_bank_read_bwd_audit_p32_train4_eval1.log`: finite but exposed unstable raw `wq_step_sum` (~9.57e8) from degenerate cosine keys.
- `logs/assoc_capacity/probe_large_bank_read_bwd_audit_p32_train4_eval1_stable_jac.log`: after skipping score-gradient for near-zero key/query norms, raw `wq_step_sum` stayed bounded (~30-52), no NaN.
- `logs/assoc_capacity/capacity_p32_k32v32_lambda2_true_b32_budget32_g0-128-256_train80_eval8_large_read_bwd.log`: train80 sanity passed gap0/gap128 but gap256 stayed random; classified as underexposed, not promoted alone.
- `logs/assoc_capacity/capacity_p32_k32v32_lambda2_true_b32_budget32_g0-128-256_train160_eval8_large_read_bwd.log`: train_avg=0.9651, gap0=0.1262, gap128=1.1067, gap256=0.7092; all gaps MEMORY WORKS; no NaN reported.
Classification: experimental useful / candidate default for large-bank read-gradient coverage. Remaining gap: storage/tiled write-side Assoc BPTT for `W_k_assoc`, event gate, and replacement policy gradients.

Change gate - scalable large-bank Assoc key-write backward
----------------------------------------------------------
1. Target failure mode: after large-bank read backward, future reads can train `W_q_assoc` but do not push gradient back into the key that was written by `W_k_assoc`. Thus large-bank training still lacks the write-key learning path.
2. Structural rationale: only the bank key has learnable write parameters in the current default Assoc path; bank value is raw token identity. A key-only adjoint needs `ASSOC_BANKS * ASSOC_RANK` floats, which fits the existing workgroup scratch for 32 banks (1024 floats), unlike full `[key|value|usage]` adjoints. Read backward accumulates `dL/d bank_key`; reverse write propagation maps the chosen-bank key adjoint through `bank_key <- keep * prev + write_mass * k_t` into `W_k_assoc`.
3. Anti-patch check: this restores the actual missing gradient for the active write-key equation. It does not approximate value BPTT or hide instability; it leaves value/event/replacement gradients marked pending where they are not yet structurally covered.
4. Validation plan: add key-only adjoint in the large branch; cargo check; audit probe must show bounded nonzero `wk_step_sum`; capacity sanity must remain finite and below random.

Validation - scalable large-bank Assoc key-write backward
---------------------------------------------------------
Change: storage-backed large-bank read backward now accumulates `dL/d bank_key` and propagates the chosen-bank key adjoint through `bank_key <- keep * prev + write_mass * k_t` into `W_k_assoc`. The same edit also restored write-mass parity for backward: `ENABLE_ASSOC_LINEAR_WRITE=true` uses linear mass and derivative 1; squared mass uses derivative `2 * effective_bind_gate`; writes below `ASSOC_WRITE_MIN_MASS` contribute zero derivative; overwrite uses zero keep gradient.
Files inspected/changed: `aideen-backbone/src/shaders/fused_fpm_retain_bwd.wgsl`; forward parity checked against `aideen-block/src/shaders/deq_slot_attn_unified_clean.wgsl` write equation and `AssocHist` metadata layout.
Validation:
- `cargo check --features wgpu -p aideen-training`: pass.
- `logs/assoc_capacity/probe_large_bank_key_write_bwd_audit_p32_train4_eval1_final.log`: finite; no NaN; `wk_step_sum` nonzero on active Assoc slots, e.g. s4=2.994e0, s5=3.276e1, s7=3.851e-1; gap128=0.1404 vs random=4.4067.
- `logs/assoc_capacity/capacity_p32_k32v32_lambda2_true_b32_budget32_g0-128-256_train160_eval8_large_key_write_bwd.log`: finite; train_avg=1.1093; gap0=1.1346, gap128=0.6694, gap256=0.6211, all MEMORY WORKS vs random=4.4067.
Classification: default stable for the p32/b32 large-bank corridor. Remaining pending: value-source gradient, event/librarian gradients, replacement-policy gradients, and exact forward-source parity for key projection if `PrevHStarBuf` is exposed to this backward pass instead of the current `S_in` approximation.
Next action: run one real-document/LM corridor with large banks and watch whether `W_k_assoc`/`W_q_assoc` deltas remain nonzero without degrading TPS or LM loss; then decide whether event/librarian backward is needed before real training.
Small-branch sanity after write-mass derivative parity:
- `logs/assoc_capacity/sanity_b1_linear_write_bwd_train16_eval4.log`: finite; no NaN; b1/p4 tiny corridor remains below random with partial results (gap0=2.4146, gap32=2.5098 vs random=3.5264). This is not a capacity promotion, only a regression/finite sanity for the low-bank branch.

Real-text sanity - large-bank key-write backward
------------------------------------------------
Command: `AIDEEN_BATCH_SIZE=4 AIDEEN_MAX_CHUNKS=10 AIDEEN_CTX_LEN=256 AIDEEN_H_SLOTS=8 AIDEEN_ASSOC_BANKS=32 AIDEEN_ASSOC_WRITE_BUDGET=32 AIDEEN_ASSOC_SLOT_OWNER=1 AIDEEN_ASSOC_HASH_LANE=1 AIDEEN_ASSOC_HASH_REPLICA=1 AIDEEN_ASSOC_EVENT_GATE=1 AIDEEN_ASSOC_SALIENCE_REPLACE=1 AIDEEN_ASSOC_CONF_READ=1 cargo run --release --features wgpu -p aideen-training --bin train -- --file aideen-bench/tinyshakespeare.txt --epochs 1 --log-every 1 --save-every 0`.

Result: finite; no NaN/INVALID in log; loss=6.7561, tps_epoch=155.5, tokens=10240. Classification: diagnostic sanity only, not quality promotion. It shows the large-bank key-write backward coexists with real-text training without immediate TPS collapse or numerical failure.
Open issue observed: FPM debug still reports dead token counts and zero retain/write telemetry on slots 4..7; this appears to be slot-role/gating behavior or existing instrumentation, not yet attributed to the new key-write backward. Next real-training stabilization should compare against the pre-key-write or b1 corridor and inspect whether Assoc slots are intentionally excluded from FPM write telemetry.

Change gate - Assoc-to-FPM bridge telemetry
-------------------------------------------
1. Target failure mode: real-text training shows base FPM write counters as zero on Assoc slots, but that does not tell whether the Assoc-to-FPM contextual bridge is inactive, weak, or merely unobserved. Without this measurement we cannot decide what is necessary for serious training.
2. Structural rationale: the active forward bridge computes `consolidate = ASSOC_TO_FPM_SCALE * clamp(assoc_write_gate_token, 0, ASSOC_WRITE_CAP) * effective_write_mass` and updates `fpm_m_cache <- (1-consolidate) * fpm_m_cache + consolidate * h_trace`. Logging write mass, consolidate, trace RMS, and delta RMS observes the exact causal path from explicit Assoc binding to contextual FPM state.
3. Anti-patch check: this is measurement only. It does not change model dynamics, gates, gradients, loss, or optimizer behavior. It prevents a false architecture conclusion from missing telemetry.
4. Validation plan: add temporary DebugLog slots for Assoc bridge metrics; decode and print `[ASSOC-BRIDGE]`; cargo check; run short tinyshakespeare b32 corridor and require finite log with nonzero/zero bridge metrics interpretable per slot and no NaN/INVALID.

Measurement correction - Assoc bridge debug collision
----------------------------------------------------
Finding: first bridge telemetry log showed `cons_max=2.43e2` on one slot, impossible because `consolidate <= ASSOC_TO_FPM_SCALE * ASSOC_WRITE_CAP`. Cause: bridge debug indices `992..1015` collided with existing debug markers around index 1000 from other GPU paths. This invalidates that one `cons_max` field but not the training run itself.
Correction plan: increase the DEQ debug buffer from 1024 to 2048 floats, move Assoc bridge telemetry to `1024 + bridge_slot * 6`, and update trainer decoding. Also fix train-side assoc-state bank clamp from 16 to 32 so state summaries match the active `AIDEEN_ASSOC_BANKS=32` corridor.
Classification: measurement/layout fix. No model equation, gradient, or optimizer behavior changes.

Validation - Assoc-to-FPM bridge telemetry
------------------------------------------
Changes:
- Enlarged DEQ debug buffer from 1024 to 2048 floats and moved bridge metrics to `1024 + assoc_bridge_slot * 10` to avoid collisions with existing debug markers around index 1000.
- Fixed train-side `AIDEEN_ASSOC_BANKS` summary clamp from 16 to 32.
- Added `[ASSOC-BRIDGE]` metrics: total-average mass/consolidate/trace/delta, max consolidate, total count, active count, and active-average mass/consolidate/delta.
- Made `AIDEEN_ASSOC_AUDIT=1` refresh the debug snapshot when the cached one is invalid, so Assoc diagnostics do not depend on `AIDEEN_DEBUG_SAMPLE=1`.

This suggests the next serious-training question is not "is the bridge wired?" but "is sparse contextual consolidation strong/useful enough over longer real documents?"

Change gate - configurable Assoc-to-FPM scale
---------------------------------------------
1. Target failure mode: bridge telemetry shows Assoc-to-FPM consolidation is wired but sparse/low average on real text. To evaluate serious-training behavior, we need controlled scale sweeps without code edits or recompilation.
2. Structural rationale: `ASSOC_TO_FPM_SCALE` is the explicit multiplier in the forward bridge equation. Making it a WGSL override plumbed from `AIDEEN_ASSOC_TO_FPM_SCALE` changes only this documented coupling strength and preserves the default value `0.02`.
3. Anti-patch check: this does not silently tune the default or hide a bug. It exposes an existing architectural coupling as an experimental axis while keeping the validated default unchanged.
4. Validation plan: add shader override and Rust pipeline constant; cargo check; run a short audit with default scale to confirm finite bridge telemetry; optional next runs compare `0.0`, `0.02`, and a higher value under the same real-text corridor.

Inspection - Direct Assoc-to-LM logit coupling
----------------------------------------------
Finding: `AIDEEN_ASSOC_LOGIT_LAMBDA` is wired in the real GPU LM training path, not only in the `assoc_recall` binary. Default is `0.0`, so the serious-training baseline does not use direct Assoc logits unless explicitly enabled.
Circuit: `gpu.bridge.assoc_pooled_buf` is copied into LM `dl_dh_temp_buf` before `lm_probs_main`; when lambda is positive, logits add `lambda * emb_ref[v,d] * assoc_read[t,d]`. During LM backprop, the shader writes `dlassoc = sum_k (p_k - y_k) * lambda * emb_ref[v,d]` into `s_h_rms`, which Rust exposes as `assoc_grad_buf()` and passes to DEQ adjoint as the Assoc RHS.
Validation:
- `logs/real_text/sweep_assoc_logit_0p02_seed42_chunks10.log`: finite; no NaN/INVALID; loss=6.7994; tps_epoch=131.7; config isolated `AIDEEN_ASSOC_TO_FPM_SCALE=0.0`, `AIDEEN_ASSOC_LOGIT_LAMBDA=0.02`.
- Comparable baseline with both bridges off: `logs/real_text/sweep_assoc_to_fpm_0p00_seed42_chunks10.log`, loss=6.7839, tps_epoch=156.4.
Interpretation: direct Assoc-to-LM is structurally present and gradient-coupled, but this short real-text corridor does not justify enabling it for serious training. Keep default `0.0`; classify as experimental pending stronger evidence that Assoc reads are predictive under LM objective.

Change gate - held-out validation file for serious training
----------------------------------------------------------
1. Target failure mode: current training evidence only has train loss and in-stream eval windows. This cannot distinguish genuine learning/generalization from stream-local loss decrease, so serious-training readiness is under-measured.
2. Structural rationale: add a validation-only execution path that reuses the existing GPU `train_sequence` forward path with `eval_mode=true`, which sets LM lr to zero and returns before DEQ/embedding/LM updates. This measures the same model circuit without changing weights.
3. Anti-patch check: this is measurement, not dynamics. It does not tune gates, scales, memory, optimizer, or training equations. It restores the experimental invariant that every serious baseline must have a separated evaluation metric before architecture promotion.
4. Validation plan: add `--val-file <path>` CLI support plus a bounded `Trainer::eval_tokens_gpu` helper; cargo check; run a short train with `--val-file aideen-bench/tinyshakespeare.txt` as a smoke and require finite `[HELDOUT] val_loss`, no NaN/INVALID, and no behavior change when `--val-file` is omitted.

Current stability assessment - end-to-end serious-prep corridor
---------------------------------------------------------------
Question answered: whether the model currently runs end-to-end without skipping the required training circuit, and what stability level is supported by evidence.

End-to-end status for the current promoted corridor:
- Promoted corridor: batch=4, ctx=256, h_slots=8, assoc_banks=32, assoc_write_budget=32, slot owner, hash lane+replica, event gate, salience replacement, confidence read, `AIDEEN_ASSOC_TO_FPM_SCALE=0.0`, `AIDEEN_ASSOC_LOGIT_LAMBDA=0.0`.
- The main GPU training path runs end-to-end: token ids -> embeddings -> DEQ/slot solve -> FPM slots + Assoc slots -> hpooled/assoc_pooled -> sampled LM head -> loss -> LM backward -> DEQ adjoint -> GPU parameter/state updates -> optional held-out eval.
- No training freeze flags are part of the promoted corridor (`--freeze-deq`, `--freeze-emb`, `--freeze-lm` are not used).
- `--val-file` evaluation is forward-only by design; it skips updates intentionally because it is validation, not training.

Evidence level:
- `logs/real_text/serious_prep_b32_no_bridges_seed42_chunks40.log`: finite, no NaN/INVALID, loss=6.5218, 132.5 TPS, 40960 tokens.
- `logs/real_text/serious_prep_b32_no_bridges_seed7_chunks40.log`: finite, no NaN/INVALID, loss=6.4912, 132.2 TPS, 40960 tokens.
- `logs/real_text/serious_prep_b32_no_bridges_seed42_val10_chunks40.log`: finite, no NaN/INVALID, in-stream eval improves 6.7764 -> 6.6075 -> 6.5065.
- `logs/real_text/pretrain_minimal_heldout_tiny_smoke_chunks20.log`: finite, no NaN/INVALID, train loss=6.7353, held-out val_loss=6.7181, 135.7 TPS, train tokens=20480, held-out tokens=2048.
- `cargo check --features wgpu -p aideen-training`: pass after held-out validation support.

Stability classification:
- Numerical stability: medium-high for short serious-prep runs. Evidence covers two seeds at 40 chunks on tinyshakespeare and one 20-chunk pretrain-corpus smoke with held-out eval. No NaN/Inf/DEQ-INVALID appeared in these logs.
- Training-loop stability: medium-high for the promoted corridor. Loss decreases across longer smoke and eval windows, and held-out evaluation executes after training without corrupting the run.
- Quality/generalization stability: early/medium-low. The model learns in the smoke corridor, but this is not yet a long training proof, not a multi-document held-out benchmark, and not a generation-quality guarantee.
- Memory-utility stability: medium for occupancy and finite operation, pending for proven usefulness. Assoc banks occupy and read/write paths run, but bridge usefulness and long-horizon memory benefit over the baseline are not yet proven by held-out metrics.

Important exclusions / not yet promoted:
- Direct Assoc-to-LM logits are wired but default-off. First short test with `AIDEEN_ASSOC_LOGIT_LAMBDA=0.02` was finite but did not beat the no-bridge baseline.
- Assoc-to-FPM bridge is wired and observable, but default serious-prep runs set `AIDEEN_ASSOC_TO_FPM_SCALE=0.0` because scale sweeps did not support promoting it.
- Large-bank Assoc backward currently covers scalable key-write adjoint; full value adjoint, event/librarian/replacement-policy gradients, and exact previous-hstar key-source parity remain open.
- CPU fallback paths are not the promoted training path. The evidence here is GPU/Metal path only.

Operational conclusion:
The current model is stable enough to start longer serious-prep training runs under the documented profile, with bridges off and held-out evaluation enabled. It is not yet stable enough to claim full architecture convergence or final memory-quality success. The next correct validation is duration scaling: increase `AIDEEN_MAX_CHUNKS`, then held-out token count, across at least two seeds, before reintroducing experimental bridges or more dynamics.

Structural inspection - remaining large-bank Assoc backward gaps
----------------------------------------------------------------
Files inspected:
- `aideen-backbone/src/shaders/fused_fpm_retain_bwd.wgsl`
- `aideen-block/src/shaders/deq_slot_attn_unified_clean.wgsl`

Finding:
- The promoted 32-bank corridor uses the large-bank Assoc backward branch because `ASSOC_BANKS * (ASSOC_RANK + d_model + 1)` exceeds the 4096-float workgroup cache cap.
- Large-bank backward currently accumulates compact key adjoints in `assoc_gb[bank * RETAIN_RANK + r]` and propagates selected key-write gradients into `W_k_assoc` / `W_q_assoc`.
- It does not store full value adjoints per bank because that would require `ASSOC_BANKS * d_model` storage, which is exactly the layout that no longer fits in workgroup memory.
- The small-bank branch also computes `g_value_dim` from normalized value write but does not clearly propagate it into a durable upstream source in the inspected section. This means the next fix must be designed as a forward/backward invariant update, not copied blindly from the small-bank branch.
- `AIDEEN_ASSOC_TRANSITION_GATE` defaults to false in the current serious-prep corridor, so `W_v_assoc` is reserved/inactive for the promoted baseline. Therefore, the immediate missing default-path piece is not `W_v_assoc` training; it is value-source adjoint/utility for the explicit value stored in Assoc banks.

Classification:
- Current baseline remains valid as duration-stable training evidence.
- Remaining Assoc backward is `experimental pending`, not default-stable complete. It does not block training stability, but it limits how fully Assoc memory can learn from LM loss.

Next change gate candidate - large-bank Assoc value adjoint design
------------------------------------------------------------------
1. Target failure mode: large-bank Assoc write backward trains address/key paths but does not close the value-write adjoint to the value source. The model can store/read values in forward, but the learning signal for what value representation should be stored is incomplete.
2. Structural rationale: forward value write stores a normalized current value vector into the selected bank with `value_new = keep * value_prev + write_mass * value_current_norm`. Backward must propagate `dL/dvalue_new` through `write_mass`, overwrite keep semantics, and the normalization of `value_current_norm`. Because full per-bank value adjoints do not fit in workgroup memory at 32 banks, the large-bank branch needs either a compact selected-bank value adjoint computed directly from the read-gradient equation, or a tiled/storage-backed value adjoint buffer.
3. Anti-patch check: do not add a scalar gain or bridge to compensate for missing value learning. The correct locus is the value-write adjoint equation and storage strategy, because the missing mechanism originates at the forward write equation.
4. Validation plan: implement behind the large-bank branch only; `cargo check`; run short 32-bank assoc-recall and real-text smoke; require no NaN/INVALID, no TPS collapse, and improved/nonzero value-adjoint diagnostics before promoting. Then re-run the 80/200 chunk serious-prep profile.

Change gate - compact selected-bank value adjoint for large-bank Assoc
---------------------------------------------------------------------
1. Target failure mode: large-bank Assoc backward does not propagate value-read gradients into the selected bank value write. Forward writes `bank_value <- keep * old + write_mass * value_norm`, but backward only keeps compact key adjoints, so value learning from LM loss is incomplete in the 32-bank corridor.
2. Structural rationale: read backward can compute `dL/dbank_value_b` directly from the read equation without storing all bank value adjoints: for each bank and dimension, `g_value_b_dim = alpha_assoc * assoc_read_conf * p_b * g_ctx_dim`. Accumulate only the chosen forward-write bank's value adjoint into a per-dim scratch vector, then apply the existing value-write adjoint through `write_mass`, overwrite keep, and normalization of `value_norm`.
3. Anti-patch check: this restores the missing adjoint of the exact forward value write equation. It does not add a bridge, gain, guard, or loss mask, and remains valid across bank counts because it avoids workgroup storage proportional to all bank values.
4. Validation plan: implement only in the `assoc_slot_stride > ASSOC_BWD_STATE_CAP` branch; add debug counters for selected-bank value adjoint magnitude; `cargo check`; run short real-text smoke with `AIDEEN_DEBUG_SAMPLE=1`; require no NaN/INVALID and nonzero value-adjoint telemetry before longer validation.

Implementation - compact selected-bank value adjoint for large-bank Assoc
-------------------------------------------------------------------------
Change:
- Added a compact selected-bank value adjoint in `fused_fpm_retain_bwd.wgsl` for the `assoc_slot_stride > ASSOC_BWD_STATE_CAP` path.
- The large-bank read backward now computes `dL/dbank_value` directly from the read equation for the forward-selected bank only: `alpha_assoc * assoc_read_conf * p_bank * g_ctx`.
- The selected value adjoint contributes to the write-mass/event-gate gradient through `value_norm - previous_bank_value`, matching the forward write equation `bank_value <- keep * old + write_mass * value_norm`.
- Added `[ASSOC-BWD-STEP] value_adj_sum` telemetry using existing debug slot `+4`.
Validation:
- `cargo check --features wgpu -p aideen-training`: pass.
- `logs/real_text/assoc_large_value_adj_smoke_debug_chunks2.log`: finite; no NaN/INVALID; `value_adj_sum` nonzero on Assoc slots s4-s7.
- `logs/real_text/pretrain_value_adj_smoke_seed42_chunks20.log`: finite; no NaN/INVALID; train loss=6.7172; held-out val_loss=6.7238; tps_epoch=134.4; train tokens=20480.
- `logs/real_text/pretrain_value_adj_baseline_seed42_chunks80.log`: finite; no NaN/INVALID; train loss=6.2889; held-out val_loss=6.3675; tps_epoch=131.6; train tokens=81920.
- `logs/real_text/pretrain_value_adj_baseline_seed7_chunks80.log`: finite; no NaN/INVALID; train loss=6.2731; held-out val_loss=6.3571; tps_epoch=133.5; train tokens=81920.
Interpretation:
- Numerical stability is preserved through 80 chunks on two seeds.
- The missing value-adjoint path is now active and observable.
- Quality effect is mixed at 80 chunks: seed42 held-out improved slightly versus previous 80-chunk baseline (`6.3758 -> 6.3675`), while seed7 regressed versus previous seed7 80-chunk baseline (`6.3091 -> 6.3571`). This is not a reason to reject the structural adjoint, but it is not yet a quality promotion. Next validation is 200 chunks on at least seed42 before treating this as the new serious baseline.
Classification: structural pending/default-candidate. It restores a missing adjoint in the active large-bank path and remains finite, but needs 200-chunk validation before default-stable classification.

Composite change result - large-bank value adjoint gated after 200-chunk regression
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Failure observed:
- `logs/real_text/pretrain_value_adj_baseline_seed42_chunks200.log`: train loss=22.9376; held-out val_loss=22.9476; final diagnostics contained NaN entropy/move and saturated `a_delta_max=1.0e12`.
- This refutes promoting the value-write adjoint as default dynamics in its current form, despite short 20/80 chunk stability.

Piece classification:
- Measurement: `[ASSOC-BWD-STEP] value_adj_sum` is useful and remains default-stable as telemetry.
- Layout/invariant: no new large `ASSOC_BANKS * d_model` buffer was introduced; compact selected-bank computation remains structurally useful.
- Dynamics: using selected value adjoint to train the event/write gate is experimental useful but rejected as default because it destabilized at 200 chunks.
- Diagnostics: logs above are retained as evidence; removal criterion for telemetry is after a stable normalized value-adjoint design replaces this one.

Action:
- Added `ENABLE_ASSOC_VALUE_WRITE_BWD` / `AIDEEN_ASSOC_VALUE_WRITE_BWD`, default `false`.
- Default serious-prep corridor again has the validated no-bridge/no-value-adjoint dynamics.
Validation:
- `cargo check --features wgpu -p aideen-training`: pass.
- `logs/real_text/value_adj_gated_default_smoke_chunks2.log`: default flag-off smoke finite; no NaN/INVALID; loss=6.9269; tokens=2048.
Next action:
- Do not continue tuning this by gain alone. The failure likely means the selected value adjoint needs normalization/clipping through the same optimizer-scale discipline as address/event parameters, or must target a safer value-representation parameter rather than event/write mass directly.

Change gate - temporal storage-backed large-bank value adjoint
-------------------------------------------------------------
1. Target failure mode: the first large-bank value-adjoint path used the current token read gradient as if it trained the current token write. A write at token t only changes bank state visible to future reads, so the same-token selected-bank shortcut violated the Assoc state timeline and produced a 200-chunk regression with NaN diagnostics/loss ~22.94.
2. Structural rationale: maintain a per-slot/per-bank/per-dim value-state adjoint buffer during the reverse token scan. At token t, the write equation consumes the adjoint already accumulated from future reads (`dL/dM_post_t`), propagates it through `value_keep_gate` into `dL/dM_pre_t`, and only then adds the current read contribution (`dL/dread_t -> dL/dM_pre_t`). This restores the temporal invariant: read_t observes pre-write state; write_t affects future state.
3. Anti-patch check: this does not tune a gain, clip the symptom, or disable the failing term. It changes the gradient owner/lifetime to match the forward state equation, so the write gate receives only gradients from future consequences of the write.
4. Validation plan: add the buffer behind `AIDEEN_ASSOC_VALUE_WRITE_BWD=1`; `cargo check`; run 2-chunk debug and 20-chunk held-out smoke with the flag enabled. Success requires no NaN/INVALID, nonzero `value_adj_sum`, and no default-path behavior change when the flag is off.

Implementation - temporal storage-backed large-bank value adjoint
-----------------------------------------------------------------
Change:
- Added `AssocValueGrad` as a per-slot/per-bank/per-dim storage buffer for the large-bank Assoc backward branch.
- Kept the path behind `AIDEEN_ASSOC_VALUE_WRITE_BWD=1`; default behavior remains flag-off.
- Corrected the value-write adjoint timeline: write_t consumes only future accumulated value-state adjoint, propagates it through overwrite/keep semantics, then current read_t adds its value gradient to the pre-write state.
Validation:
- `cargo check --features wgpu -p aideen-training`: pass.
- `logs/real_text/assoc_value_state_adj_smoke_debug_chunks2.log`: finite; no NaN/INVALID; nonzero `value_adj_sum` on Assoc slots s4-s7.
- `logs/real_text/pretrain_value_state_adj_seed42_chunks20.log`: finite; no NaN/INVALID; train loss=6.7226; held-out val_loss=6.7218; tps_epoch=141.0; train tokens=20480.
- `logs/real_text/pretrain_value_state_adj_seed42_chunks80.log`: finite; no NaN/INVALID; train loss=6.2902; held-out val_loss=6.3678; tps_epoch=136.2; train tokens=81920.
- `logs/real_text/pretrain_value_state_adj_seed42_chunks200.log`: finite; no NaN/INVALID; train loss=5.7024; held-out val_loss=5.9449; tps_epoch=132.2; train tokens=204800.
- `logs/real_text/value_state_adj_default_off_smoke_chunks2.log`: default flag-off finite; no NaN/INVALID; loss=6.9217; tps_epoch=142.0.
Interpretation:
- The previous same-token value-adjoint failure is corrected for the seed42 200-chunk corridor that previously regressed to loss ~22.94/NaN diagnostics.
- Quality is neutral/slightly mixed versus the no-value-adjoint 200-chunk seed42 baseline (`5.7281` train, `5.9472` held-out): train improves, held-out is effectively equal (`5.9472 -> 5.9449`).
Classification: experimental useful / default-candidate, not promoted default until repeated on seed7 and/or longer serious-prep runs. The code remains opt-in behind `AIDEEN_ASSOC_VALUE_WRITE_BWD=1`.
Next action: repeat 200 chunks with seed7 before considering promotion; if stable, evaluate whether value-source parameter learning or event-gate scaling is the next missing Assoc backward piece.

Inspection - W_v_assoc / value-source role after temporal value adjoint
-----------------------------------------------------------------------
Files inspected:
- `aideen-block/src/shaders/deq_slot_attn_unified_clean.wgsl`
- `aideen-backbone/src/shaders/fused_fpm_retain_bwd.wgsl`
- `aideen-backbone/src/gpu_deq.rs`
Finding:
- In the current promoted corridor, stored `bank_value` is normalized `S_in[t]` literal source, not `W_v_assoc(S_in[t])`.
- `W_v_assoc` is reserved for `ENABLE_ASSOC_TRANSITION_GATE`: it builds a rank-space auxiliary vector used to modulate `transition_gate`, not the value written into the bank.
- Therefore the temporal value adjoint currently trains write/event dynamics, not a value projector. This is consistent with the explicit-memory philosophy, but means value representation learning through Assoc is not yet closed to upstream source/embedding/DEQ state.
Decision:
- Do not enable/promote `AIDEEN_ASSOC_TRANSITION_GATE` as the next step without isolated validation; it changes forward allocation/write mass and is not required for the stable literal-value Assoc path.
Next action:
- The next structural gap is source-adjoint ownership for literal values: decide whether value-write gradients should flow back into `S_in`/embedding/DEQ state, or remain stop-grad so Assoc stays an explicit memory over the current representation.

Change gate - experimental embedding source adjoint from clean Picard
---------------------------------------------------------------------
1. Target failure mode: embedding updates currently consume `gpu_lm.dl_dh_buf`, the LM-head gradient at pooled output, while the DEQ Picard adjoint computes a slot-major `v_state` after the reasoning core. This can train embeddings against a gradient that bypasses the DEQ/Assoc/FPM circuit.
2. Structural rationale: compute `dL/dS_in[token,dim]` from the final clean Picard slot adjoint by mirroring the same RMSNorm Jacobian used in `picard_clean_step_main` for the direct slot-branch/source term, then reduce across slots into the token-major buffer consumed by `embedding_train.wgsl`.
3. Anti-patch check: do not feed raw summed `v_state` to embeddings. The reducer must apply the clean Picard normalization derivative and slot pooling/source path, restoring the missing gradient ownership at the source-input boundary rather than tuning embedding LR or masking the symptom.
4. Validation plan: keep behind `AIDEEN_EMB_USE_DEQ_ADJOINT=1`; `cargo check`; run 2-chunk probe to verify finite source gradient and no NaN/INVALID; then 20-chunk held-out smoke before any promotion.

Change gate - promote embedding DEQ-source adjoint as default training path
---------------------------------------------------------------------------
1. Target failure mode: serious training default still updates embeddings from LM pooled-output gradient only, bypassing the DEQ/Assoc/FPM reasoning circuit even though the DEQ source adjoint is validated.

3. Anti-patch check: this promotes the corrected gradient path at the source-input boundary; it does not tune LR, add clipping, or hide instability. The value adjoint remains disabled because its combination was causally rejected.
4. Validation plan: `cargo check`; GPU default-on smoke without setting `AIDEEN_EMB_USE_DEQ_ADJOINT`; require no NaN/INVALID and metrics consistent with prior flag-on corridor. Also allow opt-out with `AIDEEN_EMB_USE_DEQ_ADJOINT=0` for ablation.

Validation - default serious-training corridor after embedding-adjoint demotion, 200 chunks seed42
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

This run also beats the earlier no-flag seed42 baseline (`5.9472 -> 5.8978`) and the rejected promoted-default run (`5.9535 -> 5.8978`). Because the run uses the default-off corridor, the improvement should be treated as validation of the current clean baseline, not as evidence for the demoted adjoint.

Change gate - skip embedding update on invalid fixed point
----------------------------------------------------------
1. Target failure mode: seed7 default training reports `DEQ-INVALID` by step 11 and later collapses to NaN/FPM-dead state by 80 chunks. Current code disables LM LR and skips DEQ weight update on `invalid_fixed_point`, but still updates embeddings from `dl_dh` produced by the invalid forward state.
2. Structural rationale: if the DEQ solve did not produce a valid fixed point, gradients that depend on that state are not reliable. The same invariant used to skip implicit DEQ gradients must apply to token embeddings, because their update consumes the LM gradient through the invalid DEQ output path.
3. Anti-patch check: this is not NaN masking or clipping. It prevents an invalid solver state from becoming a parameter update at the exact boundary where corruption enters persistent weights. Valid fixed-point steps continue to train normally; invalid steps are treated as no-update recovery windows.
4. Validation plan: `cargo check`; seed7 20 chunks should remain finite and not corrupt embeddings after the step-11 invalid event; seed7 80 chunks should no longer collapse to NaN/FPM-dead state. Compare against seed42 smoke to ensure no broad regression.

Change gate - slot owner prepass as single token-level coordinator
------------------------------------------------------------------
1. Target failure mode: slot memory paths still decide read/write/retain locally. Previous `AIDEEN_SLOT_OWNER_COORD` sketch was invalid because it recomputed owner scores inside each slot workgroup and had no global synchronization guarantee.
2. Structural rationale: add a separate GPU prepass before the DEQ slot pass. One workgroup per `(batch, token)` computes the owner distribution once from shared slot anchors and token source, writes current-token and previous-source owner vectors into the token's `Scratch` region, and the DEQ/Assoc paths consume those values as upstream coordination gates. Command-buffer pass ordering provides the global barrier missing inside the slot dispatch.
3. Anti-patch check: this does not suppress NaNs, clamp loss, or tune around seed7. It restores the missing invariant: allocation/read/write gates for all slots are conditioned on the same token-level owner distribution computed before local slot decisions. The path remains opt-in via `AIDEEN_SLOT_OWNER_PREPASS=1` until validated.
4. Validation plan: add Rust/WGSL plumbing behind `AIDEEN_SLOT_OWNER_PREPASS`; `cargo check --features wgpu -p aideen-training`; run only current canonical smokes after confirming command shape. Success requires no default behavior change when the flag is omitted, finite opt-in smoke, owner diagnostics nonzero/nonuniform, and no stale invalid-command logs cited as evidence.

Implementation - opt-in slot owner prepass
------------------------------------------
Change:
- Added `aideen-block/src/shaders/slot_owner_prepass.wgsl`.
- Added `AIDEEN_SLOT_OWNER_PREPASS=1`, `AIDEEN_SLOT_OWNER_BETA`, and `AIDEEN_SLOT_OWNER_MIN_GATE` plumbing in `aideen-block/src/deq_bridge.rs`.
- The prepass runs before `deq_slot_coord_unified_main` and writes two owner vectors into each token's existing `Scratch` slack region:
  - current-token owner over all slots for FPM read/write/retain coordination.
  - previous-source owner over Assoc slots for Assoc read/write coordination.
- The main DEQ shader consumes these owner probabilities as residual gates. With the flag omitted, gates are exactly neutral (`1.0`) and the prepass is not dispatched.
Validation:
- `cargo check --features wgpu -p aideen-training`: pass.
- `logs/real_text/slot_owner_prepass_compile_smoke.log`: opt-in GPU/Metal compile smoke, 1 chunk, finite.
- `logs/real_text/default_after_slot_owner_prepass_compile_smoke.log`: default flag-off GPU/Metal compile smoke, 1 chunk, finite.
Classification: experimental useful / pending. The coordinator is now structurally placed correctly, but it is not promoted and has not yet passed seed-stability or quality validation.
Next action: confirm the exact current stabilization command/corridor before running longer owner-prepass validation.

Change gate - make slot owner prepass the single owner authority
----------------------------------------------------------------
1. Target failure mode: slot behavior remains inconsistent because three owner mechanisms can stack on the same token: `slot_coord_weights`, Assoc hash/anchor owner, and the new owner prepass. This means a slot can be selected, attenuated, and diagnosed by different distributions in the same forward pass.
2. Structural rationale: when `AIDEEN_SLOT_OWNER_PREPASS=1`, treat prepass owner gates as the only slot ownership authority for FPM/Assoc gating. Existing hash/anchor owner logic remains fallback only when the prepass is disabled. This restores the invariant that read/write ownership is decided once, before local memory paths execute.
3. Anti-patch check: this does not tune thresholds or hide NaNs. It removes contradictory decision sources at the slot-allocation layer where the failure originates. The old behavior remains available with the prepass off for ablation/default parity.
4. Validation plan: update WGSL branching; `cargo check`; run default-off and opt-in compile smokes. Success requires default-off unchanged/finite, opt-in finite, and no path where prepass owner is multiplied by an independent hash/anchor owner decision.

Implementation - single owner authority under prepass

Validation - owner prepass criterion does not separate enough
-------------------------------------------------------------
Command: `AIDEEN_SLOT_OWNER_PREPASS=1 AIDEEN_DEBUG_SAMPLE=1 AIDEEN_DEBUG_FPM=1 AIDEEN_MAX_CHUNKS=4 AIDEEN_CTX_LEN=512 ...`.

- `prev=[0,0,0,0,0.260,0.220,0.263,0.257]`
