Correction - owner staging must not write past Scratch stride
-------------------------------------------------------------
Finding: the first owner prepass implementation wrote owner vectors after the alpha matrix (`alpha + h*h`), but the current scratch stride ends exactly there. That was an out-of-bounds write and produced garbage owner values in later probes.
Fix: owner prepass now stages `owner_current` and `owner_prev` in the first two rows of the existing alpha matrix. The main DEQ shader reads those values before `compute_slot_coord` overwrites alpha, so no buffer-size or backward-stride change is required.
Classification: layout/invariant fix for the experimental prepass path.

Change gate - add content-hash component to owner criterion
-----------------------------------------------------------
1. Target failure mode: anchor-only owner scoring produces nearly uniform ownership, so slots receive no strong differentiated responsibility.
2. Structural rationale: use one global prepass to compute `score(slot, token) = anchor_cos(slot, token) + hash_mix * content_hash_projection(slot, token)`. The hash projection is deterministic from token content and slot id, so different data is assigned to different slots even before anchors specialize. Learned anchors remain in the equation and can later reshape the routing.
3. Anti-patch check: this is not a loss clamp or seed-specific bias. It fixes the assignment criterion at the router origin: a router with indistinguishable anchors cannot separate data, so it needs a content-dependent tie-breaker/partitioner. The change remains opt-in under `AIDEEN_SLOT_OWNER_PREPASS=1`.
4. Validation plan: add WGSL/Rust constants; rerun owner probe. Success requires finite run and visibly nonuniform owner distributions without reintroducing per-slot local ownership.

Implementation - role-split owner criterion
--------------------------------------------
Changes:
- Owner prepass now uses `anchor_cos + SLOT_OWNER_HASH_MIX * content_hash_projection`.
- Default opt-in owner constants changed to `SLOT_OWNER_BETA=16`, `SLOT_OWNER_HASH_MIX=8`.
- Current-token owner competition is restricted to FPM slots (`0..h/2`).
- Previous-source owner competition is restricted to Assoc slots (`h/2..h`).
- Main shader masks owner values by role and gates using the role count, not total `h_slots`.
- Added `[SLOT-OWNER]` trainer diagnostics: `curr`, `prev`, `prev_gate`.
Corrections found while validating:
- Fixed invalid owner staging that wrote past the scratch stride.
- Fixed out-of-role softmax writes that leaked uninitialized negative values.
Validation:
- `cargo check --features wgpu -p aideen-training`: pass.
- `logs/real_text/slot_owner_prepass_role_gate_probe_chunks4.log`: finite 4-chunk owner probe.
- Latest owner telemetry:
  - `curr=[0.206,0.226,0.223,0.168,0.000,0.000,0.000,0.000]`
  - `prev=[0.000,0.000,0.000,0.000,0.218,0.141,0.143,0.148]`
  - `prev_gate=[0.100,0.100,0.100,0.100,0.556,0.597,0.611,0.632]`
Interpretation: slot roles are now structurally separated and no longer assign current/FPM ownership to Assoc slots or previous/Assoc ownership to FPM slots. The distribution is nonuniform enough to break the previous all-slot uniform behavior, but it is only a 4-chunk probe, not stability proof.
Classification: experimental useful / pending longer validation.
Next action: run the current canonical short stability corridor with `AIDEEN_SLOT_OWNER_PREPASS=1`, then compare seed7 invalid/NaN behavior against default-off.

Change gate - enable Assoc address updates by default
-----------------------------------------------------
1. Target failure mode: with `AIDEEN_ASSOC_LOGIT_LAMBDA=0.1`, Assoc RHS is nonzero and multi-bank read/write produces nonzero `score_grad`, `wq_step`, `wk_step`, `key_grad`, and `gprev`, but `wq_update_max`/`wk_update_max` remain zero.
2. Structural rationale: `trainer.rs` defaults `cfg_assoc_addr_lr_mult` to `0.0` when neither `AIDEEN_ASSOC_ADDR_LR_MULT` nor `AIDEEN_ASSOC_LR_MULT` is set. The fused FPM/Assoc backward applies `W_q_assoc/W_k_assoc` updates as `AllGradients * assoc_addr_lr_scaled`, so a zero multiplier freezes the address matrices even when gradients are valid. Defaulting to `1.0` restores the intended invariant: active trainable Assoc address weights update unless explicitly frozen by env.
3. Anti-patch check: this does not mask loss, clamp instability, or invent a compensating gradient. It removes an accidental training-path freeze at the exact update multiplier that nulls otherwise valid gradients. Users can still explicitly freeze with `AIDEEN_ASSOC_ADDR_LR_MULT=0`.
4. Validation plan: patch the default; run `cargo check`; rerun the 1-chunk multi-bank probe with `AIDEEN_ASSOC_BANKS=4 AIDEEN_ASSOC_LOGIT_LAMBDA=0.1 AIDEEN_SLOT_OWNER_PREPASS=1`. Success requires nonzero `wq_update_max` or `wk_update_max`, finite loss, and no NaN/Inf.

Implementation/validation - Assoc address LR default
----------------------------------------------------
Change:
- `aideen-training-lab/src/trainer.rs`: `cfg_assoc_addr_lr_mult` fallback changed from `0.0` to `1.0`.
Circuit trace result:
- `LM assoc_rhs`: requires `AIDEEN_ASSOC_LOGIT_LAMBDA > 0`; otherwise Assoc is intentionally absent from LM logits and RHS is zero.
- `rhs_slot_buf`: receives the Assoc RHS in `run_staged_adjoint_picard_no_readback`.

## 2026-05-12 - Change Gate: Model A DEQ blend must match FPM solve contract
- Target failure mode: owner/Assoc corridor is finite but DEQ remains in `mode=EMERG` with `contr > 1` across seeds. A/B on seed 11 chunks=5 showed `AIDEEN_HIST_MIN_ITERS=32` only changed `iters ~16 -> ~23` and small `exit_err` deltas; it did not restore normal convergence, so the failure is not primarily iteration budget.
- Structural rationale: the FPM health/homeostatic contract is parameterized by `FPM_ALPHA_H=0.2` (`homeo_band = 0.15 * alpha_h`), but the active Model A path uses `shape.damping` (observed 0.60 in EMERG) for `H_curr <- blend*f(H)+ (1-blend)*H_curr`. That makes the actual fixed-point update 3x more aggressive than the equation used by the convergence policy. For the normalized self-feedback map, this violates the contraction margin and produces `contr > 1` even when extra iterations are allowed.
- Anti-patch check: this does not mask NaNs or loosen thresholds. It restores the invariant that the FPM Model A solver update coefficient and the FPM convergence/health contract refer to the same alpha. If correct, it should reduce contractivity in the same corridor without depending on a seed-specific guard or suppressing diagnostics.
- Validation plan: run `cargo check --features wgpu -p aideen-training`, then repeat the seed 11 chunks=5 A/B corridor with owner prepass, 4 assoc banks, assoc lambda 0.1. Success: no NaN/INVALID, `mode` should move toward NORMAL or `contr`/hit/exit_err should materially decrease at the same iteration budget. If loss/TPS degrades heavily or `EMERG` remains unchanged, classify as rejected/pending and continue isolating attention/self-feedback scale.

Change gate - scale Assoc read injection under FPM residual budget
------------------------------------------------------------------
1. Target failure mode: enabling Assoc read with otherwise stable Model A alpha blend returns the solve to `EMERG` and `contr > 1`, especially in Assoc slots.
2. Structural rationale: FPM memory read is scaled as a residual branch by `read_residual_scale = shape.fpm_alpha_m` and normalized to signal energy before entering `fpm_ctx`. Assoc read currently normalizes only by its own RMS floor and adds directly to `fpm_ctx`, bypassing the FPM residual budget and also bypassing the H-operator RMS denominator in Model A. This makes Assoc a hidden unbudgeted context branch and can expand the Picard map.
3. Anti-patch check: do not disable Assoc read and do not relax convergence thresholds. Keep Assoc read active, but route its H-solve injection through the same residual-budget invariant as FPM memory. AssocReadBuf export remains raw for LM coupling, so this does not hide Assoc from the output objective.
4. Validation plan: patch Assoc H injection scale; run `cargo check`; rerun seed 11 chunks=5 with `AIDEEN_ASSOC_READ=1`. Success: no NaN/INVALID, `mode=NORMAL` or contractivity close to the read-off ablation, while Assoc backward updates remain nonzero.

Implementation/validation - Assoc H injection residual budget
-------------------------------------------------------------
Change:
- `deq_slot_attn_unified_clean.wgsl`: Assoc read still exports raw `assoc_ctx` to `AssocReadBuf` for LM coupling, but its injection into the H solve is now scaled by `signal_norm * read_residual_scale / assoc_norm`, matching the FPM memory residual budget.
- Together with the previous Model A alpha blend fix, FPM/Assoc memory branches now share the same conservative H-solve coupling contract.
Validation:
- `cargo check --features wgpu -p aideen-training`: pass.
- `logs/real_text/assoc_read_scaled_fpm_alpha_seed11_chunks5.log`: finite, `loss=6.1912`, `tps_epoch=92.9`.
- All sampled steps `mode=NORMAL`, `conv=OK`.
- `contr=1.028..1.050`, matching the Assoc-read-off ablation instead of the previous `EMERG` spikes.
- Assoc backward remains live: step 1 Assoc slots show nonzero `wq_update_max` and `wk_update_max`; later chunks keep nonzero `wq_update_max` while `wk_update_max=0` when `write_mass=0`, as expected.
Classification: default-stable candidate for the experimental owner/Assoc corridor; requires multi-seed 20-chunk validation before promotion.
Next action: repeat 20-chunk multi-seed corridor with Assoc read active.

Change gate - ignore contractivity ratios inside accepted homeostatic band
-------------------------------------------------------------------------
1. Target failure mode: after Assoc H injection scaling, 3/4 long seeds stay `NORMAL`, but seed 7 still enters `EMERG` even though the offending per-slot residuals are already inside/near the accepted homeostatic band (`exit_err` around `2.8e-2`, `hit=0`, early exit). The emergency is caused by a high ratio between small residuals, not by an unconverged or invalid solve.
2. Structural rationale: `max_contractivity` is intended to detect expansion of the active Picard residual. The current shader records `d_curr/d_prev` whenever `d_prev > epsilon*10`, even if `d_curr` and/or `d_prev` are below the homeostatic convergence band. Ratios between accepted-band residuals are not a valid divergence invariant; they should not drive emergency renorm/damping. The correct invariant is to evaluate contractivity only while both residuals are outside the accepted convergence band.
3. Anti-patch check: this does not loosen convergence acceptance and does not hide failed solves. `failed_hits`, `exit_err_h`, `max_delta_seen`, NaN/Inf checks, and status classification still observe unconverged/invalid tokens. It only prevents a measurement/control false positive where already-accepted residual jitter triggers emergency.
4. Validation plan: patch the contractivity accumulation floor to `max(homeo_band, epsilon*10)` for both previous and current residuals; run `cargo check`; rerun seed 7 chunks=20. Success: no NaN/INVALID, `mode=NORMAL` at sampled steps, `conv=OK`, loss/TPS not worse, Assoc updates remain live.

Implementation/validation - contractivity measurement floor
-----------------------------------------------------------
Change:
- `deq_slot_attn_unified_clean.wgsl`: `max_contractivity` now records `d_curr/d_prev` only when both residuals are above `max(homeo_band, epsilon*10)`. Accepted-band residual jitter no longer drives emergency mode.
Validation:
- `cargo check --features wgpu -p aideen-training`: pass.
- `logs/real_text/contractivity_band_floor_seed7_chunks20.log`: finite, `loss=5.9844`, `tps_epoch=101.8`, `tokens=10240`.
- Seed 7 sampled steps now all `mode=NORMAL`, `conv=OK`; `contr=1.043..1.058`.
- Assoc backward remains live with nonzero `wq_update_max` in Assoc slots.
Multi-seed status for the current 20-chunk corridor:
- seed 7: `NORMAL=4`, `EMERG=0`, no visible NaN/INVALID/panic/error, `loss=5.9844`.
- seed 11: `NORMAL=4`, `EMERG=0`, no visible NaN/INVALID/panic/error, `loss=5.9625`.
- seed 13: `NORMAL=4`, `EMERG=0`, no visible NaN/INVALID/panic/error, `loss=5.9742`.
- seed 42: `NORMAL=4`, `EMERG=0`, no visible NaN/INVALID/panic/error, `loss=5.9995`.
Classification: measurement/control fix promoted for the experimental owner/Assoc corridor. Next required validation before serious training: longer chunks (80+) and then a non-debug throughput run.

2026-05-12 - Change gate: decouple GPU step fence from TPS benchmarking
-----------------------------------------------------------------------
1. Target failure mode: seed 11 with owner/Assoc corridor passes when debug/readback or `AIDEEN_TPS_SYNC_EVERY=1` forces a per-step GPU wait, but fails with NaN diagnostics when `AIDEEN_TPS_SYNC_EVERY=0` and debug is sparse. This makes a benchmarking flag change model correctness.
2. Structural rationale: the training step mutates/reuses persistent GPU buffers across forward, LM backward, DEQ adjoint, weight updates, embedding updates, debug buffers, and next chunk input. The invariant is that a step boundary must not let the CPU enqueue the next chunk against reusable state before the previous step's GPU work has completed. The existing implementation accidentally ties that lifecycle fence to `AIDEEN_TPS_SYNC_EVERY`, whose name invites disabling it for throughput measurement.
3. Anti-patch check: this does not clamp NaNs, disable Assoc/FPM, relax convergence checks, or alter model equations. It restores an execution-order invariant at the GPU step boundary and separates it from human-facing TPS benchmarking. The old unsafe behavior remains available only by explicitly disabling the new lifecycle fence.
4. Validation plan: add `AIDEEN_GPU_STEP_FENCE_EVERY` with default 1 and use it for step-boundary polling. Run `cargo check --features wgpu -p aideen-training`, then rerun seed 11 chunks=20 with `AIDEEN_TPS_SYNC_EVERY=0` and no explicit fence override. Success: finite, `mode=NORMAL`, no NaN diagnostics. Then test explicit `AIDEEN_GPU_STEP_FENCE_EVERY=0` remains a known unsafe diagnostic path, not a promoted training path.

Implementation/validation - GPU step fence separated from TPS sync
------------------------------------------------------------------
Change:
- `aideen-training-lab/src/trainer.rs`: introduced `AIDEEN_GPU_STEP_FENCE_EVERY` with default `1` and moved the step-boundary `device.poll(Maintain::Wait)` checks from the legacy `AIDEEN_TPS_SYNC_EVERY` control to this lifecycle control.
- Removed `cfg_tps_sync_every` from the trainer hot config so TPS benchmarking no longer silently owns training correctness.
Validation:
- `cargo check --features wgpu -p aideen-training`: pass, no warnings.
- `logs/real_text/seed11_debug20_tpssync1_chunks20.log`: pre-change falsifier; `AIDEEN_TPS_SYNC_EVERY=1` made seed 11 chunks=20 pass, proving the failure was sync/lifecycle-sensitive.
- `logs/real_text/seed11_debug20_gpu_step_fence_default_chunks20.log`: post-change with `AIDEEN_TPS_SYNC_EVERY=0` and default `AIDEEN_GPU_STEP_FENCE_EVERY=1`; finite, `loss=5.9645`, `tps_epoch=106.0`, `tokens=10240`, sampled `mode=NORMAL`, `conv=OK`, `contr=1.026`, no NaN diagnostics.
Interpretation:
- The previous seed 11 NaN at sparse debug was not evidence against the Assoc/FPM equations. It was an execution-order invariant leak: disabling a TPS sync also disabled the effective GPU step fence.
Classification: default stable for serious-training safety. `AIDEEN_GPU_STEP_FENCE_EVERY=0` is now an explicit unsafe/throughput diagnostic mode until the GPU pipeline is redesigned to avoid same-buffer cross-step hazards without blocking.
Next action: rerun the 80-chunk multi-seed corridor with the default GPU step fence, then decide whether to promote the current owner/Assoc/FPM setup as the serious-training baseline.

2026-05-12 - Change gate: align emergency control with FPM Model A solve status
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------
1. Target failure mode: seed 7 80-chunk validation stays finite and reaches `loss=5.3614`, but sampled step 80 enters `mode=EMERG` solely because one slot records `contractivity=1587` / `max_err_h=74.72`, while the same slot's `exit_err_h=0.0477`, `conv=OK`, activations are finite, and the FPM Model A classifier returns `HealthyConverged`.
2. Structural rationale: Model A FPM solve health is defined by exit residual (`exit_err_h <= 0.15`) because transient Picard overshoot can recover within the token solve. `classify_fpm_solve` already encodes this invariant, but the later emergency controller still treats raw `contractivity > 1.20` as an unconditional emergency even when FPM status is healthy. The control invariant must use the same solve-status semantics as classification: for FPM Model A, emergency should trigger from `NumericInvalid`/unconverged status, not from recovered transient overshoot.
3. Anti-patch check: this does not hide NaNs or failed solves. Numeric invalid status, NaN checks, growth streaks, and non-FPM contractivity alarms remain active. It only prevents a recovered transient from changing damping/iters/renorm after the solve has met the accepted exit invariant.
4. Validation plan: patch controller to gate contractivity warning/alarm through FPM solve status. Run `cargo check --features wgpu -p aideen-training`; rerun seed 7 chunks=80. ## 2026-05-12 - FPM telemetry split and seed validation

### Finding: retain/m_inner zeros on slots 4..7
- Log inspected: `logs/real_text/seed7_gpu_step_fence_default_chunks80.log`.
- Observed line: `[FPM-PATH] retain_max/retain_avg` and `[FPM-WRITE] m_inner` are nonzero for slots 0..3 and zero for slots 4..7.
- Cause: this telemetry belongs to the base FPM plastic-write block. The shader only enters that block when `fpm_write_enabled && !is_segment_memory_slot && !is_assoc_slot && d_model == WG_SIZE * 2u`; with the current 8-slot split, slots 4..7 are Assoc slots and intentionally skip the base FPM write path.
- Interpretation: zeros in those fields are expected and do not imply dead Assoc slots. Assoc slots must be evaluated through `[ASSOC-BWD-STEP]`, Assoc read diagnostics, and `[ASSOC-BRIDGE]` when bridge telemetry is active.
- Evidence from the same seed7 log: slots 4..7 show nonzero `val_rms`, `value_adj_sum`, `score_grad_max`, `wq_step_max`, `wq_update_max`, and occasional `wk_step_max/write_mass`, confirming Assoc-side activity.
- Classification: measurement interpretation, default stable.

2026-05-13 - Change gate: checkpoint/inference parity for text generation
-------------------------------------------------------------------------
1. Target failure mode: stable training runs lower loss and keep DEQ/FPM/Assoc finite, but text inference from `model_large.aidn` still produces incoherent deterministic output. Existing checkpoints were saved before the current stable corridor, and the checkpoint path can also lose GPU per-slot specialization because `sync_inference_weights()` returns early in slot-coordinate mode to avoid averaging per-slot matrices into shared CPU prototypes.
2. Structural rationale: the active training source-of-truth for DEQ slot-coordinate mode is `GpuDeqBackend::all_weights_buf`, which contains per-slot `W_q/W_k/W_v/W_o/W_in`, FPM history params, and Assoc params. The CPU `FixedPointMemoryReasoning` object cannot exactly represent all learned per-slot matrices. A checkpoint used for generation must serialize the GPU buffer layout and reload/upload that exact layout before inference, otherwise generation evaluates a different model than the one trained.
3. Anti-patch check: this does not tune sampling or hide poor text quality. It restores the train->save->load->infer invariant by preserving the actual learned tensors at their owner/source-of-truth. If generation is still poor after parity is restored, that becomes evidence about training/data/objective, not about checkpoint loss.
4. Validation plan: implement exact GPU checkpoint tensors as additional `.aidn` weights with backward-compatible fallback. Run `cargo check --features wgpu -p aideen-training`. Train a short checkpoint with the current corridor and `save-every=1`, then run `infer` from that checkpoint and verify logs show finite generation path; compare output quality only after parity is confirmed.

Implementation/result - exact GPU checkpoint tensors
----------------------------------------------------
Files changed:
- `aideen-training-lab/src/trainer.rs`
- `aideen-training-lab/src/bin/infer.rs`

Change:
- New checkpoints can store exact GPU DEQ/FPM/Assoc tensors under `reasoning.gpu_exact.*`.
- `Trainer::load_full` detects those tensors and keeps them as the first-upload source for GPU inference.
- `generate`/`generate_stream` upload the exact GPU checkpoint tensors before the first forward when available, instead of reconstructing slot-coordinate weights from the incomplete CPU representation.
- `infer --stats` now reports `gpu_exact: yes/no`.

Validation:
- `cargo check --features wgpu -p aideen-training` passed.
- Short checkpoint probe:
  - Train log: `logs/real_text/text_parity_probe_train.log`.
  - Command used `AIDEEN_CHECKPOINT_BASE=logs/real_text/text_parity_probe`, current corridor flags, `AIDEEN_MAX_CHUNKS=20`, `--save-every 1`.
  - Result: completed 20 chunks, `loss=5.9739`, checkpoint saved, no NaN/INVALID/FAIL in sampled output.
- Reload/infer probe:
  - Log: `logs/real_text/text_parity_probe_infer_stats.log`.
  - Result: `gpu_exact: yes`, inference completed finite.

Interpretation:
- The train->save->load->infer tensor parity gap is closed for new checkpoints.
- The generated text from a 20-chunk probe is still incoherent; that is not a new contradiction. It means the parity issue is no longer a blocker, and the next question is whether a real text-training run with enough updates/data starts improving generation quality.
Classification: default-stable structural fix for checkpoint/inference parity. Existing old checkpoints without `reasoning.gpu_exact.*` remain backward-compatible but should not be used as evidence for the current serious-training corridor.

2026-05-13 - Change gate: full-vocab text learning diagnostic
--------------------------------------------------------------
1. Target failure mode: real-text runs can report stable sampled LM loss, while deterministic generation remains incoherent. The current training LM objective normalizes over target tokens plus sampled negatives (`num_samples=512` by default), but generation ranks against the full tokenizer vocabulary (`50257` tokens). Existing `eval_tokens_gpu` follows the sampled training circuit, so it cannot prove that the correct next token is globally ranked well at generation time.
2. Structural rationale: text generation quality depends on the full-vocab logit ordering after the exact GPU DEQ inference path. A diagnostic must run the same checkpoint/inference H* path as `generate`, then compute full softmax CE and target rank over the complete LM head. This measures the actual invariant needed by generation: `logit[target]` should become competitive against all vocabulary rows, not only against the sampled subset seen by the training shader.
3. Anti-patch check: this does not change training, sampling, gates, slots, or losses. It only adds measurement at the evaluation boundary where the symptom appears. If the metric is poor while sampled loss improves, the root cause is objective/calibration/ranking or insufficient training. If it improves, incoherent text is more likely due to decoding/data scale.
4. Validation plan: add an opt-in `infer --eval-file --eval-max-positions` path. Run `cargo check --features wgpu -p aideen-training`. Evaluate the short parity checkpoint and confirm the report includes finite full-vocab CE, top1/top5, mean rank, and `gpu_exact: yes` when exact tensors are active.

Implementation/result - full-vocab diagnostic
---------------------------------------------

- `aideen-training-lab/src/trainer.rs`
- `aideen-training-lab/src/bin/infer.rs`

- Added `Trainer::eval_full_vocab_gpu`, a teacher-forced diagnostic that uses the same GPU inference path as generation, then computes full-vocab CE, top1/top5, mean rank, and logit margins.

Interpretation:
- The metric now separates sampled training loss from actual generation-time ranking.

2026-05-13 - Change gate: LM/embedding checkpoint parity under slot-coordinate mode
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------
1. Target failure mode: micro text overfit lowered sampled loss from `6.2390` to `5.9815`, but the saved `best_loss` checkpoint still showed near-initial `embeddings`/`lm_w` stats and full-vocab CE near random. The final checkpoint then contained NaN embeddings after the later collapse. This means checkpoint evaluation was still not faithfully measuring the trained text model.
2. Structural rationale: `save_full` calls `sync_inference_weights()` before serializing LM-head and tokenizer embeddings. In slot-coordinate mode that function returned immediately to avoid lossy DEQ per-slot averaging. That early return also skipped LM-head and embedding GPU->CPU sync, even though LM/embedding CPU tensors are the serialized source for checkpoint/inference. The correct invariant is: skip only lossy DEQ CPU projection, but always sync LM-head and embeddings from their GPU owners before checkpointing.
3. Anti-patch check: this does not tune the text objective or hide the collapse. It restores ownership parity at checkpoint boundaries: DEQ per-slot tensors stay exact via `reasoning.gpu_exact.*`, while LM-head and embeddings are serialized from their actual GPU-trained values. If full-vocab ranking remains poor after this, it is real training/objective evidence.
4. Validation plan: modify `sync_inference_weights()` so slot-coordinate mode bypasses only DEQ CPU averaging, not LM/embedding sync. Run `cargo check --features wgpu -p aideen-training`. Rerun a short micro text overfit and verify the saved checkpoint `--stats` shows changed finite LM/embedding tensors and `gpu_exact: yes`; then rerun full-vocab eval.

Implementation/result - slot-coordinate sync split
--------------------------------------------------
Files changed:
- `aideen-training-lab/src/trainer.rs`

Change:
- `sync_inference_weights()` now skips only the lossy DEQ CPU projection when slot-coordinate mode is active.
- LM-head and embedding GPU->CPU sync still run before checkpoint serialization.

Validation:
- `cargo check --features wgpu -p aideen-training` passed.
- Short micro sync probe completed 12 epochs and saved finite checkpoints.
- Full-vocab eval of that checkpoint still stayed random-scale, so checkpoint sync was necessary but not sufficient for text learning.

2026-05-13 - Change gate: sampled LM objective full-vocab estimator
--------------------------------------------------------------------
1. Target failure mode: the LM training loss can improve on the sampled objective while full-vocab CE/rank remains random at inference. Baseline sampled loss is `log(num_samples) ~= log(512) = 6.238`, while generation baseline is `log(vocab_size) ~= log(50257) = 10.824`; the current metric and objective therefore underrepresent the denominator seen by generation.
2. Structural rationale: for uniform sampled negatives, a full-vocab denominator can be estimated by weighting each sampled negative by `(vocab_size - 1) / (num_samples - 1)` while keeping the target unweighted. This restores the full-vocab softmax invariant at the LM boundary: the target probability is measured against an unbiased estimate of all non-target rows, not only the sampled subset.
3. Anti-patch check: this is not a sampling/decoding tweak and it does not hide poor generation. It changes only the LM objective estimator, behind an explicit experimental flag, so we can compare sampled-subset training vs full-vocab-estimated training under the same model path. If it fails, we reject the objective estimator without touching the stable default corridor.
4. Validation plan: add `AIDEEN_LM_FULL_VOCAB_ESTIMATE=1` as opt-in. Run `cargo check --features wgpu -p aideen-training`. Run a short micro text probe with the flag and compare sampled/full-vocab eval logs against the current sync probe.

Implementation/result - full-vocab estimator flag
--------------------------------------------------
Files changed:
- `aideen-backbone/src/gpu_lm_head.rs`
- `aideen-backbone/src/shaders/lm_train.wgsl`

Change:
- Added opt-in env flag `AIDEEN_LM_FULL_VOCAB_ESTIMATE=1`.
- When active, LM sampled softmax weights non-target sampled probabilities by `(vocab_size - 1) / (num_samples - 1)` while leaving the target unweighted.
- This makes reported CE estimate the full-vocab denominator instead of the sampled-subset denominator.

Validation:
- `cargo check --features wgpu -p aideen-training` passed.
- Short micro run: `logs/real_text/micro_text_fullvocab_est_probe_train.log`.
- Loss scale moved as expected from sampled random baseline `~6.238` to full-vocab random baseline `~10.824`.
- The 3-epoch run stayed finite and saved `gpu_exact: yes` checkpoint; full-vocab eval remained near random, which is expected for such a short run and does not validate text learning yet.

Current interpretation:
- Stability path and checkpoint parity are improved.
- We now have the correct diagnostic and an opt-in objective estimator, but coherent text is not proven.
- The next real test is a longer controlled micro-overfit with the full-vocab estimator and a collapse detector around epoch 30+, or an LM-only/DEQ-frozen ablation to determine whether the remaining failure is LM objective coverage, DEQ representation, or embedding update instability.

2026-05-13 - Change gate: fused-train vs autoregressive full-vocab parity metric
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------
1. Target failure mode: with `AIDEEN_LM_FULL_VOCAB_ESTIMATE=1` and even `--freeze-deq`, training loss improves while `infer --eval-file` full-vocab CE remains near random. That suggests a path mismatch, but current metrics do not separate "the fused training path learns" from "the autoregressive inference path uses a different state/query contract".
2. Structural rationale: add a full-vocab CE/rank diagnostic that reads `h_pooled` directly from the fused GPU training/eval path after `train_sequence(..., eval_mode=true)`. This keeps the forward path identical to training while swapping only the final LM metric to full-vocab. Comparing this against the existing autoregressive full-vocab metric isolates whether the mismatch originates before or after the path split.
3. Anti-patch check: this is pure measurement. It does not change optimization, sampling, or model dynamics. It only reveals whether the learned signal exists in the fused path and is lost in the autoregressive path.
4. Validation plan: add an opt-in infer flag for fused-train-path full-vocab evaluation, run `cargo check --features wgpu -p aideen-training`, then evaluate the same micro checkpoints with both metrics and compare CE/rank.

2026-05-13 - Change gate: expose LM sample count and exact char-level micro path
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------
1. Target failure mode: we need to test two distinct hypotheses with evidence:
   - whether stronger sampled coverage (`num_samples` >> 512) improves exact ranking on the current BPE corridor;
   - whether exact full-vocab training becomes meaningful on the micro corpus when the vocabulary is genuinely small.
   Today neither is directly configurable from the training entrypoint.
2. Structural rationale: the LM trainer already honors `config.num_samples`, but `train` hardcodes the architecture default. Also, the exact/full-vocab path only becomes truly exact if `num_samples >= vocab_size`; that is unrealistic for BPE-50k on the current GPU shader, but entirely feasible for a char-level micro corpus. Exposing `AIDEEN_NUM_SAMPLES` and `AIDEEN_FORCE_CHAR_TOKENIZER` restores the intended control surfaces without altering default behavior.
3. Anti-patch check: these flags do not mask symptoms or retune the model implicitly. They only let us run the two evaluations the current architecture already suggests. Defaults remain unchanged; the new behavior is opt-in and diagnostic/experimental.
4. Validation plan: wire both env flags in `train`, run `cargo check --features wgpu -p aideen-training`, then run:
   - BPE micro probes with `AIDEEN_NUM_SAMPLES=2048`;
   - char-level micro probe with `AIDEEN_NUM_SAMPLES >= vocab_size` and `AIDEEN_FORCE_CHAR_TOKENIZER=1`.

Implementation/result - sample count and char-level exact path
--------------------------------------------------------------

Experiment A: BPE + `num_samples=2048` + `DEQ frozen`

- Result:

Experiment B: char-level exact full vocab + `DEQ frozen`

Interpretation:
- Exact full-vocab training on a truly small vocabulary does produce a measurable, if still small, ranking gain over random.
- Therefore the model is not fundamentally incapable of moving exact next-token ranking; the larger BPE corridor remains bottlenecked by objective scale/coverage and stability, not by the mere existence of exact training.

2026-05-13 - Parallel follow-up: exact small-vocab vs stronger BPE objective
----------------------------------------------------------------------------

  - `AIDEEN_NUM_SAMPLES=512` with `vocab_size=52` (exact full softmax)
  - `--freeze-deq`

  - exact eval: `logs/real_text/micro_text_char_exact_long_v3_best_loss_eval.log`

    - top5 `0.2109`

  - with exact objective and small vocab, the model continues to turn training progress into exact-ranking gains.

Experiment D: BPE `num_samples=2048`, LM-only
- Train log: `logs/real_text/micro_text_bpe_2048_lm_only_probe_train.log`
- Setup:
  - `AIDEEN_NUM_SAMPLES=2048`
  - `AIDEEN_LM_FULL_VOCAB_ESTIMATE=1`
  - `--freeze-deq --freeze-emb`
- Result:
  - remained finite
  - best train loss improved strongly to `9.7229`
  - exact eval (short window): `logs/real_text/micro_text_bpe_2048_lm_only_probe_best_loss_eval64.log`

    - train-path CE `10.8248`
    - top1 `0`
    - top5 at most `0.0312`
- Interpretation:
  - freezing embeddings removes the NaN instability seen in the earlier `2048` BPE run, confirming embeddings as the main instability source for that branch.
  - however, even with a much better training loss, exact full-vocab ranking on BPE barely moves. So the objective approximation/scaling problem is still the dominant blocker on the real-vocab corridor.

Current conclusion after both lines
-----------------------------------
- The model can learn exact next-token ranking when:
  - the vocabulary is small enough for exact softmax, and
  - the optimization path remains stable.
- On the real BPE corridor:
  - DEQ training adds instability,
  - embedding updates add another instability source under stronger negative coverage,
  - and even LM-only stronger sampled training does not yet translate into exact full-vocab ranking gains.

Practical implication:
- The next structural work should focus on the BPE objective/interface itself, not on proving again that the model can learn in principle.
- The cleanest next target is a better real-vocab objective for BPE plus a safer embedding-update regime, since those are now the two places with direct evidence.

2026-05-13 - Change gate: embedding row-frequency invariance under BPE 2048
----------------------------------------------------------------------------
1. Target failure mode: on the real BPE corridor with `AIDEEN_NUM_SAMPLES=2048` and embeddings trainable, training collapses early and `Embedding Moments Checksum` becomes `NaN`, while the same corridor remains finite when embeddings are frozen. The instability therefore originates in the embedding update path, not only in DEQ or LM-head.
2. Structural rationale: `lm_backprop_h_t_main` already scales `dl_dh[t]` by `1 / active_targets`, so the per-position hidden gradient is sequence-normalized. `embedding_adamw_update` then regroups those per-position gradients by token row using a raw sum across all occurrences of the token in the chunk. That makes an embedding row update proportional to local repetition count, so the effective row step is not invariant to how many times a token happened to appear in the window. Averaging by occurrence count restores the intended invariant: each embedding row follows the mean gradient of its active positions in the current chunk rather than a frequency-amplified sum.
3. Anti-patch check: this is not a cosmetic clamp or emergency guard. It corrects the update equation at the row owner itself, where the mismatch is introduced during token-position regrouping. The fix does not depend on a special seed or threshold; it removes a duplicated scaling factor that should not be there if row updates are meant to reflect sequence-normalized token evidence.
4. Validation plan:
  - `cargo check --features wgpu -p aideen-training` must pass.
  - Re-run the BPE `2048` probe with embeddings trainable and `--freeze-deq`, reusing the existing log corridor under `logs/real_text/`.
  - Success threshold 1: no `NaN` in embedding moments over the prior failure window.
  - Success threshold 2: train loss remains finite and improves versus epoch 0.
  - Follow-up metric: exact full-vocab eval may still remain weak; that would mean the stability fix is valid but objective coverage remains the next blocker.

2026-05-13 - Change gate: tokenizer-specific token-cache ownership
-------------------------------------------------------------------
1. Target failure mode: `train` writes tokenized corpora to `docs/vision/micro_corpus_real.txt.tokens.bin` without encoding which tokenizer produced it. A later BPE run can silently reuse a char-level cache (or vice versa), so the training corridor no longer matches the declared tokenizer and all downstream metrics become causally invalid.
2. Structural rationale: token IDs are owned by the tokenizer configuration, not just by the source text path. Therefore the cache key must include tokenizer identity. Splitting the cache path by tokenizer family (`bpe` vs `char`) restores the correct owner/source-of-truth boundary: a BPE run can only reuse BPE token IDs, and a char-level run can only reuse char-level token IDs.
3. Anti-patch check: this is not a logging workaround or a cache disable. It fixes the origin of the mismatch at the persistence boundary where token IDs are serialized. No metric changes, no training dynamics change, no heuristic post-check; the wrong cache simply becomes unreachable from incompatible tokenizers.
4. Validation plan:
  - `cargo check --features wgpu -p aideen-training` must pass.
  - A BPE run on `docs/vision/micro_corpus_real.txt` must create/reuse a `*.bpe.tokens.bin` cache and report a BPE token count consistent with `infer` (`235` on the current corpus).
  - A forced char-level run must create/reuse a separate `*.char.tokens.bin` cache and report `1162` tokens.
  - Re-run the BPE `2048` embedding probe after the cache fix; only then is the stability result admissible as a real BPE outcome.

Implementation/result - tokenizer-specific token cache
------------------------------------------------------
Files changed:
- `aideen-training-lab/src/bin/train.rs`

Change:
- Token cache path now includes tokenizer ownership:
  - BPE: `*.bpe.tokens.bin`
  - char-level: `*.char.tokens.bin`
- Cache reuse is now valid for both families because incompatible tokenizers no longer alias the same serialized token IDs.

Validation:
- `cargo check --features wgpu -p aideen-training` passed.
- BPE smoke:
  - `docs/vision/micro_corpus_real.txt -> docs/vision/micro_corpus_real.txt.bpe.tokens.bin`
  - `1162 chars -> 235 tokens`
- Char-level smoke:
  - `docs/vision/micro_corpus_real.txt -> docs/vision/micro_corpus_real.txt.char.tokens.bin`
  - `1162 chars -> 1162 tokens`

Interpretation:
- Earlier mixed logs that reused `docs/vision/micro_corpus_real.txt.tokens.bin` across tokenizer families were causally contaminated and must not be used as evidence for BPE behavior.
- The cache boundary now matches the real token-ID owner.

2026-05-13 - Change gate: coverage-oriented sampled negative schedule
---------------------------------------------------------------------
1. Target failure mode: on the clean BPE micro corridor, exact full-vocab ranking remains near random even after the embedding instability fix. This corridor effectively executes about one LM training step per epoch, so with `2048` sampled rows out of `50257`, short runs can leave a large fraction of vocabulary rows untouched or redundantly revisited.
2. Structural rationale: exact softmax gives every non-target row a small negative gradient every step. Our sampled objective can only approximate that if the fixed negative budget is spread efficiently across vocabulary rows over time. Replacing duplicate-prone random draws with a deterministic coverage schedule over vocabulary rows restores the intended property at the sampler boundary: each short run uses its finite update budget to touch as many distinct non-target rows as possible.
3. Anti-patch check: this does not clamp logits or retune learning rates. It changes the owner of the approximation error itself: the sampled negative set. The fix is causal because the failure comes from omitted-row starvation in a short-step regime, and the coverage schedule directly reduces that starvation without changing DEQ, embeddings, or optimizer dynamics.
4. Validation plan:
  - `cargo check --features wgpu -p aideen-training` must pass.
  - Add the coverage schedule behind an explicit experimental flag so default behavior stays unchanged.
  - Re-run the clean BPE `2048` corridor with the coverage sampler.
  - Success threshold 1: remain finite, no embedding NaN regression.
  - Success threshold 2: exact full-vocab eval should improve over the clean-random baseline (`ce 10.8240`, `mean_rank 22080.9`), even if only modestly.

Implementation/result - coverage-oriented sampled negative schedule
-------------------------------------------------------------------
Files changed:
- `aideen-backbone/src/gpu_lm_head.rs`

Change:
- Added experimental env flag `AIDEEN_LM_COVERAGE_SAMPLER=1`.
- Under this flag, sampled negatives are filled by a deterministic vocabulary-coverage walk instead of the previous duplicate-prone pseudo-random draw path.
- Default behavior remains unchanged.

Validation:
- `cargo check --features wgpu -p aideen-training` passed.
- Short clean run: `logs/real_text/micro_text_bpe_2048_coverage_train.log`
  - stable, finite
  - best loss `10.6170`
  - embedding moments remained finite
- Short exact eval: `logs/real_text/micro_text_bpe_2048_coverage_eval64.log`
  - CE `10.8245`
  - mean rank `23535.9`
  - no exact-ranking gain over clean-random baseline
- Long clean run: `logs/real_text/micro_text_bpe_2048_coverage_long_train.log`
  - stable through 40 epochs
  - best loss `10.5902`
  - no NaN
- Long exact eval: `logs/real_text/micro_text_bpe_2048_coverage_long_eval64.log`
  - CE `10.8249`
  - mean rank `24671.7`
  - top1 `0`, top5 at most `0.0156`

- `coverage sampler`: experimental useful for stable broad row-touching, rejected as the main quality fix

Interpretation:
- Omitted-row coverage alone is not the dominant reason exact full-vocab ranking stays random.
- The sampled objective can reduce its own training loss while still failing to produce a useful exact ranking signal on real BPE vocabulary.
- The next correct target is the objective itself: a stronger exact or near-exact BPE LM loss, not just a different negative schedule.

2026-05-13 - Change gate: exact full-vocab LM objective on frozen-DEQ/frozen-emb corridor
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
1. Target failure mode: the sampled BPE LM objective keeps improving its own loss while exact full-vocab ranking stays random. We need to test whether the approximation itself is the blocker, without mixing in DEQ or embedding backward.
2. Structural rationale: if `DEQ` and embeddings are frozen, the only trainable component on the text corridor is the `LM head`. Replacing sampled softmax with exact full-vocab cross-entropy at that boundary removes the approximation error exactly where the mismatch originates: the LM objective over the real vocabulary. This directly tests whether exact supervision can move BPE ranking in the same model/state corridor.
3. Anti-patch check: this is not a heuristic sampler tweak or a metric massage. It changes the objective at the owner of the approximation error itself. The mode is explicitly experimental and isolated to the frozen-DEQ/frozen-emb corridor so it does not silently change default training semantics.
4. Validation plan:
  - `cargo check --features wgpu -p aideen-training` must pass.
  - Add the mode behind an explicit env flag.
  - Run BPE micro training with `--freeze-deq --freeze-emb` and exact LM enabled.
  - Success threshold 1: remain finite.
  - Success threshold 2: exact full-vocab eval should improve over the LM-only sampled baseline (`ce ~10.8243`, near-zero top1/top5).

Measurement note discovered during validation:
- `eval_full_vocab_train_path_gpu` currently scores `h_pooled` rows with `W*h + b` directly, while the real LM path applies `RMSNorm + g` first. Any disagreement between autoregressive eval and train-path eval must therefore be interpreted carefully until that measurement path is corrected.

Follow-up hypothesis after exact LM-only:
- If exact full-vocab LM supervision still fails with frozen embeddings, the remaining bottleneck may be lexical representation adaptation rather than the sampled objective itself. The next exact-objective experiment should therefore keep `DEQ` frozen but allow embedding updates driven by exact `dl/dh`.

2026-05-13 - Change gate: exact `dl/dh` handoff into DEQ adjoint
-----------------------------------------------------------------
1. Target failure mode: we now have exact BPE signal on the frozen-DEQ corridor, but the real architecture requires DEQ to train as well. If the exact LM path cannot feed its exact `dl/dh` into the DEQ adjoint, we still do not know whether the remaining blocker lives in DEQ backward or only in the sampled LM objective.
2. Structural rationale: the DEQ backward owner already consumes `dl_dh_buf` as the source gradient for the adjoint solve. Therefore the structurally correct integration point is not a new side path, but writing the exact full-vocab `dl/dh` sequence into that same buffer and letting the existing DEQ adjoint/update path use it unchanged.
3. Anti-patch check: this is not bypassing DEQ or freezing more of the system. It preserves the existing DEQ training route and only replaces the origin of the source gradient with the exact LM gradient where the objective approximation error originates.
4. Validation plan:
  - `cargo check --features wgpu -p aideen-training` must pass.
  - Exact LM mode with trainable DEQ must remain finite on a short micro run.
  - Compare against the sampled-DEQ instability corridor: if failure returns, inspect DEQ adjoint/backward as the next owner; if exact BPE metrics improve while DEQ is trainable, then the LM objective mismatch was a major contributor to the prior instability.

Invariant note:
- Exact LM handoff may require writing zero associative-gradient rows into `s_h_rms_buf`. If that buffer is used as a queue upload target, its usage flags must include `COPY_DST`; otherwise validation fails before any model dynamics are tested. This is a layout/ownership fix, not a training hypothesis.

Implementation/result - exact full-vocab LM objective (frozen-DEQ corridor)
---------------------------------------------------------------------------
Files changed:
- `aideen-training-lab/src/trainer.rs`

Change:
- Added experimental flag `AIDEEN_LM_EXACT_CPU=1`.
- In this mode, when `DEQ` is frozen, the LM objective is computed exactly on CPU over the full BPE vocabulary using the real `LmHead` path (`RMSNorm + g + W + b`), instead of sampled softmax.
- CPU Adam moments become the owner of LM optimization state in this mode; checkpoint sync was updated so the save path no longer overwrites valid CPU LM moments with zero GPU moments.
- `eval_full_vocab_train_path_gpu` measurement was corrected to score `h_pooled` through the real `LmHead` path rather than `W*h+b` directly.

Validation A: exact LM-only (`--freeze-deq --freeze-emb`)
- Train log: `logs/real_text/micro_text_bpe_exact_lm_train.log`
  - remained finite
  - best loss only moved from `10.824893` to `10.823918`
- Exact eval: `logs/real_text/micro_text_bpe_exact_lm_eval64.log`
  - autoregressive CE `10.8268`
  - top1/top5 `0`
- Interpretation:
  - exact LM supervision alone is not enough when embeddings are frozen.

Validation B: exact LM + exact embedding updates (`--freeze-deq`)
- Train log: `logs/real_text/micro_text_bpe_exact_lm_emb_train.log`
  - remained finite
  - embedding moments stayed finite and active (`m=41.7874` at epoch 8)
  - best loss moved only slightly, but the path remained stable
- Exact eval: `logs/real_text/micro_text_bpe_exact_lm_emb_eval64.log`
  - autoregressive CE `10.8123`
  - top1 `0.0156`
  - top5 `0.0156`
  - mean rank `5095.3`
- Interpretation:
  - this is the first BPE corridor with a real exact-ranking gain on the true vocabulary.
  - therefore the sampled objective was indeed a major blocker, but embeddings also had to remain trainable; exact LM-only was too weak because the lexical representation itself still needed to adapt.

Classification:
- `AIDEEN_LM_EXACT_CPU`: experimental useful
- `train-path metric correction`: default stable measurement fix

Validation C: exact LM + DEQ trainable
- Short probe:
  - train: `logs/real_text/micro_text_exact_deq_probe_train.log`

    - top5 `0.0469`

Current status:
- A longer 20-epoch exact-DEQ run was launched (`logs/real_text/micro_text_exact_deq_20ep_train.log`) and remained alive past epoch 0, but had not yet emitted its terminal metrics at the time of this update. The short and seed-7 probes are therefore the current validated evidence.

Follow-up failure:
- The first 20-epoch exact-DEQ attempt aborted at checkpoint because the LM moment checksum guard still assumed GPU-owned LM moments unless both `DEQ` and embeddings were frozen. In exact-LM mode, CPU owns LM Adam state regardless of DEQ freeze. This is a checkpoint ownership bug, not a training-dynamics failure.

  - `mean_rank` moved from random-scale to double-digit scale, which is the strongest evidence so far that the trainable DEQ can use exact LM supervision productively.

Conclusion at this stage:
- The main blocker was indeed the sampled LM objective, not an inherent inability of the DEQ corridor to learn on text.
- The next question is no longer "does exact-DEQ work at all?" but "how stable/reproducible is this corridor across more seeds and longer horizons, and how do we migrate it back toward a performant GPU-native path?"

2026-05-13 - Change gate: periodic exact-LM refresh schedule
-------------------------------------------------------------
1. Target failure mode: the exact-DEQ corridor is now effective but very slow. We need a practical bridge toward efficiency without abandoning the only objective that currently gives reliable BPE signal.
2. Structural rationale: exact LM supervision is now the trusted owner of the corrective signal, but it may not be necessary on every step if periodic exact refreshes are enough to keep sampled training aligned. A periodic schedule (`exact every N steps, sampled otherwise`) preserves the exact objective as the anchor while reducing its frequency, creating a controlled near-exact corridor to compare against the full-exact baseline.
3. Anti-patch check: this is not replacing exact supervision with an unmeasured approximation. It keeps exact supervision explicitly in the loop and behind a deterministic schedule, so any efficiency gain can be evaluated against the known exact baseline. The exact path remains unchanged and default behavior remains gated.
4. Validation plan:
  - `cargo check --features wgpu -p aideen-training` must pass.
  - Add the schedule behind an explicit env flag/interval; interval `1` must preserve current exact behavior.
  - Run a short `DEQ`-trainable BPE probe with `exact every 2 steps`.
  - Success threshold 1: remain finite.
  - Success threshold 2: exact eval should stay materially better than the old sampled baseline, even if worse than full-exact.

Implementation/result - periodic exact refresh (`exact every 2 steps`)
----------------------------------------------------------------------
- Train: `logs/real_text/micro_text_exact_deq_every2_8ep_train.log`
  - stable, finite
  - much faster than full-exact (`tps_epoch ~96.8` at epoch 0 on this corridor)
- Eval: `logs/real_text/micro_text_exact_deq_every2_8ep_eval64.log`
  - autoregressive CE `10.8117`
  - top1 `0.0000`
  - top5 `0.0312`
  - mean rank `3965.5`

Interpretation:
- The periodic exact refresh schedule preserves some advantage over the old sampled baseline, but loses most of the exact-DEQ signal.
- It is therefore an experimental efficiency bridge only, not a replacement for the full-exact baseline.

2026-05-13 - Change gate: char-level tokenizer checkpoint parity
----------------------------------------------------------------
1. Target failure mode: the exact/full-vocab char-level micro probe is only meaningful if `infer` reloads the same character tokenizer used during training. Current checkpoints serialize embeddings and `vocab_size`, but `load_full()` rebuilds char-level tokenizers with `Tokenizer::new_empty(...)`, which fills `vocab` with dummy spaces.
2. Structural rationale: for char-level checkpoints, token ID semantics are defined by the ordered `vocab` characters, not just by `vocab_size`. If the vocab ordering is not serialized, `encode()` on reload no longer maps text to the trained token IDs, so any evaluation/generation after load is semantically invalid. Saving and restoring the exact char vocab fixes the owner/source-of-truth at the tokenizer boundary.
3. Anti-patch check: this does not massage the metric or change training. It restores checkpoint parity for char-level tokenization exactly where the failure originates: token ID reconstruction on load.
4. Validation plan: serialize char vocab metadata when `hf_tokenizer` is absent, restore it in `load_full()`, run `cargo check --features wgpu -p aideen-training`, then rerun the char-level micro checkpoint eval and verify `positions` matches the requested budget and the output is no longer based on dummy-space encoding.

Follow-up note:
- Restoring `char_vocab` is not enough if `load_full()` then unconditionally reattaches the standard BPE tokenizer from disk. For char-level checkpoints, that would silently override the restored char tokenizer and make eval counts nonsensical. The load path must prefer serialized char vocab over ambient BPE files.

2026-05-13 - Change gate: exact LM forward offload to GPU without changing objective
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
1. Target failure mode: the current exact-DEQ baseline is causally correct but slow because the exact full-vocab `LM` step computes all logits on CPU. That makes iteration cost too high even though this is now the only corridor with reliable BPE signal.
2. Structural rationale: the exact objective is defined by the same `LmHead` map used in inference, `RMSNorm(h) * g -> W,b -> logits -> full-vocab cross-entropy`. The heaviest part of that exact step is the dense logits matmul over the whole vocabulary. Offloading only that forward logits computation to GPU preserves the exact same objective and leaves backward, optimizer ownership, and DEQ adjoint unchanged. This isolates implementation efficiency from training dynamics.
3. Anti-patch check: this does not alter the loss, sampler, normalization, gradients, or DEQ path. It changes only where the exact logits are computed. If metrics change, that is an implementation bug, not a new learning hypothesis.
4. Validation plan:
  - Add the path behind an explicit experimental flag.
  - `cargo check --features wgpu -p aideen-training` must pass.
  - Run a short exact-LM probe with and without the GPU-forward flag on the same corridor.
  - Success threshold 1: finite run, no checkpoint/layout regression.
  - Success threshold 2: exact CE/rank must remain in the same range as the CPU-exact baseline; this stage is about parity, not new quality.
  - Success threshold 3: the exact path should report a lower forward-side wall time or better throughput on the micro probe.

Blocking invariant found during validation:
- The debug smoke aborted before touching the new exact-forward path because `gpu_deq` builds an initialization hash with plain `u32` multiplication, which panics on overflow in debug builds. The intended semantics of that hash are wrapping integer mix, so the validation blocker must be fixed with `wrapping_mul`/`wrapping_add` before any runtime comparison is meaningful.

Implementation/status - exact LM forward offload stage 1
--------------------------------------------------------
Files changed:
- `aideen-backbone/src/gpu_lm_head.rs`
- `aideen-backbone/src/shaders/lm_exact_forward.wgsl`
- `aideen-training-lab/src/trainer.rs`
- `aideen-backbone/src/gpu_deq.rs`

Change:
- Added experimental flag `AIDEEN_LM_EXACT_GPU_FORWARD=1`.
- In this mode, the exact-LM path still keeps exact full-vocab loss/backward/Adam ownership on CPU, but offloads the full-vocab logits matmul (`RMSNorm + g + W + b`) to a dedicated GPU shader and reads the exact logits back in chunks.
- The default exact path remains unchanged when the flag is absent.
- During validation a separate debug-only blocker was found in `gpu_deq`: an initialization hash used plain `u32` multiplication and panicked on overflow in debug builds. That invariant was corrected with wrapping integer semantics so runtime probes can proceed.

Validation so far:
- `cargo check --features wgpu -p aideen-training` passed.
- `cargo check --features wgpu -p aideen-backbone` passed.
- First runtime probe on the new path exposed a layout bug in the exact-forward uniform buffer (`32` bytes allocated where the shader required `48`). The Rust-side uniform padding was corrected to match the shader layout.

Classification:
- `AIDEEN_LM_EXACT_GPU_FORWARD`: experimental useful, not yet promoted
- `gpu_deq` wrapping-hash fix: default stable invariant fix for debug/runtime parity

Current status:
- The GPU-forward stage is implemented and compiles.
- Runtime parity/throughput validation is still pending; the exact-CPU smoke corridor remains very slow even under tiny debug probes, so the next clean step is to build a more surgical micro-probe that exercises a single exact LM update rather than waiting on full training loops.

2026-05-13 - Change gate: exact loss/grad allocation cleanup on CPU path
------------------------------------------------------------------------
1. Target failure mode: after moving exact logits to GPU, the exact LM corridor still burns unnecessary CPU time and heap churn in the remaining CPU owner by rebuilding temporary softmax/gradient vectors token by token.
2. Structural rationale: the exact objective on CPU still needs `CE(logits,target)` and `dL/dlogits = softmax(logits) - one_hot(target)`, but those equations do not require constructing fresh `DVector` objects for each token. Reusing a flat grad buffer and computing the stable softmax directly over slices preserves the exact same math while removing avoidable allocation overhead at the exact loss owner.
3. Anti-patch check: this does not approximate the loss or retune learning. It preserves the same stable softmax and exact gradient formula, changing only the temporary representation and ownership of scratch buffers.
4. Validation plan:
  - `cargo check --features wgpu -p aideen-training` must pass.
  - Re-run the exact-forward parity probe to ensure logits parity remains unchanged.
  - Re-run the one-step exact training probe and verify loss/checkpoint integrity stay unchanged.

2026-05-14 - Change gate: exact LM backward accumulation in-place
-----------------------------------------------------------------
1. Target failure mode: after GPU offload of exact logits, the exact LM training path still allocates a full `vocab × d_model` gradient matrix per token through `lmhead_backward`, then adds it into the running accumulators. That is structurally too expensive for the exact corridor.
2. Structural rationale: the exact LM backward equations are linear accumulations:
  - `dW[v,d] += dl_dlogits[v] * h_rms[d]`
  - `db[v] += dl_dlogits[v]`
  - `dl_dh_rms[d] = Σ_v W[v,d] * dl_dlogits[v]`
  - `dg[d] += dl_dh_rms[d] * h_norm[d]`
  - `dl_dh` follows the same RMSNorm backward already encoded.
  These do not require constructing a fresh `DMatrix`/`DVector` result object per token. Accumulating directly into the running buffers preserves the exact equations at their true owner.
3. Anti-patch check: this does not approximate, clip, or retune the exact gradient. It computes the same exact terms, but removes temporary matrix/vector materialization that was never part of the mathematical objective.
4. Validation plan:
  - `cargo check --features wgpu -p aideen-training` must pass.
  - Re-run the exact-forward parity probe to verify logits parity is unaffected.
  - Re-run the one-step exact training probe and verify loss/checkpoint integrity remain unchanged.

2026-05-14 - Change gate: exact LM stage timing instrumentation
---------------------------------------------------------------
1. Target failure mode: after exact-forward GPU validation and in-place backward accumulation, wall time of the one-step exact training probe did not improve in a clearly measurable way. We need to identify the remaining dominant owner before moving more logic.
2. Structural rationale: the exact LM update already has distinct stages with different ownership: exact logits acquisition, exact loss/grad formation, exact backward accumulation, and optimizer/update handoff. Instrumenting these stage boundaries does not alter training behavior, but it reveals which owner still dominates the exact corridor.
3. Anti-patch check: this is diagnostics only. It does not change equations, learning rates, or execution order; it only measures existing stages behind an explicit flag.
4. Validation plan:
  - `cargo check --features wgpu -p aideen-training` must pass.
  - Run the one-step exact training probe with timing enabled.
  - Confirm logs show per-stage timings without changing loss/checkpoint results.

2026-05-14 - Change gate: specialized exact LM Adam on CPU slices
-----------------------------------------------------------------
1. Target failure mode: timing shows the dominant remaining owner is `Adam` over `lm_w` on CPU (`adam_ms` far above all other exact stages). The current path also creates temporaries like `dw * grad_scale` and uses higher-level `nalgebra` update helpers that are not specific to this exact corridor.
2. Structural rationale: Adam for the exact LM update is an elementwise recurrence over `w`, `m`, `v`, and `grad`. It does not require matrix algebra once the exact gradients are already accumulated. Applying the same Adam equations directly over contiguous slices preserves the exact optimizer math while removing matrix-expression temporaries and generic abstraction overhead at the dominant owner.
3. Anti-patch check: this does not change the optimizer formula, learning rate, bias correction, or gradient source. It only changes the implementation of the already-validated exact LM Adam update to an equivalent in-place slice loop.
4. Validation plan:
  - `cargo check --features wgpu -p aideen-training` must pass.
  - Re-run the exact timing probe.
  - Success threshold 1: `loss` and checkpoint integrity remain unchanged.
  - Success threshold 2: `adam_ms` decreases materially relative to the previous timing probe.

2026-05-14 - Change gate: exact LM accumulation memory-order optimization
-------------------------------------------------------------------------
1. Target failure mode: after reducing exact LM Adam cost, the dominant remaining owner is the exact accumulation stage (`accum_ms`). The current implementation updates `dw[(v,d)]` and reads `w[(v,d)]` with per-element matrix indexing in a loop order that is unfriendly to the underlying column-major storage.
2. Structural rationale: the exact accumulation equations are still:
  - `dW[v,d] += dl_scaled[v] * h_rms[d]`
  - `dl_dh_rms[d] = Σ_v W[v,d] * dl_scaled[v]`
  With `DMatrix` stored column-major, the natural contiguous owner is each column `d` over all `v`. Reordering the loop to operate column-by-column over contiguous slices preserves the exact sums while reducing indexing overhead and improving cache locality.
3. Anti-patch check: this does not drop vocabulary rows, approximate the sum, or change scaling. It computes the same exact accumulation with a storage-order-aligned traversal.
4. Validation plan:
  - `cargo check --features wgpu -p aideen-training` must pass.
  - Re-run the exact timing probe on the same one-step setup.
  - Success threshold 1: `loss` and checkpoint integrity remain unchanged.
  - Success threshold 2: `accum_ms` decreases materially relative to the previous probe (`≈1353 ms`).

2026-05-14 - Change gate: parallel exact LM Adam on CPU slices
--------------------------------------------------------------
1. Target failure mode: after storage-order optimization, the remaining largest exact LM owner is again `Adam` over `lm_w` (`~1077 ms`) even though its math is already specialized and in-place.
2. Structural rationale: the exact Adam recurrence for `lm_w` is elementwise and independent across weight indices once the exact gradient buffer is fixed. Therefore chunking the contiguous `w/m/v/grad` slices and applying the same Adam recurrence in parallel across disjoint chunks preserves the exact optimizer equations while exploiting CPU parallelism at the true owner.
3. Anti-patch check: this does not approximate, shard, or reorder reductions that would change the result. Each weight index still executes the same Adam update with the same `grad`, `t`, `beta1`, `beta2`, and `eps`; only independent indices are evaluated concurrently.
4. Validation plan:
  - `cargo check --features wgpu -p aideen-training` must pass.
  - Re-run the exact timing probe on the same one-step setup.
  - Success threshold 1: `loss` and checkpoint integrity remain unchanged.
  - Success threshold 2: `adam_ms` decreases materially relative to the previous probe (`≈1077 ms`).

2026-05-14 - Change gate: flat exact `dW` buffer without `DMatrix` owner
------------------------------------------------------------------------
1. Target failure mode: even after accumulation and Adam specializations, the exact LM path still stores `dW` as a `DMatrix`, while the optimized accumulation and update stages already operate on contiguous slices. That leaves avoidable matrix-wrapper overhead at the dominant owner.
2. Structural rationale: exact `dW` is just a flat column-major buffer of size `vocab × d_model`. The exact accumulation already writes it column-by-column, and the specialized Adam update already consumes contiguous slices. Representing `dW` directly as `Vec<f32>` preserves the exact same gradient values and memory order while removing the `DMatrix` owner from the hot path.
3. Anti-patch check: this does not approximate gradients or alter update math. It only changes the scratch representation of the exact `dW` buffer to match the storage order already used by accumulation and Adam.
4. Validation plan:
  - `cargo check --features wgpu -p aideen-training` must pass.
  - Re-run the exact timing probe on the same one-step setup.
  - Success threshold 1: `loss` and checkpoint integrity remain unchanged.
  - Success threshold 2: either `accum_ms` or `adam_ms` improves, with no regression in exactness.

2026-05-14 - Change gate: optimizer moment ownership API fix
------------------------------------------------------------
1. Target failure mode: the next step in exact LM GPU migration needs mixed ownership for weights and moments to remain checkpoint-safe. Current optimizer accessors only expose one matrix/vector map, but sync code uses them as if they represented both `m` and `v`. That makes GPU/CPU moment ownership unsafe for a serious mixed path.
2. Structural rationale: Adam state has two independent owners per parameter family: first moment `m` and second moment `v`. The checkpoint and GPU sync layers must preserve that separation explicitly. Restoring dedicated `m`/`v` accessors fixes the ownership invariant at the optimizer-state boundary, which is the correct source of truth for checkpoint-safe mixed execution.
3. Anti-patch check: this does not change any optimizer math or training dynamics. It fixes state ownership and serialization semantics so future GPU migration of exact LM update can be done without corrupting moment state.
4. Validation plan:
  - `cargo check --features wgpu -p aideen-training` must pass.
  - Existing exact corridor code paths must still compile unchanged.
  - No promotion of mixed GPU exact update until this ownership fix is in place.

2026-05-14 - Change gate: exact `lm_w` GPU owner with checkpoint-safe moment sync
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------
1. Target failure mode: the remaining exact LM bottleneck now lives in the `W` update on CPU. But migrating `W` to GPU is unsafe unless LM weight/moment ownership is consistent across trainer creation, resume, and checkpoint sync.
2. Structural rationale: `lm_w` can become a GPU owner while `b/g` remain CPU-owned if and only if:
  - exact logits read `W` from GPU,
  - exact backward uses GPU-produced `dl_dh_rms` instead of CPU `W`,
  - `m_w/v_w` are uploaded to GPU on trainer creation/resume,
  - checkpoint sync reads back `m_w/v_w` from GPU while preserving CPU-owned `b/g` moments.
  This isolates the migration to the true bottleneck owner without changing the exact gradient source.
3. Anti-patch check: this is not a heuristic offload. The exact gradient still comes from the exact objective, and the Adam recurrence for `W` remains unchanged. The change is only the owner of the `W` update and its moment state.
4. Validation plan:
  - `cargo check --features wgpu -p aideen-training` must pass.
  - Re-run the exact-forward parity probe with the new path active.
  - Re-run the one-step exact timing probe on the same tiny setup.
  - Success threshold 1: `loss` and checkpoint integrity remain unchanged.
  - Success threshold 2: the dominant `W`-update cost should move materially off CPU.

2026-05-13 - Change gate: exact-forward parity micro-probe
----------------------------------------------------------
1. Target failure mode: using the full training loop as a validation harness for the new GPU exact-forward stage is too slow and confounds runtime issues with unrelated training-loop cost. We need a direct parity probe that isolates the exact logits owner itself.
2. Structural rationale: the stage-1 GPU-native change only replaces exact logits computation on top of an already-produced `h*`. Therefore the correct validation point is: run the normal fused forward to produce `h*`, then compare exact full-vocab logits computed from that same `h*` by the CPU `LmHead` path versus the GPU exact-forward shader. This tests the changed mechanism at its source without involving optimizer or DEQ backward.
3. Anti-patch check: this does not tweak training or hide instability. It is a measurement-only harness that checks whether the new implementation preserves the exact logits equation and reports timing separately for CPU and GPU forward owners.
4. Validation plan:
  - Add an explicit probe entrypoint behind a CLI flag; default behavior unchanged.
  - `cargo check --features wgpu -p aideen-training` must pass.
  - Run the probe on a tiny eval file with and without `AIDEEN_LM_EXACT_GPU_FORWARD=1`.
  - Success threshold 1: the probe must complete and report parity metrics.
  - Success threshold 2: `max_abs_diff` and `mean_abs_diff` over logits must stay near floating-point parity.
  - Success threshold 3: GPU exact-forward wall time should be lower than CPU exact-forward wall time on the same `h*` slices.


2026-05-14 - Change gate: mixed-owner exact LM `W` GPU migration closure
--------------------------------------------------------------------
1. Target failure mode: the current `lm_w` GPU-owner path is internally inconsistent in three places: (a) `grad_scale` is consumed before definition inside the exact token loop, so the new path cannot compile cleanly; (b) after an exact step, the training loop still calls `upload_weights_only`, which zeroes GPU Adam moments and destroys `lm_w` GPU ownership; (c) checkpoint sync still treats exact LM mode as full CPU-owner, so `m_w/v_w` updated on GPU would be dropped on save/resume.
2. Structural rationale: a correct mixed-owner path must preserve a single source of truth per state family. For `lm_w` GPU-owner exact mode, that means `W,m_w,v_w` stay GPU-owned across token updates, post-step LM sync, and checkpoint save/load, while `b/g` and their moments remain CPU-owned until migrated. Fixing compile order, post-step sync semantics, and mixed-owner moment readback restores that ownership invariant at the exact points where it was being violated.
3. Anti-patch check: this does not add guards or relax correctness. It closes the actual ownership breaks that would otherwise either fail compilation, wipe GPU moments, or serialize stale CPU moments. The exact objective, exact gradient source, and Adam equations remain unchanged.
4. Validation plan:
  - `cargo check --features wgpu -p aideen-training` must pass.
  - Re-run the exact-forward parity probe with `AIDEEN_LM_EXACT_GPU_FORWARD=1` and confirm parity stays unchanged.
  - Re-run the one-step exact timing probe with `AIDEEN_LM_EXACT_GPU_W_UPDATE=1`.
  - Success threshold 1: `loss` stays at exact baseline scale and checkpoint/integrity path does not report CPU-owner for `lm_w`.
  - Success threshold 2: CPU exact `accum_ms` and/or `adam_ms` drop materially versus the stable CPU-owner timing baseline because `W` update work has moved off CPU.


2026-05-14 - Change gate: exact `lm_w` GPU apply must preserve per-sequence Adam semantics
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
1. Target failure mode: the first `lm_w` GPU-owner prototype updates `W,m_w,v_w` once per token inside the exact loop. That matches the CPU baseline only when `seq_len=1`; for any longer sequence it changes both the logits owner seen by later tokens and the Adam update semantics, because the validated CPU corridor accumulates `dW` over the whole sequence and applies one Adam step at the end.
2. Structural rationale: to preserve the exact baseline, GPU ownership of `lm_w` must move only the final Adam owner, not the accumulation semantics. The correct mixed path is: sync exact `W` from GPU to CPU once at sequence start, compute exact per-token logits/loss and accumulate `dW` exactly as before, then upload the accumulated full-sequence `dW` to GPU and apply the same elementwise Adam recurrence there exactly once. This restores the baseline invariant that all tokens in the sequence see the same pre-update `W`.
3. Anti-patch check: this is not a throughput guard or a token-count special case. It removes a real semantic mismatch at the update locus by making the GPU owner execute the same sequence-level optimizer equation as the CPU baseline.
4. Validation plan:
  - `cargo check --features wgpu -p aideen-training` must pass.
  - Re-run the one-step timing probe with `AIDEEN_LM_EXACT_GPU_W_UPDATE=1`; `loss` must remain unchanged and CPU `adam_ms` must stay near zero.
  - Re-run a multi-token exact run afterwards and confirm it stays finite and checkpoint-safe with mixed-owner checksum.

  - checkpoint sync now reads back GPU LM moments under exact GPU-owner mode instead of misclassifying the path as pure CPU-owner.

2026-05-14 - Change gate: exact accumulation GPU owner
-----------------------------------------------------
1. Target failure mode: after migrating exact LM parameter ownership (`W,b,g`) to GPU, the remaining dominant CPU owner in the exact corridor is full-sequence accumulation: forming `dW/db/dg` and `dl_dh_seq` on CPU. This still forces `h*` and `dl_dh` through CPU scratch even though the owning LM parameters already live on GPU.
2. Structural rationale: exact loss/target gradients can stay CPU-owned for now, but the full-sequence accumulation equations can be evaluated on GPU without changing semantics if we preserve the same sequence-level contract: clear grad accumulators once per sequence, accumulate exact `dW/db/dg` token by token into GPU grad buffers using the pre-update `W,g`, write exact `dl_dh_seq` into the LM gradient buffer, then apply one exact Adam step at sequence end from those GPU grad buffers. Embedding update can then consume `dl_dh` directly from that GPU buffer, removing the remaining readback/writeback loop.
3. Anti-patch check: this does not approximate the exact objective or change update ordering. It preserves the validated sequence-level exact equations and only moves their execution owner from CPU scratch to GPU buffers. The earlier rejected per-token `W` apply is explicitly not reused.
4. Validation plan:
  - `cargo check --features wgpu -p aideen-training` must pass.

  - Success threshold 2: CPU `accum_ms` drops materially versus the current GPU-owner probe baseline (`~391 ms`).
  - Success threshold 3: embedding update path can consume the exact `dl_dh` from GPU buffer directly in this corridor.

2026-05-15 - Change gate: exact GPU path loss reporting under DEQ-trainable mode

The per-step visible loss for the exact LM corridor must use the exact loss already produced in that same step when no separate sampled-GPU loss readback is expected. Returning `self.last_gpu_loss` in that branch restores the reporting invariant without altering optimization or state updates.
3. Anti-patch check: this does not mask instability or replace a broken loss with a heuristic. It only returns the exact loss value that the step already computed and stored, instead of dropping it during the final reporting path.

2026-05-15 - Change gate: exact autoregressive eval must consume GPU-owner logits

This violates the new ownership boundary and turns exact eval into repeated full-matrix readback.
2. Structural rationale: exact autoregressive eval must consume logits at the same ownership layer where the exact LM now lives. Routing eval through `gpu_lm.read_exact_logits_from_h(...)` restores that invariant: DEQ still produces `h*`, but logits are formed by the GPU exact owner directly, with CPU only consuming the resulting logits for CE/rank metrics.
3. Anti-patch check: this does not hide slowness with a timeout or reduce the metric. It removes the ownership violation that caused repeated full-weight readback. The metric remains exact full-vocab CE/rank over the same logits, only produced at the correct structural locus.
4. Validation plan:

2026-05-17 - Change gate: exact autoregressive eval must reuse fixed-history sequential state
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------
1. Target failure mode: exact autoregressive eval remains impractically slow beyond 1 position even after removing per-position LM weight readback, because it still rebuilds the full teacher-forced context and reruns DEQ from scratch for each position.
2. Structural rationale: when `AIDEEN_DEQ_FIXED_HISTORY_REFERENCE=1`, the intended inference/reference circuit is sequential over tokens with temporal carrier `m_prev`. Exact autoregressive eval should follow that same circuit: solve one token at a time with fixed-history state reuse, update `m_prev`, and score the next target. This changes the DEQ cost from repeated prefix recomputation to the same sequential recurrence used by generation.
3. Anti-patch check: this does not shorten eval windows, cache final metrics, or skip positions. It restores the correct inference-path invariant for fixed-history reference mode by evaluating the same token circuit we intend to deploy, only without sampling.
4. Validation plan:
  - `cargo check --features wgpu -p aideen-training` must pass.
  - With `AIDEEN_DEQ_FIXED_HISTORY_REFERENCE=1`, exact eval over a few positions must return substantially faster than the old prefix-recompute path and keep exact CE/rank reporting intact.
  - Small-position outputs must remain finite and structurally plausible.

2026-05-17 - Change gate: fixed-history GPU solve must update only slot_anchor after initial upload
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
1. Target failure mode: even with sequential fixed-history eval, GPU token solves stay very slow because `gpu_solve_token_with_fixed_history` reuploads the full DEQ weight block on every token just to inject the updated history into `slot_anchor`.
2. Structural rationale: the causal quantity that changes token-to-token in fixed-history reference mode is the effective `slot_anchor`, not the rest of the DEQ parameter block. After one full upload initializes the GPU owner, subsequent token solves should write only the `slot_anchor` subrange inside `all_weights_buf`. This preserves the exact fixed-history equations while removing redundant bandwidth/packing work.
3. Anti-patch check: this does not cache results or skip DEQ iterations. It narrows the uploaded state to the exact sub-buffer whose value changes each token, keeping all equations and active weights identical.
4. Validation plan:
  - `cargo check --features wgpu -p aideen-training` must pass.
  - Fixed-history exact eval over a few positions must complete materially faster than with full weight reupload.
  - Generation/fixed-history callers must still restore the base slot anchor correctly.
